One should not be attached to non-form as form, should not be attached to non-feeling, non-perception, non-formations, and non-consciousness as consciousness, should not be attached to non-eye, non-ear, non-nose, non-tongue, non-body, and non-mind as mind, should not be attached to non-form, non-sound, non-smell, non-taste, non-touch, and non-dharmas as dharmas, should not be attached to non-four-great-elements and non-sense-field-entries as sense-field entries, should not be attached to non-twelve-links-of-dependent-arising as dependent arising, should not be attached to non-thirty-seven-factors as the thirty-seven factors, should not be attached to non-ten-powers as the ten powers, should not be attached to non-four-fearlessnesses as fearlessnesses, should not be attached to non-four-analytical-knowledges as analytical knowledges, should not be attached to non-eighteen-unique-buddha-dharmas as the unique buddha-dharmas. Thus, Śāriputra, practicing the prajñāpāramitā, for this reason, the aspiration for awakening is a mind without enemies. The minds of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas cannot attain it. Nor does one conceive of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas. Without any reliance, not following delusion, and without any attainment: therefore one accomplishes all dharmas."

### Chapter Thirteen: The Great Vehicle

At that time the Venerable Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra addressed the Buddha: "God among Gods! Am I capable of expounding the designation and meaning of 'mahāsattva' and what it refers to?"

The World-Honored One said: "You should expound it."

Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra said: "The mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha (one who dons the great armor of virtue), the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, practicing the mahāyāna with aspiration for the Great Vehicle: that person rides in the Great Vehicle. Therefore, God among Gods, 'mahāsattva' is the designation and meaning of mahāsattva!"

Śāriputra said to Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra: "For what reason is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva called 'mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha, mahāyāna, saṃprasthita'?"

Pūrṇa answered: "In this regard, Venerable One, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva does not practice the dāna-pāramitā of giving for the sake of individual students, isolated persons, or particular beings; rather, for the sake of all living beings, one abides in the dāna-pāramitā and gives. Not for individual students, beings, or isolated persons does one abide in the śīla-pāramitā to uphold the precepts; rather, for the sake of all living beings, one abides in the śīla-pāramitā and upholds the precepts. Not for individual students, beings, or isolated persons does one abide in the kṣānti-pāramitā and practice patience; rather, for the sake of all living beings, one abides in the kṣānti-pāramitā and practices patience. Not for individual students, beings, or isolated persons does one abide in the vīrya-pāramitā and practice vigor; rather, for the sake of all living beings, one abides in the vīrya-pāramitā and practices vigor. Not for individual students, beings, or isolated persons does one abide in the dhyāna-pāramitā with undistracted mind; rather, for the sake of all living beings, one abides in the dhyāna-pāramitā with one-pointed mind. Not for individual students, beings, or isolated persons does one abide in the prajñāpāramitā and practice wisdom; rather, for the sake of all living beings, one abides in the prajñāpāramitā and follows wisdom. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā does not cut off or limit sentient beings when donning the armor: 'I shall cause such-and-such a number of beings to enter cessation, but not cause such-and-such a number; I shall establish such-and-such a number on the buddha-path, but not such-and-such a number.' Rather, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva dons the armor for all living beings and practices thus: 'I myself shall completely fulfill and perfect the dāna-pāramitā and encourage all beings! I shall cause all to enter the dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā. I myself shall completely practice and perfect the prajñāpāramitā and encourage all beings, causing all to enter the perfection of wisdom.'

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, when a bodhisattva-mahāsattva practices the dāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, all is for cultivating the mind toward sarvajñā, taking all sentient beings as companions, saying 'these are my children,' thus encouraging them toward anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This, Śāriputra, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's armor of practicing the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the dāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, cultivates the mind toward sarvajñā; the mind one generates does not encourage or assist the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas. This, Śāriputra, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's armor of practicing the dāna-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the dāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, cultivates the mind toward sarvajñā, constantly thinking of protecting the precepts without any transgression, not encouraging or assisting the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, attaining anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's armor of practicing the śīla-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the dāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, cultivates the mind toward sarvajñā, constantly thinking of patience toward all dharmas, encouraging sentient beings with patience, taking them as companions, saying 'these are my children,' encouraging them through patience, not toward the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, but attaining anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's armor of practicing the kṣānti-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the dāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, cultivates the mind toward sarvajñā, constantly practicing vigor without abandoning diligence, whose vigorous practice is without any outflows, not encouraging or assisting the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, attaining anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's armor of practicing the vīrya-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the dāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, cultivates the mind toward sarvajñā. When giving, one is always single-minded without diverse thoughts, only contemplating the wisdom of sarvajñā in one's practice, contemplating without abandoning, not following the practice of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, attaining anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's armor of practicing the dhyāna-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the dāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, cultivates the mind toward sarvajñā, constantly following wisdom and departing from wrong cleverness, whose practice of wisdom opens up everything and is without any outflows, not encouraging or assisting the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, attaining anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's armor of practicing the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the dāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, cultivates the mind toward sarvajñā. When giving, one establishes a mind of illusion and transformation: there is no giving, no giver, and no receiver. When the bodhisattva-mahāsattva gives in this way, it is not to encourage or assist the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, but to attain anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's armor of practicing the prajñāpāramitā."

Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra said to Śāriputra: "If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mind reveres and follows sarvajñā, regarding the pāramitās one has no conception of seeking and nothing to attain. This is what is meant by the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the śīla-pāramitā, whose mind reveres and rests in sarvajñā, through giving cultivates the mind of sarvajñā, gathers and protects sentient beings, encouraging them toward the mind of anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the śīla-pāramitā as the dāna-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the śīla-pāramitā, regarding these dharmas, has nothing that cannot be endured and nothing one fails to endure; there is nothing one does not endure. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the śīla-pāramitā as the kṣānti-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the śīla-pāramitā naturally gives rise to matters of vigor without any negligence. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the śīla-pāramitā as the vīrya-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the śīla-pāramitā, whose mind reveres and rests in sarvajñā, contemplating one's practice, not following the minds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, always single-minded, concentrating on meditation without any confusion. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the śīla-pāramitā as the dhyāna-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the śīla-pāramitā, establishing the practice regarding all existing dharmas, contemplating them as like an illusion, not conceiving of the precepts, and having nothing to attain, not following the minds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, discerning subtle and wondrous wisdom. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the śīla-pāramitā as the prajñāpāramitā. Thus, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the śīla-pāramitā gathers and completes all the pāramitās. This is what is meant by mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha!

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the kṣānti-pāramitā, whatever one gives, generates and gives rise to the mind of sarvajñā, not following the minds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, universally able to endure without any binding resentment, encouraging all toward anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the vīrya-pāramitā, whatever one gives, generates and gives rise to the mind of sarvajñā, not following the minds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, constantly practicing vigor, neither advancing nor retreating, attaining anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the dhyāna-pāramitā, whatever one gives, generates and gives rise to the mind of sarvajñā, not following the minds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, the mind always concentrated, not dwelling in confusion or non-confusion, not confused, not seeing confusion, and not seeing concentration.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā, generating and giving rise to the mind of sarvajñā, not following the minds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, the mind vast and without any obstruction, not abiding in birth-and-death and not abiding in cessation!

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, through the formless attainment, practices samādhi without following the teaching of dhyāna to be reborn. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's upāya-kauśalya within the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, if the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practices dhyāna meditation or the four immeasurables, through the formless attainment practicing samādhi, without losing the dhyāna meditation and the four immeasurables and the formless samādhi: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's upāya-kauśalya within the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva further cultivates meditation, practicing the four immeasurables and the formless samādhi, abiding in quiescence. Having contemplated and seen emptiness, signlessness, and wishlessness, having seen these: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha within the prajñāpāramitā. Thus, Śāriputra, this is what is meant by the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha! Thus, Śāriputra, if the bodhisattva-mahāsattva dons such armor, the buddhas, God among Gods, in the worlds of the eight directions above and below, praise and extol subtle and wondrous teachings, lauding merit and proclaiming their voice: 'In a certain world there is a bodhisattva-mahāsattva who has donned the great armor of virtue, converting sentient beings and adorning and purifying buddha-fields.'"

Śāriputra asked Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra: "What is meant by the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's setting forth, riding in the Great Vehicle?"

Pūrṇa answered: "In this regard, Venerable One, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the six pāramitās, having removed all desires and extinguished all evil and unwholesome dharmas, with thought and investigation abiding in quiescence, remaining at peace, can completely practice the first dhyāna. Having departed from desires and from all evils, removing all thoughts and what one contemplates, quiescent and at peace, one can completely practice the second dhyāna. Removing all thoughts, without thought and without investigation, cultivating one's mind according to the teaching of the noble and wise, not deviating from the wise and attaining joyful peace, one can completely accomplish the third dhyāna. Removing ease and eliminating suffering, all previously experienced good and evil, pleasant and unpleasant, without suffering and without pleasure, abiding in quiescence and attaining joyful peace, one can completely accomplish the fourth dhyāna.

"Practicing the four immeasurables: the mind always with lovingkindness, without enmity, without binding, without delusion, vast and without limit, following goodness and immeasurable, pervading all worlds; what the mind practices, one does not abandon this. Compassion, sympathetic joy, and equanimity are likewise. The mind of equanimity always together, without enmity, without binding, without delusion, vast and without limit, following goodness and immeasurable, pervading all worlds; what the mind practices, one does not abandon this. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's meditation. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva through this meditation practices the four immeasurables; through these auspicious signs practices samādhi-concentration; having practiced these, all is to encourage and assist the wisdom of sarvajñā. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's foundation of the dāna-pāramitā among the six pāramitās; the śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are each likewise. This is what is meant by the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha!

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, with lovingkindness, vast and far-reaching, without duality, without limit, without binding, and without abiding in any one place, with faith in the first, second, third, and fourth dhyānas likewise, below without any limit, above without any boundary, in the eight directions above and below pervading everywhere, completely accomplishing the four dhyānas: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's samādhi. If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva reveres and directs the mind toward sarvajñā, practicing the first dhyāna, and through it rescues and gathers all sentient beings, encouraging and assisting them all toward comprehensive wisdom, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva endowed with the wisdom-mind of sarvajñā, through skillful means generates and expresses meaning, teaching the scriptures for people: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's dāna-pāramitā. Furthermore, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva whose mind reaches the wisdom of sarvajñā, contemplating and cultivating, crossing beyond the first dhyāna: if one can abide in the first dhyāna, one no longer has faith in or delights in generating different minds, and does not follow the minds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's non-transgression toward others: the śīla-pāramitā. If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva whose mind is directed toward the wisdom of sarvajñā, cultivating and contemplating, generates this thought: 'I shall cause all people and sentient beings to extinguish their painful sufferings, and I shall teach the dharma for them, observing what their minds desire and delight in, discerning their root capacities and converting them.' This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the kṣānti-pāramitā. If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva whose mind cultivates the wisdom of sarvajñā, encouraging and assisting all roots of merit, regarding all comprehensive wisdoms not seeing any destination of vigor: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the vīrya-pāramitā. If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva whose mind cultivates the wisdom of sarvajñā, from the first dhyāna through the fourth dhyāna, further contemplating impermanence, suffering, emptiness, non-self, emptiness, signlessness, and wishlessness: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the dhyāna-pāramitā. If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva whose mind reveres the wisdom of sarvajñā, contemplating all dharmas as like illusion and transformation, without any three realms, and teaching the scriptures for people: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the prajñāpāramitā. Venerable Śāriputra! This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna matters.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: establishing all the four foundations of mindfulness, four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, and further establishing all, completely accomplishing the samādhi of emptiness, signlessness, and wishlessness, the ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva does not declare or seek these two grounds, the grounds of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas; the mind delights only in the wisdom of sarvajñā. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing without negligence in the four immeasurables accomplishes the kṣānti-pāramitā. If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mind cultivates and generates all compassionate wisdom, whose practice is limitless and without any destruction: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the vīrya-pāramitā. If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva in the four immeasurables practices meditation, without losing the meditation and the four immeasurables: this is the bodhisattva's practice without negligence in the four immeasurables, the upāya-kauśalya.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's samādhi of lovingkindness: 'I shall rescue and protect all sentient beings.' Then revering and following, one practices the samādhi of compassion, with pity and sorrow practicing compassion and conforming to this. Practicing the samādhi of sympathetic joy: 'I shall liberate all sentient beings.' Gradually advancing to the samādhi of equanimity, extending to sentient beings until all outflows are exhausted. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice without negligence in the four immeasurables: the dāna-pāramitā. If through meditation without negligence one practices the four immeasurables, through these causes and auspicious signs, not encouraging or assisting the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, but exclusively following all comprehensive compassionate wisdom: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's non-transgression in the practice of the four immeasurables: the śīla-pāramitā.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: comprehending internal emptiness without falling into delusion, without any seeking and without any attainment; suffering and pleasure, good and evil, whatever exists, natural emptiness; regarding all comprehensive wisdoms also without any attainment, without interior or exterior, and not obtaining any middle. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: regarding all dharmas, without confusion and without the wisdom of samādhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: always aspiring to the Great Vehicle, whose wisdom is autonomous, whose wisdom does not abide in permanence or impermanence, does not reckon suffering or non-suffering, pleasure or non-pleasure, whose wisdom does not abide in 'mine' or 'not mine.' This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: without any attainment and not falling into delusion.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: whose wisdom is autonomous, not abiding in the past, not abiding in the future, not abiding in the present, not abiding in the three times where there is no wisdom. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: always without any attainment and not falling into delusion.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: whose wisdom does not abide attached to the desire realm, not in the form realm, not in the formless realm, yet whose wisdom is autonomous. Completely knowing the desire realm, form realm, and formless realm, yet attaining autonomy, without any attainment and not falling into delusion. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's Great Vehicle.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: whose wisdom is autonomous, not identical with worldly wisdom and not submerged in worldly wisdom, not abiding in the conditioned and not abiding in the unconditioned, not abiding in what has outflows and not abiding in what is without outflows. Regarding this dharma-wisdom, one attains autonomy. Completely knowing worldly wisdom and transcendent wisdom, without any lack. Completely knowing conditioned and unconditioned dharmas, without any lack, without any attainment and not falling into delusion. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's Great Vehicle."

## Fascicle Six

### Chapter Fourteen: Riding the Great Vehicle

The Venerable Śāriputra asked Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra: "How does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva ride in the mahāyāna?"

Pūrṇa said to Śāriputra: "Venerable One! The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, practicing the prajñāpāramitā, rides in the dāna-pāramitā yet does not apprehend the dāna-pāramitā, nor any bodhisattva, and does not perceive a receiver who has anything to gain, nor is there anything obtained. Riding in the dāna-pāramitā: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā: riding in the prajñāpāramitā, one does not apprehend the prajñāpāramitā, nor does one apprehend the bodhisattva, nor is there anything obtained. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's riding in the prajñāpāramitā, without any attainment.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, without losing the mind that cultivates and reveres the wisdom of sarvajñā, then follows and practices the four foundations of mindfulness: what is mindful is without mindfulness, what is practiced is without practice. Regarding all these meanings, there is nothing to be attained. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's riding in the mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, without losing the mind that cultivates and reveres the wisdom of sarvajñā, practices the four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, and Eightfold Path. Regarding the meaning of these, there is nothing to be attained. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's riding in the mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, without losing the mind that cultivates and reveres the wisdom of sarvajñā, practices the ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas. Regarding the meaning of all these, there is nothing to be attained. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's riding in the mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, discerning and comprehending this: what is called 'bodhisattva' is but a conventional designation that follows worldly usage. Seeking a person, one cannot apprehend one, nor is there any arising. What is called 'form' is but a conventional designation: it cannot be apprehended, nor does it arise. What is called 'feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness' are but conventional designations: they cannot be apprehended, nor do they arise. The eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are but conventional designations: they cannot be apprehended, nor do they arise. Form, sound, smell, taste, touch, and dharmas are but conventional designations: they cannot be apprehended, nor do they arise. The four foundations of mindfulness, four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, and Eightfold Path are but conventional designations: they cannot be apprehended, nor do they arise. The ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are but conventional designations: they cannot be apprehended, nor do they arise. Internal emptiness, external emptiness, and the emptiness of emptiness are but conventional designations: they cannot be apprehended, nor do they arise. The emptiness of what exists, natural emptiness, and the emptiness of what exists and is natural are but conventional designations. The dharma of the Tathāgata, the dharma of rootlessness, the dharma-realm, the quiescence of dharmas, and the original limit: the original limit cannot be apprehended, nor does it arise. The buddha-path and whatever is awakened to: the buddha-path itself cannot be apprehended, nor does it arise. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's riding in the mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, from the initial generation of aspiration, is endowed with the bodhisattva's supernatural power to convert sentient beings, traveling from one buddha-field to another, making offerings to and attending upon all the buddha world-honored ones, earnestly drawing close to the buddha world-honored ones, hearing the scriptures and dharma, and seeking the bodhisattva vehicle. That person thereupon rides in the bodhisattva's practice, traveling from one buddha-field to another, purifying buddha-fields and converting sentient beings, without being attached to any buddha-field, without any perception of a person, abiding on no secondary ground, and always through bodily strength guiding and benefiting all living beings for their sake. For what reason? It is for one's own sake that one takes up and gathers, yet the mind has never departed from this Vehicle, and one attains the wisdom of sarvajñā. Having attained the wisdom of sarvajñā, one turns the dharma-wheel. Having turned the dharma-wheel, one then benefits all śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, devas, nāgas, spirits, and people of the world. Thereupon the tathāgatas, arhats, samyak-saṃbuddhas of the eight directions above and below all together praise and proclaim: 'A certain bodhisattva-mahāsattva in a certain world, riding in the mahāyāna, has attained the wisdom of sarvajñā, and having attained the wisdom of sarvajñā, turns the dharma-wheel.' This, Śāriputra, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's riding in the mahāyāna."

### Chapter Fifteen: Without Bondage

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "What is called mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha: the bodhisattva-mahāsattva dons the great armor of virtue. What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's saṃnāha-saṃnaddha?"

The Buddha told Subhūti: "Here, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva dons the armor of morality and virtue, practicing the dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā: this is mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha. The four foundations of mindfulness, four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, the saṃnāha-saṃnaddha of internal emptiness, the saṃnāha-saṃnaddha of external emptiness, the saṃnāha-saṃnaddha of all that exists being naturally empty, the saṃnāha-saṃnaddha of the wisdom of sarvajñā, having donned the saṃnāha-saṃnaddha of the buddha-image: one then illuminates the three-thousandfold great-thousandfold world with radiance, and the eight directions above and below likewise. That great radiance pervades everywhere. Moreover, it can shake the three-thousandfold great-thousandfold world, reaching buddha-fields as numerous as the sands of the Ganges in the eastern direction, and the eight directions above and below are each likewise, all trembling and quaking. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, through this radiance, abides in the dāna-pāramitā and dons the great armor of the mahāyāna, transforming the three-thousandfold great-thousandfold world entirely into dark lapis lazuli. Having transformed the three-thousandfold great-thousandfold world into dark lapis lazuli, one further transforms into a wheel-turning sage-king. Having manifested the majestic appearance of a wheel-turning sage-king, one then gives generously: to the hungry one gives food, to the thirsty one gives drink, to those without clothing one gives garments, to those without incense one gives incense, flower ornaments, mixed incenses, ground incenses, carriages, elephants, horses, servants, and attendants, whatever people seek, houses and dwellings as they should receive, means of livelihood, and whatever else people desire, causing all to receive what they need. Food and drink, clothing, incense and flowers, elephants and horses, houses and dwellings: whatever they should receive, one gives to all people. Having caused each to receive what they need, one then teaches the dharma in detail for all sentient beings, expounding the meaning completely and cultivating the six pāramitās. All these living beings, hearing the dharma taught, then follow the path and practice the pāramitās, until they attain anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha!

"For example, Subhūti, a skilled and wise magician or his wise disciple, at a great four-way crossroads, conjures up living beings and means of livelihood. Why? Because the art of the magician is naturally thus, to use this skill to provide innumerable sentient beings with food and drink, clothing, incense and flowers, ornaments, elephants and horses, houses and dwellings that people lack. What do you think, Subhūti? Has that magician actually given and provided for the multitude in their need?"

He answered: "No, God among Gods!"

The Buddha said: "Likewise, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, practicing the six pāramitās, thirty-seven factors, internal emptiness, external emptiness, internal-and-external emptiness, and the emptiness of all that exists being naturally empty, donning the armor of the ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, and the saṃnāha-saṃnaddha of sarvajñā, transforms into a buddha-image and dons the great armor of virtue, whose radiance universally illuminates the three-thousandfold great-thousandfold world, and reaches the buddha-fields as numerous as the sands of the Ganges in the eastern direction, the eight directions above and below, pervading everywhere. The worlds in the ten directions, each as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, all tremble and quake sixfold. Through the great radiance, abiding in the dāna-pāramitā, giving whatever people seek: food and drink, clothing, incense and flowers, ornaments, elephants and horses, houses and dwellings, means of livelihood. Although one transforms and gives, in the end nothing is given. All people come and receive, taking up means of livelihood, yet there is no giver and no receiver. Why? Subhūti! These dharmas are also like an illusion; the illusion is not separate from the dharma. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, abiding in the śīla-pāramitā, wishing to rescue and protect all beings in the realms of birth, manifests birth as a wheel-turning sage-king. Having established the position of a wheel-turning sage-king, one then establishes all sentient beings in the ten wholesome courses of action, the four dhyānas, four immeasurables, four formless attainments, four foundations of mindfulness, four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, broadly teaching the scriptures for all sentient beings, never causing them to depart from this path and meaning, and enabling them to reach peace and security and attain the buddha-path. This is the saṃnāha-saṃnaddha. For example, Subhūti, a skilled and wise magician or his wise disciple, at a great four-way crossroads, conjures innumerable, incalculable people, and teaches the dharma for those conjured persons, establishing them in the ten wholesome courses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas. What do you think, Subhūti? Are there really people who abide in the ten wholesome courses? And in the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas?"

He answered: "No, God among Gods!"

"Likewise, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva converts sentient beings, causing them to abide in the ten wholesome courses, thirty-seven factors, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, yet does not actually establish any sentient being. Why? Subhūti! These dharmas are also like an illusion; the illusion is not separate from the dharma. Thus, Subhūti, this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, abiding in the kṣānti-pāramitā, encourages and converts all sentient beings to establish them in the perfection of patience. What is the bodhisattva's abiding in the kṣānti-pāramitā, converting all sentient beings and establishing them in the dharma of the perfection of patience? Here, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, from the initial generation of aspiration, equally dons the armor of virtue and takes this vow: 'Even if all living beings should attack me with swords and staves, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva should not give rise to a thought of anger and hatred for even an instant; and I shall also convert all sentient beings to establish them in this patience.' For example, Subhūti, a skilled and wise magician or his wise disciple, at a great four-way crossroads, conjures innumerable, incalculable people, then strikes and beats them, cuts them with swords. Are there really those who are struck or cut?"

He answered: "No, God among Gods!"

The Buddha said: "Likewise, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, practicing the kṣānti-pāramitā, if swords and staves are used against their body, endures all of it; and converts sentient beings to establish them in this patience, yet there is no one who strikes and no one who endures. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's kṣānti-pāramitā mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, abiding in the vīrya-pāramitā, encourages and converts all sentient beings, causing all to establish the vīrya-pāramitā."

The Buddha said: "How does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva establish sentient beings in the perfection of vigor? Here, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, whose mind cultivates and reveres the wisdom of sarvajñā, generates the aspiration for awakening, without any conception and without any vigor, and encourages sentient beings to follow the practice. For example, Subhūti, a skilled and wise magician or his wise disciple, at a great four-way crossroads, conjures innumerable, incalculable people and causes them to practice vigor, guarding body, speech, and mind, yet there are no people, no body, speech, or mind, and no practice. Likewise, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, established in the vīrya-pāramitā, encourages and converts all people to practice vigor, yet there is no characteristic of vigor and no practice, nor does one convert sentient beings and establish them in vigor. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's vīrya-pāramitā mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, abiding in the dhyāna-pāramitā, encourages and converts all living beings through the dhyāna-pāramitā. How, Subhūti, does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva abide in the dhyāna-pāramitā? Equally abiding in all dharmas, all dharmas are without confusion, and one does not perceive any dharma as disturbed or agitated. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, able to abide in this way, within the dhyāna-pāramitā equally abides in rootlessness, encouraging sentient beings toward the dharma of equanimity. Those whom one converts never depart from the teachings of the buddhas, until they attain anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi, yet there is no one who attains anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. For example, a skilled and wise magician or his wise disciple, at a great four-way crossroads, conjures innumerable, incalculable people and causes them all to sit in meditation, with the mind concentrated, yet there is no concentration and no confusion. Likewise, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva encourages and converts sentient beings, causing them to practice the dharma of equanimity, not perceiving any dharma as having one-pointed mind or as having a confused mind. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's dhyāna-pāramitā mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, abiding in the prajñāpāramitā, opens and develops all people and living beings, causing all to abide in the perfection of wisdom. How does one oneself abide in the prajñāpāramitā while encouraging and converting sentient beings toward the perfection of wisdom? Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva has no dharma, and what one practices is without any protection. This bodhisattva-mahāsattva, having abided in the prajñāpāramitā, also uses this dharma to convert all, enabling them to cross over without any obstruction. For example, a skilled and wise magician or his wise disciple conjures innumerable, incalculable people with wise and eloquent speech that makes many distinctions, yet there is no wisdom and nothing spoken. What do you think, Subhūti? Is there anything spoken or anything heard?"

He answered: "No, God among Gods!"

The Buddha said: "This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha: oneself abiding in the dharma of natural emptiness, one converts all sentient beings as numerous as the sands of the Ganges in the eastern direction, causing all to follow and practice the dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā, teaching the dharma for them. If sentient beings hear these six pāramitās, they shall never again depart from the six perfections or from anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi; in the ten directions, all are likewise. Just as with the buddha-fields of the eastern direction, in the ten directions all are likewise, equally without any difference. For example, Subhūti, a skilled and wise magician or his wise disciple, at a great four-way crossroads, conjures innumerable, incalculable people who practice giving, morality, patience, vigor, concentration, and wisdom, yet there is no giving, no morality, no patience, no vigor, no concentration, and no wisdom. Likewise, Subhūti, this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, setting forth with a mind that reveres the wisdom of sarvajñā, has never given rise to any other differing mind, without any faith in or acceptance of it, whether converting people and establishing them in the dāna-pāramitā, or converting people and establishing them in the śīla-pāramitā, or converting people and establishing them in the kṣānti-pāramitā, or converting people and establishing them in the vīrya-pāramitā, or converting people and establishing them in the dhyāna-pāramitā, or converting people and establishing them in the prajñāpāramitā: regarding these converted persons, ultimately nothing is established. Where there is no converting, one converts a certain number of people and establishes them in the four foundations of mindfulness; converts a certain number and establishes them in the four correct exertions; converts a certain number and establishes them in the four bases of supernatural power; converts a certain number and establishes them in the five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, and Eightfold Path; converts a certain number and establishes them in the ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas; or one does not convert them. One converts a certain number of people and establishes them in the fruit of stream-entry; converts a certain number and establishes them in the fruit of once-returning; converts a certain number and establishes them in the fruit of non-returning; converts a certain number and establishes them in the fruit of arhatship; converts a certain number and establishes them in the fruit of pratyekabuddhahood; or a certain number cannot be converted. One establishes a certain number of people in the wisdom of sarvajñā; a certain number should not be converted. There are incalculably, immeasurably many living beings whom one shall convert and establish in the dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā; the four foundations of mindfulness, four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas; converting sentient beings, incalculably and immeasurably, toward the wisdom of sarvajñā. What do you think, Subhūti? Converting these incalculably many people, each having their destination, each having their arising, each enabled to cross over: is there any arising or anyone who crosses over?"

He answered: "No, God among Gods!"

The Buddha said: "Thus the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, through the six pāramitās, converting with the thirty-seven factors and all the buddha-dharmas, the four paths and pratyekabuddha-realization: there is no destination and no one who crosses over. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "God among Gods! If I hear the dharma and examine its inner meaning, I should observe that the bodhisattva-mahāsattva is in fact without saṃnāha-saṃnaddha. Why? Because it arises from emptiness, and all natural characteristics arise from emptiness. Therefore, God among Gods, all forms are empty in form. All feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are empty. Examining the eye, the eye is empty; the ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are empty. Examining eye-form-consciousness, ear-sound-consciousness, nose-smell-consciousness, tongue-taste-consciousness, body-touch-consciousness, and mind-dharma-consciousness, the eighteen elements are all also empty. What the eye habituates to, what the ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind habituate to: all the habituations of the six sense faculties are likewise, all being habituations of emptiness; all dharmas are completely empty, and the habituated dharma is empty. God among Gods! The dāna-pāramitā is also empty; the śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are all also completely empty. Examining the internal, it is also empty; internal emptiness is also empty, and is without any existence. The natural is also empty, and its emptiness is also empty. The four foundations of mindfulness are also empty; the four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, and Eightfold Path are also empty. The ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are also empty. What is called a bodhisattva is also empty, and saṃnāha-saṃnaddha is also empty. God among Gods! For this reason, one should observe the bodhisattva-mahāsattva as being without saṃnāha-saṃnaddha."

The Buddha told Subhūti: "So it is, so it is! Subhūti! It is truly as you say."

The Buddha told Subhūti: "The wisdom of sarvajñā, being conditioned, is without any action, neither not acted upon, and is without any existence. All sentient beings are likewise without action and without any existence. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, for the sake of sentient beings, dons the great armor, yet is without any action, neither not acted upon, and is without any existence."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "God among Gods! Why is the wisdom of sarvajñā without any action, neither not acted upon, and without any existence? And these sentient beings are also without action, neither not acted upon, and without any existence? And the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's saṃnāha-saṃnaddha is likewise?"

The World-Honored One answered: "Where there is action and attainment, there is arising. But the wisdom of sarvajñā is without any action, neither not acted upon, and is without any existence. These sentient beings are also without any action, neither not acted upon, and without any existence. Why? Form has no creator, and is not uncreated. It has no practice and no action. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no creator, are not uncreated, have no practice, and no action. The eye has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action. The ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind have no creator, are not uncreated, have no practice, and no action. Form, sound, smell, taste, touch, and dharmas have no creator, are not uncreated, have no practice, and no action. The eighteen elements, the six sense habituations, and the feelings they occasion have no creator, are not uncreated, have no practice, and no action. The self, Subhūti, has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action. And what is known and what is seen have no creator, are not uncreated, have no practice, and no action. For this reason, investigating the root and end, there is no original source, and it cannot be apprehended. Sentient beings and dreams have no creator, are not uncreated, have no practice, and no action. Why? Investigating the root and end, there is no original source, and it cannot be apprehended. Like a calling voice, an echo, the moon in water, an illusion, or a mirage: they have no creator, are not uncreated, have no action, and no practice. Why? Investigating the root and end, there is no original source, and it cannot be apprehended. Internal emptiness, Subhūti, has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action; external emptiness is likewise. What exists and is naturally empty has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action. The thirty-seven factors, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas have no creator, are not uncreated, have no practice, and no action. Why? Investigating the root and end, there is no original source, and it cannot be apprehended. The rootless, Subhūti, has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action; the rootless is likewise, without any different dharma. The dharma-element abides in the dharma-realm; all dharmas are quiescent. The original limit has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action. Why? Investigating the root and end, there is no original source, and it cannot be apprehended. The bodhisattva has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action. The wisdom of sarvajñā, the wisdom of complete compassion, has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action. Why? Investigating the root and end, there is no original source, and it cannot be apprehended. The bodhisattva has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action. The wisdom of sarvajñā, the wisdom of complete compassion, has no creator, is not uncreated, has no practice, and no action. Why? Investigating the root and end, there is no original source, and it cannot be apprehended. For this reason, Subhūti, there is no action. The wisdom of sarvajñā is also without any action, and neither not acted upon. Sentient beings are likewise, without any action and neither not acted upon. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, through the mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha: for this reason, Subhūti, one should observe the bodhisattva-mahāsattva as being without the mahāyāna saṃnāha-saṃnaddha."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "So it is, World-Honored One! As the teaching distinguishes the meaning, I shall distinguish the meaning: form is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation."

Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra asked Subhūti: "Is form without attachment, without bondage, without liberation? Are feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness without attachment, without bondage, without liberation?"

Subhūti said to Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra: "So it is, Venerable One! Form is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation."

Pūrṇa further asked Subhūti: "What is the form that is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation? What are the feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness that are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation?"

Subhūti answered: "Form being naturally empty is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being naturally empty are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being like an echo is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being like an echo are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being like a mirage is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being like a mirage are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being like an illusion is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being like an illusion are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being like a transformation is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being like a transformation are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Past form is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; past feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Future form is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; future feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Present form is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; present feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being without substance is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being without substance are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being tranquil is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being tranquil are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being unborn is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being unborn are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Pūrṇa! Form being wholesome is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being wholesome are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being unwholesome is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being unwholesome are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being indeterminate is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being indeterminate are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form being undifferentiated is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being undifferentiated are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Pūrṇa! Worldly form is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; worldly feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Transcendent form is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; transcendent feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Form with outflows and without outflows is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness with outflows and without outflows are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The indistinct is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The illusory is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. All dharmas are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Non-existence is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Quiescence is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The dāna-pāramitā is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Reaching truth is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Reaching stillness is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Internal emptiness is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. External emptiness is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The emptiness of what exists being natural is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The four foundations of mindfulness are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, and Eightfold Path are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Arising from the indistinct is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The buddha-path is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The wisdom of sarvajñā is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Learning the bodhisattva-path is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Arising from the indistinct is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Quiescence being unborn is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The rootless is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The rootless being equally without difference, abiding in conformity with the dharma, is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The dharma of quiescent concentration is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The original limit and the unconditioned are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Arising from what is without substance is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Arising from empty quiescence and non-arising is without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. This, Venerable Pūrṇa, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's pāramitā of being without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The wisdom of sarvajñā, the rootless wisdom, the wisdom of complete compassion, and what is accomplished through ever-higher progress: all are also without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Progressing ever higher: giving, morality, patience, vigor, concentration, and wisdom. Progressing and ascending ever higher: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Ascending ever higher to abide in the wisdom of sarvajñā and the wisdom of complete compassion: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Converting sentient beings: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Purifying buddha-fields: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Making offerings to the buddha world-honored ones: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Hearing and studying the scriptures: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Never departing from the buddhas: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Never losing supernatural powers: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Not departing from the five faculties: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Not releasing the dhāraṇī: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Not abandoning samādhi: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Generating compassion on the path: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. The wisdom of sarvajñā: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Turning the dharma-wheel: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Converting sentient beings and preserving the three vehicles: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation."

Subhūti said to Pūrṇa Maitrāyaṇīputra: "This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's six pāramitās: without attachment, without bondage, without liberation. Awakening to all dharmas of true awakening, arising from the indistinct, still and tranquil, together with the unborn. This, Pūrṇa, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahā-saṃnāha-saṃnaddha of being without attachment, without bondage, without liberation."

### Chapter Sixteen: Samādhi

The Venerable Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "God among Gods! What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna armor? What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna? What does one who studies the Great Vehicle aspire to in the Vehicle? Where does the Vehicle abide, and from where does it arise? Within the Vehicle, who accomplishes the Vehicle?"

The Buddha told Subhūti: "As Subhūti has asked: 'What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's Vehicle?' The six pāramitās are the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. What six? The dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā. What is the dāna-pāramitā? Here, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva reveres and generates the mind abiding in sarvajñā and practices giving, not begrudging anything internal or external, giving all to sentient beings, making it firm and strong, without any enmity, and thus encouraging them toward anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's dāna-pāramitā. What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's śīla-pāramitā? Here, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva reveres and generates the mind abiding in sarvajñā, personally practicing the ten wholesome courses of action, and further encouraging others with the ten wholesome courses so they do not fall into delusion, without any attainment. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's śīla-pāramitā, without any loss, not falling into delusion, without any attainment."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "God among Gods! What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's kṣānti-pāramitā?"

The Buddha told Subhūti: "Here, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva personally and completely fulfills patience and converts others, establishing them in patience, not falling into delusion, without any attainment. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's kṣānti-pāramitā!"

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "God among Gods! What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's vīrya-pāramitā?"

The Buddha told Subhūti: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, whose mind reveres the wisdom of sarvajñā, regarding the five pāramitās does not distance oneself from them, and converts sentient beings through the five pāramitās, not falling into delusion, without any attainment. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's vīrya-pāramitā!"

Subhūti further asked the World-Honored One: "God among Gods! What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's dhyāna-pāramitā?"

The Buddha told Subhūti: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, who reveres and generates the mind abiding in the wisdom of sarvajñā, personally always practices meditation in samādhi through upāya-kauśalya, without following concentration to be reborn, and also teaches others to learn meditation, not falling into delusion, without any attainment. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's dhyāna-pāramitā!"

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "God among Gods! What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's prajñāpāramitā?"

The Buddha told Subhūti: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, who reveres and generates the mind of the wisdom of sarvajñā, regarding all dharmas without reliance, observing all dharmas as originally pure, not falling into delusion, without any attainment. Regarding all dharmas without any attachment, observing all dharmas as originally pure, one then uses this dharma to convert sentient beings, not falling into delusion, without any attainment. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's prajñāpāramitā. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: the internal is empty, the external is also empty, the internal and external are completely empty, emptiness is also empty, extending to great emptiness, the emptiness of the true and wondrous, the emptiness of purity, the emptiness of the conditioned, the emptiness of the unconditioned, the emptiness of the natural, the emptiness of all dharmas, the emptiness of the unobtainable, the emptiness of what has no emptiness and is itself empty, and the emptiness of what is perceived yet is non-existent.

"What is internal emptiness? Internal dharmas are the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind. What the eye sees is empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure. What the ear hears is empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure. What the nose smells is empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure. What the tongue tastes is empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure. What the body receives is also empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure. What the mind cognizes is also empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure. This is called internal emptiness.

"What is external emptiness? External dharmas are form, sound, smell, taste, touch, and mental objects. Form in its nature is also empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure. Sound, smell, taste, touch, and dharmas are empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure.

"What is the emptiness of internal and external dharmas? The internal six sense-fields and the external six sense-fields: this is the emptiness of internal and external dharmas. What is the emptiness of external dharmas? They are indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because they are originally pure. Internal dharmas and external dharmas are thus completely empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because they are originally pure. This is the emptiness of internal and external dharmas.

"What is the emptiness of emptiness? All dharmas are empty, all dharmas are empty, and this emptiness too is empty. This is called the emptiness of emptiness.

"What is great emptiness? The eastern direction is empty, the southern direction, western direction, northern direction, northeast, southwest, northwest, southeast, above, and below are all also completely empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because they are originally pure.

"What is the emptiness of the true and wondrous? It is the unconditioned. The unconditioned is empty in the unconditioned, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure. This is called the emptiness of the true and wondrous.

"What is the emptiness of what exists? The desire realm, form realm, and formless realm are empty, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because they are originally pure.

"What is the emptiness of the unconditioned? The unconditioned does not arise and does not cease, is not autonomous, and has no abode, yet abides in the truth. This is the emptiness of the unconditioned. The emptiness of the unconditioned is indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because it is originally pure.

"What is ultimate emptiness? Ultimate emptiness is that whose limit or edge cannot be apprehended. Why? Because it is originally pure. This is called ultimate emptiness.

"What is the emptiness of the far-reaching? It is that whose coming is not seen, which cannot be apprehended. Why? Because it is originally pure. This is called the emptiness of the far-reaching.

"What is the emptiness of non-differentiation? There is no dharma that can be abandoned, and nothing that abides. Why? Because it is originally pure. This is the emptiness of non-differentiation.

"What is the emptiness of original purity? It completely comprehends all dharmas as originally pure, conditioned and unconditioned, neither made by śrāvakas nor made by pratyekabuddhas. This is called the emptiness of original purity.

"What is the emptiness of all dharmas? All dharmas means: form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness; the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind; form, sound, smell, taste, touch, and dharmas; eye-form-consciousness, ear-sound-consciousness, nose-smell-consciousness, tongue-taste-consciousness, body-touch-consciousness, and mind-dharma-consciousness; what the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind contact and the feelings they occasion; conditioned dharmas and unconditioned dharmas. This is the emptiness of all dharmas. The dharma of all dharmas is empty, without any destruction, indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because they are originally pure. This is the emptiness of all dharmas.

"What is the emptiness of natural characteristics? Form's characteristic is that form is without any existent characteristic; the characteristic of feeling, the characteristic of perception, the characteristic of the arising-and-perishing of formations, the characteristic of knowing that consciousness knows: feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also likewise. The eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind; form, sound, smell, taste, touch, and dharmas; the eighteen elements; all contacted conditioned and unconditioned dharma-characteristics: these are the emptiness of the natural characteristics of all dharmas.

"What is the emptiness of the unobtainable non-existent? All dharmas cannot be apprehended, are without any destruction or harm, are indestructible and imperishable. Why? Because they are originally pure. This is called the emptiness of the unobtainable non-existent.

"What is the emptiness of non-existence? Seeking what exists in form and appearance, one cannot apprehend it. This is called the emptiness of non-existence.

"What is the emptiness of the natural? There being no conjunction or assemblage is the natural. This is the emptiness of the natural.

"What is the emptiness of what is non-existent and natural? What is natural has no conjunction or assemblage. This is the emptiness of what is non-existent and natural.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, what exists is empty in what exists. What does not exist is empty in non-existence. What is natural is empty in its nature. What is for the sake of others is empty in being for others.

"What is the emptiness of what exists in what exists? It is the five aggregates. The five aggregates are empty in what exists. This is the emptiness of what exists in what exists.

"What is the emptiness of non-existence in non-existence? It is the unconditioned. The unconditioned is empty because it is unconditioned. This is the emptiness of non-existence in non-existence.

"What is the emptiness of what is naturally empty? Emptiness is without any characteristic, without any action, and without any perception. This is the emptiness of the natural!

"What is the emptiness of being for the sake of others? Whether or not the Tathāgata appears in the world, the dharma constantly abides; the dharma-realm is quiescent; what is rootless is thus the original limit. Regarding this, it is empty for the sake of others. This is called the emptiness of being for the sake of others. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: the Śūraṅgama Samādhi! There is also a samādhi called True Seal, a samādhi called Lion's Sport, a samādhi called Auspicious Moon, a samādhi called Moon Banner Blossom, a samādhi called Surpassing All Dharmas, a samādhi called Contemplating the Summit, a samādhi called Distinguishing All Dharmas, a samādhi called Discerning Banner Blossom, a samādhi called Vajra Comparison, a samādhi called Entering the Dharma Seal, a samādhi called Emitting Light Without Seizure, a samādhi called King of Concentration, a samādhi called Well-Abiding, a samādhi called Emitting Light, a samādhi called Power of Vigor, a samādhi called Equal Transcendence, a samādhi called Distinguishing and Conforming, a samādhi called Entering All Words, a samādhi called Illuminating All Directions, a samādhi called Dhāraṇī Seal, a samādhi called Without Seizure, a samādhi called Equally Guiding the Ocean Seal of All Dharmas, a samādhi called Pervading Empty Space, a samādhi called Vajra Seat of Awakening, a samādhi called Surpassing All Jewels, a samādhi called Illumination, a samādhi called Unblinking, a samādhi called Abiding Without Ultimacy, a samādhi called Discernment, a samādhi called Stainless Lamp Light, a samādhi called Immeasurable Light, a samādhi called Light-Creating, a samādhi called Universal Illumination, a samādhi called Guiding All Purities, a samādhi called Stainless Radiance, a samādhi called For the Sake of Delight, a samādhi called Wisdom Lamp, a samādhi called Inexhaustible, a samādhi called Majestic Power, a samādhi called Utterly Exhausting, a samādhi called Without Distinction, a samādhi called Opening and Penetrating, a samādhi called Sun Lamp Light, a samādhi called Moon Free From Stain, a samādhi called Pure Illumination, a samādhi called Having Illumination, a samādhi called Accomplishing What Should Be Done, a samādhi called Wisdom Blossom, a samādhi called Vajra Comparison, a samādhi called Well-Established Aspiration, a samādhi called Jewel Accumulation, a samādhi called Surpassing Dharma Seal, a samādhi called Dharma Universal, a samādhi called Victorious Delight, a samādhi called Crossing Beyond the Summit of Dharmas, a samādhi called Having Destruction, a samādhi called Distinguishing All Phrases, a samādhi called Equally Creating Letters, a samādhi called Departing From Letters, a samādhi called Eliminating and Severing Conditions, a samādhi called Departing From Action, a samādhi called Without Action, a samādhi called Practice Without Reaching Completion, a samādhi called Removing Darkness, a samādhi called Traces of Practice, a samādhi called Unmoving, a samādhi called Crossing Beyond Realms, a samādhi called Discerning All Virtues, a samādhi called Discerning What Abides, a samādhi called Pure Flower Adornment, a samādhi called Factor of Awakening Phrase, a samādhi called Immeasurable Lamp Light, a samādhi called Equal Without Equal, a samādhi called Crossing Beyond All Dharmas, a samādhi called Severing the Past, a samādhi called Departing From Action, a samādhi called Departing From Abiding, a samādhi called One Purification, a samādhi called Guiding Practices and Affairs, a samādhi called One Affair, a samādhi called Mastering All Affairs, a samādhi called Eliminating Weariness of All Actions, a samādhi called Entering Concordant Image Sound, a samādhi called Liberating Sound Teaching Letters and Words, a samādhi called Blazing Radiance, a samādhi called Characteristic Purification, a samādhi called Signlessness, a samādhi called Creating All Instruments, a samādhi called Not Delighting in Any Suffering or Pleasure, a samādhi called Being Inexhaustible, a samādhi called Dhāraṇī Phrase, a samādhi called Guarding All Right and Wrong, a samādhi called Entering All Form and Formlessness, a samādhi called Soundless Severing of Sound, a samādhi called Stainless Radiance, a samādhi called Guiding the Essential, a samādhi called Stainless Full Moon, a samādhi called Great Purification, a samādhi called All Light Illuminating the World, a samādhi called Universal Illumination, a samādhi called Guiding Space, a samādhi called Equal Guiding, a samādhi called Nameless Ultimate Without Delight, a samādhi called Ultimately Rootless Abiding, a samādhi called Body at Ease in Due Time, a samādhi called Speech Eliminating Thoughts of Empty Space, and a samādhi called Liberating the Formless from the Indistinct: the one hundred and ten concentrations without attachment!

"What is the Śūraṅgama Samādhi? With this concentration, one enters into and pervades all samādhi practices. This is called the Śūraṅgama Samādhi. What is the True Seal Samādhi? With this concentration, one seals all samādhis at all times. This is called the True Seal Samādhi. What is the Lion's Sport Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one delights in all concentrations. This is called the Lion's Sport Samādhi. What is the Auspicious Moon Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all is equal and without any existence. This is called the Auspicious Moon Samādhi. What is the Moon Banner Blossom Samādhi? Abiding in this samādhi-concentration, one universally holds the banner of all samādhis. This is called the Moon Banner Blossom Samādhi. What is the Surpassing All Dharmas Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all completely reaches equality. This is called the Surpassing All Dharmas Samādhi. What is the Contemplating the Summit Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one contemplates and perceives the summit of all samādhi-concentrations. This is called the Contemplating the Summit Samādhi. What is the Distinguishing the Dharma-Realm Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one can distinguish all existing dharma-realms. This is called the Distinguishing the Dharma-Realm Samādhi. What is the Discerning Banner Blossom Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all concentrations ultimately hold the banner. This is called the Discerning Banner Blossom Samādhi. What is the Vajra Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all is equal, and nothing can destroy it. This is called the Vajra Samādhi. What is the Entering the Dharma Seal Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one immediately enters the seal of all dharmas. This is called the Dharma Seal Samādhi. What is the Well-Abiding King Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all dharmas are established by the king of samādhis. This is called the Well-Abiding King Samādhi. What is the Emitting Radiance Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis emanate radiance. This is called the Emitting Radiance Samādhi. What is the Power of Vigor Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis are aroused through the power of vigor. This is called the Power of Vigor Samādhi. What is the Equal Transcendence Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis all reach equality. This is called the Equal Transcendence Samādhi. What is the Conforming to Entering Verbal Teaching Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one universally enters and conforms to sounds of intentional speech. This is called the Conforming to Verbal Teaching Samādhi. What is the Entering All Verbal Teachings Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all follow the verbal teaching of samādhi. This is called the Entering Verbal Teaching Samādhi. What is the Illuminating All Directions Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one illuminates the concentrations of all directions. This is called the Illuminating All Directions Samādhi. What is the Dhāraṇī Seal Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one retains the seal of all samādhis. This is called the Dhāraṇī Seal Samādhi. What is the Without Seizure Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one immediately never forgets any concentration. This is called the Without Seizure Samādhi. What is the Equally Guiding the Ocean Seal of All Dharmas Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one practices equally and contemplates, guiding and controlling. This is called the Equally Guiding the Ocean Seal Samādhi. What is the Pervading Empty Space Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis pervade empty space everywhere. This is called the Pervading Empty Space Samādhi. What is the Vajra Seat of Awakening Samādhi? Abiding in this samādhi-concentration, one retains the seat of awakening of all concentrations. This is called the Vajra Seat of Awakening Samādhi. What is the Surpassing All Jewels Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one eliminates all dust and defilement, and all desires cannot blemish it. This is called the Surpassing All Jewels Samādhi. What is the Illumination Samādhi? Abiding in this samādhi-concentration, one brings all to equality, and illuminates all paths without any illumination. This is called the Illumination Samādhi. What is the Unblinking Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis one does not seek any dharma. This is called the Unblinking Samādhi. What is the Abiding Without Ultimacy Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any dharma of the three realms as having any abode. This is called the Abiding Without Ultimacy Samādhi. What is the Discernment Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, without mind or thought, where dharmas tend. This is called the Discernment Samādhi. What is the Stainless Radiance Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis mutually illumine. This is called the Stainless Radiance Samādhi. What is the Immeasurable Light Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, the radiance is without any place it does not illuminate. This is called the Immeasurable Light Samādhi. What is the Light-Creating Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, if one attains samādhi, all concentrations emit radiance. This is called the Light-Creating Samādhi. What is the Universal Illumination Samādhi? Attaining this concentration, all samādhi doors naturally emanate radiance. This is called the Universal Illumination Samādhi. What is the Guiding All Purities Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one attains universal purity and equality of all samādhis. This is called the Guiding All Purities Samādhi. What is the Stainless Radiance Samādhi?
