Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis one eliminates all defilements and reduces them to ash. This is called the Stainless Radiance Samādhi. What is the Delight Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one delights in all samādhis. This is called the Delight Samādhi. What is the Wisdom Lamp Light Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one illuminates all samādhis. This is called the Wisdom Lamp Light Samādhi. What is the Inexhaustible Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis there is no exhaustion, no non-exhaustion, and one does not perceive exhaustion or non-exhaustion. This is called the Inexhaustible Samādhi. What is the Majestic Power Phrase Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all is equally endowed with majestic power, magnificent radiance illuminating far. This is called the Majestic Power Phrase Samādhi. What is the Eliminating All Exhaustion Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one perceives all samādhis as entirely inexhaustible; one perceives yet without any root and without any perception. This is called the Eliminating All Exhaustion Samādhi. What is the Without Distinction Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all is equally without attachment, without thought, without any affliction, and without any condition. This is called the Without Distinction Samādhi. What is the Opening and Penetrating Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any dharma as having any penetration or any delusion. This is called the Opening and Penetrating Samādhi. What is the Sun Lamp Light Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one opens all samādhi doors and emanates radiance. This is called the Sun Lamp Light Samādhi. What is the Moon Free From Stain Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis one uses radiance to remove darkness. This is called the Moon Free From Stain Samādhi. What is the Pure Lamp Light Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis one universally protects all four analytical knowledges. This is called the Pure Lamp Light Samādhi. What is the Having Illumination Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one illuminates all samādhi doors. This is called the Having Illumination Samādhi. What is the Accomplishing What Should Be Done Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one approaches all samādhis and accomplishes what should be done; and moreover, the Accomplishing What Should Be Done Samādhi, when established in concentration, universally perceives the wisdom blossoms of all samādhis. This is called the Accomplishing What Should Be Done Samādhi. What is the Vajra Comparison Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one eliminates all dharmas of action, and no longer perceives any suffering or affliction. This is called the Vajra Comparison Samādhi. What is the Mind-Abiding Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, the mind does not waver, does not open or close, does not illuminate, does not perceive any arising, and does not think: 'There is this mind.' This is called the Mind-Abiding Samādhi. What is the Universal World Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one universally perceives all samādhi-concentrations, and there is nothing not illuminated. This is called the Universal World Samādhi. What is the Well-Established Aspiration Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all is universally and peacefully established in all samādhis. What is the Jewel Accumulation Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one universally perceives all practitioners of samādhi as accumulated jewels. This is called the Jewel Accumulation Samādhi. What is the Surpassing Dharma Seal Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one equally seals all dharmas; what has not been sealed is all seen to be sealed, completely and ultimately. This is called the Surpassing Dharma Seal Samādhi. What is the Dharma Equality Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any dharma as equal or uneven. This is called the Dharma Equality Samādhi. What is the Victorious Delight Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one conquers all pleasurable dharmas. This is called the Victorious Delight Samādhi. What is the Crossing Beyond the Summit of Dharmas Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one harmonizes and settles above all dharmas, crossing beyond all samādhis. This is called the Crossing Beyond the Summit of Dharmas Samādhi. What is the Destruction and Elimination Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one eliminates all dharmas in all samādhis and destroys them. This is called the Destruction and Elimination Samādhi. What is the Distinguishing All Dharmas Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one can distinguish all samādhis, comprehending and discerning the phrases of all dharmas. This is called the Distinguishing All Dharmas Samādhi. What is the Equally Creating Letters Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one distinguishes and comprehends the equal letters attained through samādhi. This is called the Equally Creating Letters Samādhi. What is the Eliminating All Letters Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis there is not a single letter, and nothing that can be apprehended. This is called the Eliminating All Letters Samādhi. What is the Eliminating and Severing Conditions Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one severs all samādhi conditions, without any confusion. This is called the Eliminating and Severing Conditions Samādhi. What is the Without Action Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not apprehend any dharma as having any action or creation. This is called the Without Action Samādhi. What is the Departing From Action Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not apprehend any dharma as created through conditions. This is called the Departing From Action Samādhi. What is the Practice Without Reaching Completion Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not apprehend the ultimate limit of any samādhi practice. This is called the Practice Without Reaching Completion Samādhi. What is the Removing All Darkness Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis remove all darkness, extinguishing all confusion and bringing about purity. This is called the Removing All Darkness Samādhi. What is the Practicing All Phrases Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one universally perceives the practices of all samādhis. This is called the Practicing All Phrases Samādhi. What is the Unmoving Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any samādhi as having any trembling or movement. This is called the Unmoving Samādhi. What is the Crossing Beyond All Realms Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis cross beyond all wrong turnings without any error, conforming to the correct meaning. This is called the Crossing Beyond All Realms Samādhi. What is the Discerning All Virtues Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one discerns all dharmas and comprehends the samādhis of sentient beings. This is called the Discerning All Virtues Samādhi. What is the Discerning What Abides Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all concentrations, one seeks the root of the mind yet cannot apprehend it. This is called the Discerning What Abides Samādhi. What is the Pure Flower Adornment Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, attaining all samādhis, all is completely pure and universally adorned with flowers. This is called the Pure Flower Adornment Samādhi. What is the Factor of Awakening Phrase Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis swiftly attain the factors of awakening. This is called the Factor of Awakening Phrase Samādhi. What is the Immeasurable Eloquence Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one immediately attains immeasurable eloquence that follows practice and makes distinctions. This is called the Immeasurable Eloquence Samādhi. What is the Equal Without Equal Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all concentrations attain the Equal Without Equal Samādhi, able to cause all what is wrong to reach equality. This is called the Equal Without Equal Samādhi. What is the Crossing Beyond All Dharmas Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one can cross beyond all three realms. This is called the Crossing Beyond All Dharmas Samādhi. What is the Severing All Actions Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one perceives all dharmas in all samādhi-concentrations as completely severed. This is called the Severing All Actions Samādhi. What is the Without Intention Without Destruction Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, having attained all concentrations, one attains all dharmas as ultimately returning to decay and ruin. This is called the Without Intention Without Destruction Samādhi. What is the Without Abode Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any dharma as having any abode. This is called the Without Abode Samādhi. What is the One Purity Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any dharma as having duality. This is called the One Purity Samādhi. What is the Guiding All Practices and Affairs Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any dharma as having any causal destination. This is called the Guiding All Practices and Affairs Samādhi. What is the Mastering All Affairs Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis do not perceive duality, nor perceive anything at all. This is called the Mastering All Affairs Samādhi. What is the Eliminating All Existences and Severing All Roots Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis one eliminates all affairs and attains wisdom; what one enters, one does not encounter. This is called the Eliminating All Existences and Severing All Roots Samādhi. What is the Entering Concordant Sound Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not follow the various sounds of samādhi. This is called the Entering Concordant Sound Samādhi. What is the Crossing Beyond All Words, Letters, and Sounds Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one completely crosses beyond all practices involving letters and words, and perceives nothing. This is called the Crossing Beyond All Words, Letters, and Sounds Samādhi. What is the Blazing Radiance Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one universally illuminates, conquering with radiant splendor. This is called the Blazing Radiance Samādhi. What is the Purification of All Characteristics Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one adorns all characteristics with merit. This is called the Purification of All Characteristics Samādhi. What is the Signlessness Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis forever do not perceive any characteristic. This is called the Signlessness Samādhi. What is the Completely Equipped Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all that is sought is universally and completely fulfilled. This is called the Completely Equipped Samādhi. What is the Not Delighting in Suffering or Ease Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any suffering or ease in any samādhi. This is called the Not Delighting in Suffering or Ease Samādhi. What is the Inexhaustible Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis there is no exhaustion and nothing perceived. This is called the Inexhaustible Samādhi. What is the Dhāraṇī Phrase Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one retains all the affairs of all samādhis. This is called the Dhāraṇī Phrase Samādhi. What is the Guarding All Right and Wrong Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis one forever does not perceive right or wrong. This is called the Guarding All Right and Wrong Samādhi. What is the Eliminating All Form and Formlessness Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis one does not perceive any form; forever without form. This is called the Eliminating All Form and Formlessness Samādhi. What is the Soundless Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one perceives all dharmas as without sound and without voice. This is called the Soundless Samādhi. What is the Stainless Radiance Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not apprehend any defilement in the radiance of all samādhis. This is called the Stainless Radiance Samādhi. What is the Essential Guiding Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not perceive any samādhi as having what is essential or inessential, guided or unguided. This is called the Essential Guiding Samādhi. What is the Full Moon Free From Stain Radiance Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all is equally endowed with complete and perfect merit and blessing, like the moon at its fullest on the fifteenth day. This is called the Full Moon Free From Stain Radiance Samādhi. What is the Great Purification Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all is equally, immeasurably pure and adorned. This is called the Great Purification Samādhi. What is the Universally Illuminating the World Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all is equally able to illuminate all dharmas. This is called the Universally Illuminating the World Samādhi. What is the Universal Concentration Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all concentrations are without confusion, yet one does not apprehend one-pointedness. This is called the Universal Concentration Samādhi. What is the Guiding Space Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one equally guides all those who do not delight in the dharma, causing them to attain delight. This is called the Guiding Space Samādhi. What is the Equally Guiding Sarvajñā Space Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all matters of equal guiding, there is nothing guided. This is called the Equally Guiding Sarvajñā Space Samādhi. What is the Nameless Ultimate Without Delight Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one does not apprehend any name or designation, and nothing is obtained. This is called the Nameless Ultimate Without Delight Samādhi. What is the Abiding in Rootlessness Without Mind Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one abides in all samādhis, universally entering rootlessness, without any turning or seeking. This is called the Abiding in Rootlessness Without Mind Samādhi. What is the Body at Ease in Due Time Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, regarding all samādhis one forever does not apprehend or perceive a body. This is called the Body at Ease in Due Time Samādhi. What is the Speech Eliminating Thoughts of Empty Space Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, all samādhis do not apprehend the destination of speech and words. This is called the Speech Eliminating Thoughts of Empty Space Samādhi. What is the Liberating the Formless from the Indistinct Samādhi? Abiding in this concentration, one attains empty space: unconditioned, innumerable, and all dharmas quiescent. This is called the Liberating the Formless from the Indistinct Samādhi. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's prajñāpāramitā mahāyāna."

## Fascicle Seven

### Chapter Seventeen: Contemplation

The Buddha told Subhūti: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the four foundations of mindfulness. What are the four foundations of mindfulness? Internally contemplating the body, one is not identical with the body, without any conception and without apprehending the body. Contemplating the external body, one is not identical with the body, without any conception and without apprehending the body; in this one is calm and composed, regulating the mind. Contemplating the world of ignorance and sorrow, internally contemplating feelings and the mind and dharmas, in this one is calm and composed, regulating the mind. Perceiving the world of ignorance and sorrow, contemplating external feelings, one is not identical with feelings, without any conception and without apprehending the body. Contemplating internal perception, one is not identical with perception, without any thought of perception, and does not apprehend perception. Contemplating external perception, one is not identical with perception, without any thought of perception, and does not apprehend perception. Contemplating internal dharmas, one is not identical with dharmas, without any thought of dharmas, and does not apprehend dharmas. Contemplating external dharmas, one is not identical with dharmas, without any thought of dharmas, and does not apprehend dharmas; in this quiescence one regulates the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow. How, Subhūti, does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva internally contemplate the body? This bodhisattva-mahāsattva knows what the mind practices: whether standing, having stood; also knows having sat or about to sit; also knows whether walking or lying, having been or about to walk or lie; whatever the body should attend to, wherever the mind tends, one knows all of it. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's contemplation of the internal body. In this, calm and composed, one regulates the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, in going and returning, is calm and composed, observing and looking without any rashness. In proceeding and stopping, bending and stretching, putting on robes and holding the bowl, eating and drinking, lying and sleeping, resting and attending to disciplined conduct, going and coming, sitting and rising, lying and waking: whatever is spoken, one always maintains composure. One delights in seclusion and the mind does not race about. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practicing the prajñāpāramitā, internally contemplating the body, yet the body cannot be apprehended.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, with single-pointed mind, observes the inhalation and exhalation of the breath. Whether the breath is long or short, one knows all of it. Whether the mental breath is near or far, one knows all of it. Whether the mental breath is slow or fast, one knows all of it. Whether the mental breath is abrupt or gentle, one knows all of it. Just as a wheel-turning sage-king knows the length, breadth, and extent of the land! Just as a potter making vessels knows their size, depth, and shallowness! Likewise, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva knows the inhalation and exhalation, length and shortness, slowness and quickness, hardness and softness of the breath. The bodhisattva thus contemplates the internal body, knows it in calm composure, and regulates the mind, causing it to conform to the dharma-teaching. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's internal contemplation of the body, regulating the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva contemplates the four elements of the body: the present body has the earth element, water element, fire element, and wind element. Just as a butcher, taking a sharp knife, kills an ox or animal and cuts it into four sections, and having made four sections, sits and examines it, and there is no ox; it is a conjunction of conditions. Likewise, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, practicing the prajñāpāramitā, contemplates this body, and the body has the earth element, water element, fire element, and wind element. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, practicing the prajñāpāramitā, internally contemplates the body, yet does not perceive the body and has nothing to apprehend.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva examines the body from head to foot. The body has hair, marrow, and brain, foul and impure, fully replete. This body has head-hair, body-hair, nails, teeth, skin, hide, sinews, veins, bones, joints, intestines, stomach, belly, liver, lungs, heart, kidneys, the five organs, blood, flesh, fat, marrow, mucus, saliva, filth, impurities, feces, and urine. Just as a farmer uses a sack to store various kinds of grain: sesame, rice, millet, beans, barley, wheat, and paddy. A person with clear eyes pours it out on the ground and distinguishes each one, knowing: 'This is sesame oil, this is polished rice, this is beans and millet, this is paddy.' Likewise, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's present body, from foot to head: head-hair, body-hair, nails, teeth, skin, hide, sinews, veins, bones, joints, intestines, stomach, belly, liver, lungs, heart, kidneys, the five organs, blood, flesh, fat, marrow, mucus, saliva, filth, impurities, feces, and urine. Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva internally contemplates the body, regulates the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be apprehended.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva contemplates the present body subject to cold and heat. If one's life ends after one day, or three days, four days, or five days, the body swells and bloats, its color turns blue, it rots and gives off a foul stench, and pus and blood flow out. Reckoning such a body, it cannot escape the dharma of impermanence. Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva internally contemplates the body! Knowing calm composure, one regulates the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be apprehended and nothing to be perceived.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva contemplates a person after death, subject to cold, heat, sun, and wind. After death, one day, or two, three, four, five, six, or seven days, it is eaten by birds and crows, foxes, wolves, bears, tigers, leopards, owls, dogs, and hounds. Innumerable worms emerge from the body and in turn consume it. That person examines the places where the body once traveled. The dharma is impermanent; all is dispersed and separated. None escape this. Internally contemplating the body, one regulates the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be perceived.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, if one sees a body after the impermanence of death, subject to cold, heat, sun, and wind, swollen and bloated with blue discoloration, consumed by birds and beasts, fetid and impure, then contemplates one's own body as likewise being so. One regulates the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be apprehended and nothing to be perceived.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, if one contemplates a body after death, subject to cold, heat, sun, and wind, the bones and joints connected like interlocking chains, smeared with flesh and soaked in blood, bound by sinews, wrapped in skin and covered in hide, then contemplates one's own body, settling the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be apprehended and nothing to be perceived.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, if one sees a person after death, with only white bones hooked and chained together, with blood, veins, skin, flesh, sinews, and marrow, then examines them: 'This present body, its dharma is thus: dispersed and separated, this is the dharma of impermanence; none escape it.' Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva contemplates the body, settling the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be apprehended and nothing to be perceived.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, if one sees bones with sinews and marrow crumbled and scattered, returning to merge with the earth, observes thus: 'This present body, its dharma is thus.' Internally contemplating the body, one regulates the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be apprehended and nothing to be perceived.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, if one sees bones scattered on the ground, east, west, south, and north: foot bones in one place, kneecaps, vertebrae, ribs, and skull each in different places, then examines them: 'This present body, its dharma is thus; hands and feet dispersed and separated, this is the dharma of impermanence; none escape it.' Internally contemplating the body, settling the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be apprehended and nothing to be perceived.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva contemplates the body. Long after death, bones scattered on the ground, accumulated over years beyond counting and beyond measure, blue bones crumbled and merged with ash and earth: 'This present body, its dharma is thus: dispersed and separated, this is the dharma of impermanence; none escape it.' Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva internally contemplates the body, settling the mind regarding matters of worldly ignorance and sorrow, yet there is nothing to be apprehended and nothing to be perceived. Feeling, perception, and contemplation of dharmas are also likewise. Using this to guide those who have first generated the aspiration with the contemplation of impermanence, gradually entering into emptiness until they know rootlessness; for those who have generated the aspiration and are accomplished, one contemplates the internal and external body and there is no body, contemplates internal and external perception and there is no perception, contemplates internal and external dharmas and there are no dharmas; there is no contemplation and nothing to be perceived. The path does not depart from the worldly, and the worldly does not depart from the path; both are equally empty, and there is nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the mahāyāna is the four correct exertions. What are the four correct exertions? Here the bodhisattva-mahāsattva: regarding evil and unwholesome dharmas not yet arisen, if they should arise, one controls them and prevents their arising. With earnest vigor, one gathers the root of the mind and severs all flaws; evil, unwholesome, unlawful matters, as soon as they arise, one immediately severs them, with earnest vigor gathering the mind, bringing about equal liberation. Regarding roots of wholesome virtue, should they arise and should one wish to sever them, with earnest vigor one rescues and gathers the mind, bringing about equal liberation. Harboring wholesome dharmas that arise, one firmly abides without losing them, contemplating them completely, broadly and universally perfecting them with increasing joy. With earnest vigor one rescues and gathers the mind, bringing about equal liberation. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be perceived. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna!

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the mahāyāna is the five faculties: the faculty of faith, the faculty of vigor, the faculty of mindfulness, the faculty of concentration, and the faculty of wisdom. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the five powers. What are the five powers? The power of faith, the power of vigor, the power of mindfulness, the power of concentration, and the power of wisdom. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna of the five powers. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the seven factors of awakening. What are the seven factors of awakening? Here, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva exclusively cultivates the factor of investigation, relying on quiescence, without any desire, without any reliance, eliminating contention and abandoning all dharmas. This is the factor of investigation. The factor of vigor: relying on quiescence, without any desire, without any reliance, eliminating contention and abandoning all dharmas. This is the factor of vigor. The factor of joy, the factor of faith, the factor of tranquility, the factor of concentration, and the factor of equanimity: relying on quiescence, without any desire, without any reliance, eliminating contention and abandoning all dharmas. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna practice of the seven factors of awakening. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the eightfold noble path of the sages. What are the eight? Right view, right mindfulness, right speech, right action, right livelihood, right effort, right thought, and right concentration. These are the eight noble paths of the sages. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the three samādhi categories. What are the three? The samādhi of emptiness, the samādhi of signlessness, and the samādhi of wishlessness. What is the samādhi of emptiness? The characteristics of dharmas being empty, emptiness being a gate of liberation, this constitutes signlessness. Signlessness being a gate of liberation, what is practiced is without any practice. This is the gate of liberation of wishlessness. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. Having attained this, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna: one should distinguish and comprehend habituations, sever and extinguish, awaken to the path, know what is exhausted, and know non-arising. Comprehending all dharmas, one distinguishes non-self. Comprehending gentleness and the matter of final cessation, one knows one's own mind and comprehends the minds of others. This is called wisdom. What is distinguishing? Knowing suffering in suffering, without any arising and without any origination: this is called distinguishing suffering. What is comprehending habituations? It means eliminating habituations so they do not arise again. What is severing and extinguishing? It means suffering has been exhausted, without any root. What is awakening to the path? It is the eightfold noble path of the sages. What is knowing what is exhausted? It means the cessation of desire, anger, and delusion. What is knowing non-arising? It is the wisdom of non-arising from the unborn. What is comprehending dharma-wisdom? It is the wisdom that severs the transgressions and merits created by the five aggregates. What is distinguishing non-self? Form is impermanent; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are impermanent. The eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are not one's own possessions. Form, sound, smell, taste, touch, and dharmas are not one's own possessions. Eye-form-consciousness, ear-sound-consciousness, nose-smell-consciousness, tongue-taste-consciousness, body-touch-consciousness, and mind-dharma-consciousness are also not one's own possessions. What is comprehending gentleness and the matter of final cessation? There are sighs and much arising. What is knowing one's own mind? Knowing the original roots from of old. What is knowing the minds of others? Being able to distinguish the thoughts and mental states of other people and sentient beings. What is wisdom-mind as it truly is? It is the wisdom of the tathāgata's sarvajñā. This is called the wisdom-mind as it truly is. Having attained it, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the three roots! The root of ordinary persons, the root of difference, and the separate root. What is the root of ordinary persons? It means those practitioners who have not yet attained the faculties of equal faith, vigor, mindfulness, concentration, and wisdom. What is the root of difference? Those practitioners who have the undifferentiated faculties of faith, vigor, mindfulness, concentration, and wisdom: this is called the root of difference. What is the separate root? Those who are not yet practitioners but who generate the great aspiration for pratyekabuddhahood, bodhisattvahood, or tathāgatahood, arhatship, and samyak-saṃbuddhahood, with the faculties of faith, vigor, mindfulness, concentration, and wisdom! This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's separate root of the mahāyāna. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the equal concentration. There are three kinds: samādhi with thought and investigation, samādhi without thought with investigation, and samādhi without thought and without investigation. What is samādhi with thought and investigation? Freed from desires, having quiescently removed all evil and unwholesome dharmas, with thought and investigation, one practices the first quiescence. This is called samādhi with thought and investigation. What is samādhi without thought with investigation? When the mind's interior is without thought but with investigation, without any attachment, reaching the second quiescence, without interior or exterior: this is called samādhi without thought with investigation. What is samādhi without thought and without investigation? Passing beyond the second and third quiescences, crossing the concentration of immeasurable wisdom, transcending the realm of immeasurable consciousness-wisdom, passing the concentration of immeasurable non-perception wisdom, and crossing the concentration of immeasurable neither-thought-nor-non-thought. This is called without thought and without investigation. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the ten recollections. What are the ten recollections? Recollection of the Buddha, recollection of the dharma, recollection of the sangha, recollection of morality, recollection of giving, recollection of the heavens, recollection of tranquility, recollection of non-arising, recollection of contemplating the body, and recollection of death. These are the ten recollections. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the four dhyānas, four formless attainments, four immeasurables, eight liberations, and the concentration of the never-before-tasted flavor. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the tathāgata's ten powers. What are the ten powers? Knowing the places and non-places of other people and sentient beings, with and without limits. Fully and truly knowing the past, future, and present causes and conditions, transgressions and merits, practices and places, and their results and retributions. Fully and truly knowing that people in the world are of many kinds, and their natures are different. Fully and truly knowing the many kinds of minds of other people and sentient beings, and their different delights. Fully and truly knowing the roots and origins of other people and sentient beings, and their different beginnings and ends. Fully and truly knowing the destinations and returns of all in the five realms. Fully and truly knowing the minds of practitioners among all people: their faculties, powers, factors of awakening, one-pointed mind, gates of liberation, and samādhi proper attainment, as well as their bondage, anger and hatred, and contention, being able to distinguish them wisely. Fully and truly knowing innumerable quiescences. Knowing the events of innumerable past kalpas. Knowing the places of innumerable past kalpas. Where sentient beings travel, one examines their deaths and destinations. The dharma-eye sees clearly through the ten directions and all buddha-fields, the five realms of birth and death, good and evil, fortune and misfortune, arising and cessation, beginning and end. Fully and truly knowing that all outflows are exhausted, without any dust or defilement, having crossed beyond thought, through wisdom-liberation in present practice, through one's own supernatural powers witnessing all practices: birth and death are severed, the holy life is praised, what should be done is done, and one knows what has not yet been crossed over. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the four fearlessnesses. What are the four fearlessnesses? 'I have already attained the equal and perfect awakening. If there are śramaṇas, brāhmaṇas, devas, or people, or those with different heavenly or different awakenings, who come wishing to dispute and seek the Buddha's faults, claiming I have not attained equal and perfect awakening: I do not perceive any auspicious sign that anyone dares to generate such intent against the Tathāgata!' None dares to conceive such a thought, therefore the Buddha abides in peace and safety, practicing without difficulty and without fear. With courageous practice one attains the unattached, and for the sake of others makes the lion's roar, teaching, distinguishing, and turning the pure dharma-wheel. No śramaṇa, brāhmaṇa, deva, Māra, or Brahmā in the heavens or the world can match the meaning of the path and dharma. 'All outflows are exhausted, without any beginning or end. If any śramaṇa, brāhmaṇa, deva, Māra, or Brahmā in the heavens or the world seeks the Buddha's faults, claiming otherwise, that the outflows are not yet exhausted': I do not perceive anyone generating such a thought to seek faults; therefore the Buddha abides in peace and safety without any fear, and for the multitude makes the lion's roar. 'I fully know the internal dharma; there is no interior or exterior, and I do not perceive a self. If any śramaṇa, brāhmaṇa, deva, Māra, or Brahmā in the heavens or the world seeks the Buddha's faults, claiming otherwise, that I do not know the internal dharma and reckon a self': I do not perceive anyone generating such a thought to seek faults; therefore the Buddha abides in peace and safety without any fear, and for the multitude makes the lion's roar. 'I teach the noble dharma: those who do not understand come to understand, those who have not reached come to reach, those without a vehicle come to have a vehicle, and I universally remove suffering with equanimity. No one can ever find any fault in the Buddha.' Because one follows the dharma, one does not violate the meaning of the path. With courage, without dread, without fear, one teaches others, turning the pure dharma-wheel and making the lion's roar. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the four analytical knowledges. What are the four? First, analysis of meaning; second, analysis of dharma; third, analysis of what accords and follows; fourth, analytical eloquence. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the eighteen unique buddha-dharmas. What are the eighteen? First, the Tathāgata has no flaw or deficiency. Second, his speech is always timely. Third, he has no deficiency of mind. Fourth, he has no forgetfulness. Fifth, he has no diverse thoughts. Sixth, he has no unsettled mind. Seventh, he has no undiscriminating observation. Eighth, he has no object of delight. Ninth, his vigor is without loss. Tenth, he never loses mindfulness. Eleventh, his wisdom is without diminishment. Twelfth, his liberation is never deficient. Thirteenth, his wisdom of crossing over to knowledge and vision is never diminished. Fourteenth, all matters of the body reach everywhere without exception. Fifteenth, all words spoken by the mouth reach everywhere without exception, enabling each to receive what is fitting. Sixteenth, all that the mind contemplates, through the wisdom-mind, one knows all its origins. Seventeenth, knowing past events of incalculable, innumerable kalpas, wisdom perceives all. Eighteenth, knowing future events of incalculable, innumerable kalpas, and knowing present events of incalculable, innumerable kalpas, wisdom perceives all. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna. Where there is attainment, there is also nothing to be attained and nothing to be obtained.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is the dhāraṇī gate. What is the dhāraṇī gate? All letters are equal, and what is spoken is equal: the gate of letters, the entry of letters. What is the gate of letters, the entry of letters and conditions? All dharmas, having passed, are also without any arising. The gate of this letter: 'la' is the gate where dharmas are free from all defilement. 'Pa' is the gate of distinguishing all meanings. 'Ca' is the gate of attaining all dharma-practices, without any attainment, without any sinking, and without any arising. 'Na' is the gate where all dharmas are free from all names and letters, reckoning their original purity, yet they cannot be apprehended. 'Rā' is the gate that completely crosses beyond all worldly dharmas of gratitude, retribution, and conditions. 'Da' is the gate where all dharmas are originally rootless, and existence and non-existence are severed. 'Ba' is the gate that completely unties the bondage of all dharmas. 'Ṭa' is the gate of burning away all dharmas and attaining purity. 'Ṣa' is the gate where all dharmas are without any obstruction and do not apprehend any matter. 'Va' is the gate of severing the sounds, phrase-traces, and destinations of all dharmas. 'Ta' is the gate where all dharmas have no root and cannot be moved or shaken. 'Ya' is the gate where all dharmas do not arise. 'Ṣṭa' is the gate where all dharmas reach their ultimate end. 'Ka' is the gate where all dharmas attain what should be done and accomplished. 'Sa' is the gate where all dharmas are attained in due time, completely and without any restriction. 'Ma' is the gate of understanding that all dharmas arise from the self. 'Ga' is the gate where all dharmas attain protection. 'Dha' is the gate where all dharmas attain their proper place. 'Ja' is the gate where all dharmas do not arise. 'Śva' is the gate where all dharmas do not arise. 'Dha' is the gate where the seeds of all dharmas have no arising or assemblage. 'Śa' is the gate where all dharmas are quiescent and do not arise. 'Kha' is the gate where all dharmas are like empty space and do not arise. 'Kṣa' is the gate where all dharmas are completely extinguished and cannot be apprehended. 'Sta' is the gate where all dharmas firmly abide in their place and cannot be moved, nor can they be apprehended. 'Jña' is the gate where the wisdom of all dharmas cannot be apprehended. 'Rtha' is the gate where all dharmas attain what is retained. 'Bha' is the gate where all dharmas attain quietude. 'Cha' is the gate where all dharmas are already burned away. 'Sma' is the gate where all dharmas are without any action. 'Hva' is the gate where all dharmas attain trustworthiness. 'Tsa' is the gate where all dharmas attain complete extinction. 'Gha' is the gate where all dharmas attain the location of the cycle. 'Ṭha' is the gate where all dharmas, having a place of abode, attain non-abiding. 'Ṇa' is the gate where all dharmas do not come, do not go, do not stand, do not sit, do not lie, do not sleep, without accordance or non-accordance, without thought or non-thought. 'Pha' is the gate where all dharmas cannot be presented. 'Ska' is the gate where all dharmas do not apprehend the five aggregates. 'Ysa' is the gate where all dharmas do not apprehend the thoughts of others. 'Śca' is the gate of abandoning all dharmas without any apprehension. Another gate: all dharmas do not apprehend any location. The gate of 'aḥ': all dharmas, ultimately reaching the limit, exhausting their location, are without birth, without death, without any existence, without any action, uprooting letters, sounds, and speech. Why? Being weary of all obstructions, without any name, without any designation, without any spoken location, it cannot be apprehended, cannot be spoken, cannot be exhausted, and cannot be perceived. For example, Subhūti, empty space is indistinct; all dharmas are also completely thus. This, Subhūti, is the dhāraṇī entry of conditions, the entry through which letters are distinguished. If there is a bodhisattva-mahāsattva who knows all these conditions and skillfully distinguishes letters, then one is no longer attached to sounds and speech, and one can progressively comprehend the destinations and tendencies of all dharmas."

### Chapter Eighteen: The Ten Abodes

The Buddha told Subhūti: "As you have asked: 'What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna saṃprasthita?' Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, practicing the six pāramitās, enters the grounds of the path. How does the bodhisattva enter the grounds of the path? Entering all dharmas, without any coming or going, without any going or destruction. All dharmas cannot be known in any place, without any conception. One practices the ten grounds of the path without perceiving the grounds. What is the bodhisattva's practice of the ten grounds? The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the first abode should practice ten things. What are the ten? Cultivating and refining one's aspiration without falling into delusion. Cultivating and refining compassion, eliminating all conceptions. Having an equal mind toward sentient beings without apprehending sentient beings. Practicing the work of giving, with giver and receiver being non-dual. Respecting good teachers without any contempt. Seeking the dharma as one's profession, without any attainment. Earnestly pursuing learning without any attachment. Seeking the buddha-body without conceiving of the marks. Opening and expounding dharma-matters for all sentient beings without any expectation. Abandoning arrogance, and regarding all dharmas, being without any attachment. What one speaks is truthful in deed. These are the ten things. Subhūti! This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the first ground of the path.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the second abode should practice eight dharmas. What are the eight? One's morality is pure and one has gratitude. One can know and repay kindness. One abides in the power of patience. One always practices joyfulness. One does not abandon sentient beings, being diligent in great compassion. One receives the teaching of elders. Regarding one who has gone forth, one regards them as the World-Honored One. One practices the pāramitās, aspiring and seeking skillful means. These are the eight things.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the third abode practices five dharmas. What are the five? Asking widely without weariness, not attached to written words. Converting through dharma-giving without any thought of clothing or food. Purifying buddha-fields. Encouraging roots of virtue. Also without any expectation. These are the five things.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the fourth abode should practice ten dharmas and never abandon them. What are the ten? Not abandoning seclusion. Having aspiration for few desires. Knowing contentment. Not departing from seated meditation. Not violating the precepts. Not being weary of sense-desires. Not stopping at cessation. Giving away all possessions without begrudging. Not being timid or weak. Regarding all that exists, being without any longing. These are the ten things.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the fifth abode should abandon eight things. What are the eight? Abandoning attachment to household life. Departing from bhikṣuṇīs. Abandoning restlessness. Not coveting merit. Abandoning sleep and drowsiness. Departing from anger and contention. Not praising oneself. Not disparaging others. These are the eight things.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the sixth abode is endowed with six dharmas. What are the six? The six pāramitās. Not engaging in the six negative dharmas. Not seeking the śrāvaka path, without any thought of pratyekabuddhahood, not conceiving of the lesser vehicle. When seeing beggars and supplicants, one's countenance is harmonious and joyful. When one has something to give, one does not feel sorrow. The mind does not harbor resentment. These are the six things.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the seventh abode is endowed with departing from twenty dharmas. What are the twenty? No reception. No self. Not reckoning a person. Not having a lifespan. Not conceiving of longevity. Not conceiving of permanence. Not attached to annihilation. Without any conception or attachment. Departing from views of causation. Not relying on the aggregates. Not longing for the elements. Abandoning the elements. Abandoning the sense-fields. Without conceptions of the three realms. Not attached to the Buddha. Not attached to the dharma. Not attached to the sangha. Guarding the precepts, abandoning views. Not relying on the thought of emptiness. Abandoning all wrong views, without any defilement. These are the twenty things. One should further be endowed with twenty more dharma-matters. What are the twenty? Comprehending emptiness. Not realizing signlessness. Benefiting with wishlessness. Purifying the three spheres. Having compassion for sentient beings. Not perceiving sentient beings. Without any contempt. Viewing all dharmas equally. Comprehending the meaning of the dharma. Without any differentiation. Comprehending the true and correct. Also without any attachment. The patience of non-arising. Teaching the single category. Extinguishing all conceptions. Abandoning dust and defilement. Quiescently departing from wrong views. The mind being settled. Not departing from wisdom. Without any rashness. These are the twenty.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the eighth abode is endowed with four dharmas. What are the four? Entering the minds of sentient beings, delighting in supernatural powers. Manifesting in all buddha-fields and observing them as they are. Completing one's own field and paying homage to all buddhas. Contemplating the bodies of all buddhas with the true view. These are the four dharmas.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the ninth abode should further be endowed with four dharmas. What are the four? Comprehending the roots and faculties of beings, completing the buddha-fields. Earnestly cultivating the illusion-samādhi. Converting sentient beings, causing them to create roots of virtue and abide in purity. Manifesting a complete body for all, teaching the path-meaning. These are the four things.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the tenth abode is completely endowed with twelve things. What are the twelve? Establishing protection for immeasurable places. Fulfilling all that sentient beings wish for. What the mouth proclaims: devas, nāgas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kiṃnaras, and mahoragas, hearing the sound, each understand. Eloquence is thus. Matters of the womb, the nobility of one's lineage, one's birthplace, one's retinue and homeland, renouncing the kingdom and leaving home, proceeding to the bodhi-tree, and purity and completion. All excellent virtues are fully equipped. These are the twelve.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva of the tenth ground is precisely the Buddha."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "What is the bodhisattva's cultivation and refinement of aspiration?"

The Buddha said: "Whatever roots of virtue one creates, the mind always encourages and assists toward the wisdom of sarvajñā. What is the bodhisattva's equal mind? One always aspires to sarvajñā, practicing the four immeasurables of lovingkindness, compassion, sympathetic joy, and equanimity. What is the bodhisattva's work of giving? Giving to all, without any conception. What is the bodhisattva's associating with good teachers? Converting all and establishing them on the correct path, paying homage and inquiring with faith, respect, and deference toward elders. What is the bodhisattva's endowment of seeking the dharma? Whatever dharma one seeks, the mind is always directed toward the wisdom of sarvajñā, without falling to the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas. What is the bodhisattva's earnest going forth? In every place of birth, generation after generation, one abandons worldly work without any destruction, following the tathāgata's teaching; one who has gone forth practices the supreme practice. What is the bodhisattva's seeking the buddha-body? If one sees the buddha-form, one's mind has never departed from the Buddha, until one reaches the wisdom of sarvajñā. What is the bodhisattva's opening and expounding all dharmas? If a bodhisattva, whether a buddha is presently seen or has entered nirvāṇa, teaches the dharma for sentient beings: the beginning is also good, the middle is also good, and the end is also good. The meaning is complete, subtle and wondrous, the conduct of complete purity, together with the twelve divisions of the scriptures: sūtras, merit texts, reception texts, analytical texts, indicative texts, parable texts, spoken texts, birth texts, vaipulya texts, unprecedented texts, verse texts, and conduct texts. This is the bodhisattva's twelve divisions of scriptures, opening and expounding all dharmas. What is the bodhisattva's abandoning the mind of arrogance? One has never harbored conceit and is never born into a lowly family. What is the bodhisattva's truthfulness in what one speaks? Whatever is spoken, words and deeds are in accord."

The Buddha said to Subhūti: "This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the first abode, carrying out the ten things!"

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "What is the bodhisattva's purity of the morality precepts?" The Buddha said: "The mind does not conceive of seeking the śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha vehicle, and one does not slander any bodhisattva. If there are those who violate the precepts, one admonishes and guides them, not letting them fall into the pit. What is the bodhisattva's gratitude and knowing how to repay kindness? If a bodhisattva, while practicing the bodhisattva-path, receives even a small gift, one does not forget it; how much more so with great gifts! What is the bodhisattva's abiding in the power of patience? One is always without confusion of mind toward sentient beings, and one's aspiration does not harbor harm. What is the bodhisattva's harmonious and joyful countenance? One thinks of converting sentient beings without deviating from the correct practice. What is the bodhisattva's not abandoning sentient beings? Being able to rescue, aid, and protect all people. What is the bodhisattva's drawing near to great compassion? If a bodhisattva, while practicing the path, thinks to oneself: 'For the sake of all people, through kalpas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, I shall endure in hell. Even if I see the marks of torment, I shall never slacken, and I shall cause those beings to accomplish the buddha-vehicle and attain cessation.' For all sentient beings of this kind, one's mind encourages itself thus. The subtlety and wonder is such. What is the bodhisattva's receiving the teaching of elders? One who has gone forth, if one sees a teacher, regards them as the Buddha. What is the bodhisattva's seeking the pāramitās? If the bodhisattva does not aspire to other works, does not conceive of other dharmas, without any contempt, one seeks the perfections. What is the bodhisattva's hearing widely without weariness? Whatever the buddhas, God among Gods, have spoken and expounded, and whatever the buddhas of the ten directions have spoken, one receives and upholds all of it. What is the bodhisattva's dharma-giving without thought of clothing or food? With this dharma-giving, the mind thinks thus, without conceiving of the buddha-path. What is the bodhisattva's purifying the buddha-field? Whatever roots of virtue one plants, all encourage and assist in the purification and adornment of the buddha-field. What is the bodhisattva's not being weary of birth-and-death? One always wishes to be endowed with all merit, accomplishing the roots of goodness, converting sentient beings, purifying the buddha-field, and never slackening, until one is endowed with the wisdom of sarvajñā. What is the bodhisattva's knowing shame and conscience? One never has the mind of a śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha. What is the bodhisattva's not abandoning seclusion? Not entering the grounds of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas. What is the bodhisattva's aspiring to few desires? Practicing the bodhisattva-path without any attachment, aspiring to the buddha-path. What is the bodhisattva's knowing contentment? Because one accomplishes the wisdom of sarvajñā. What is the bodhisattva's not abandoning restraint? Being able to distinguish and comprehend the deep dharma. What is the bodhisattva's not abandoning the study of the precepts? The precepts one upholds are without negligence. What is the bodhisattva's not being weary of sense-desires? One's mind has never given rise to desire. What is the bodhisattva's mind not stopping at cessation? Regarding all dharmas, one has no practice. What is the bodhisattva's giving away all possessions? Being able to give generously and protect, without attachment to internal or external dharmas. What is the bodhisattva's aspiration not being timid or weak? The mind has never generated dual consciousness. What is the bodhisattva's contemplating all that exists without any attachment? Regarding all myriad things, without any thought. What is the bodhisattva's renouncing the kingdom and leaving home? One travels from one buddha-field to another; in every place of birth, one shaves the head and dons the kāṣāya, manifesting as a śramaṇa. What is the bodhisattva's departing from bhikṣuṇīs? Not engaging with them for even a finger-snap, not giving rise to any thought regarding them. What is the bodhisattva's abandoning attachment to lineage? The bodhisattva should think: 'I shall cause sentient beings to abide in peace and security, naturally at ease.' If one sees them, one never gives rise to a jealous mind. What is the bodhisattva's abandoning many desires and sleep? If the bodhisattva is in an assembly, should there be anyone generating the mind of a śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha, one should not engage with them. What is the bodhisattva's departing from anger? Not following resentful, wrathful, or harmful minds, without the intention to fight or contend, without any dispute. What is the bodhisattva's not praising oneself? Not perceiving any internal dharma, without any contemplation. What is the bodhisattva's not disparaging others? Regarding all external things, without any perception. What is the bodhisattva's abandoning the ten unwholesome courses? Practicing the noble path as the supreme practice, purifying body, speech, and mind. What is the bodhisattva's abandoning arrogance? As one practices, not perceiving any dharma as having arrogance. What is the bodhisattva's abandoning conceit? One's practice does not perceive form or possessions. What is the bodhisattva's departing from delusion? Examining all that exists, it cannot be apprehended. What is the bodhisattva's abandoning desire, anger, and delusion? One forever does not perceive any place where the defilements of desire, anger, and delusion abide. What is the bodhisattva's being endowed with the six dharmas? One who practices the sixth abode should be endowed with six dharmas. What are the six? The six pāramitās, which one should be endowed with completely. How does one completely fulfill the six pāramitās? Abiding in the six pāramitās, one can transcend the grounds of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas. What is the bodhisattva's not generating the mind of a śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha? The practices of such persons are not fitting for the path; those who practice the lesser vehicle do not accord with the buddha-path. If one sees supplicants, one harbors timidity and weakness. One who practices the bodhisattva-path should abandon and depart from this, without any sorrow in the mind. Why? The practices of such persons do not accord with the path. From the initial generation of aspiration, one always practices giving, and the mind never forgets or abandons generosity. What is the bodhisattva's not being attached to one's own body? The reason is this: investigating the root and end, there is no self; the same holds for the reckoning of persons and lifespans. Why? When one truly examines, the mind has no existence. What is the bodhisattva's not falling into the view of annihilation? The reason is this: regarding all dharmas, the mind severs nothing; the root and end do not arise; all dharmas also have no arising. What is the bodhisattva's not reckoning permanence? The reason is this: if all dharmas are entirely without arising, then there is no permanence. What is the bodhisattva's not having any conception or attachment? The reason is this: when one reckons thus, there is no dust or defilement; without views of causation. The reason is this: what is perceived does not perceive any views. What is the bodhisattva's not relying on name-and-form? The reason is this: all conditioned things are non-existent. What is the bodhisattva's not being attached to the aggregates? Not relying on the elements, not longing for the sense-fields. The reason is this: such practices are all enmity toward oneself and are without any existence; therefore one should not rely on or be attached to the aggregates, elements, or sense-fields. What is the bodhisattva's not relying on the three realms? The three realms are naturally formless; although one is in the three realms, one does not rely on them. What is the bodhisattva's not abiding in what exists? Not making any fixed determination about empty space; all that exists is entirely non-existent. What is the bodhisattva's seeing the Buddha without attachment? Not relying on perception to perceive the buddhas. What is the bodhisattva's not contending over emptiness? All dharmas are completely empty; emptiness does not disturb emptiness; without any contention. What is the bodhisattva's being endowed with emptiness? The body's characteristics being empty space is the bodhisattva's being endowed with emptiness. What is the bodhisattva's not realizing signlessness? Regarding all characteristics, one has no thought. What is the bodhisattva's aspiring to the wisdom of wishlessness? Regarding the three realms, one has no practice. What is the bodhisattva's purifying the three spheres? Being able to be endowed with the ten wholesome merits. What is the bodhisattva's having compassion for all sentient beings? Being able to practice the immeasurable great compassion of the perfection of virtue. What is the bodhisattva's not having contempt for sentient beings? Wishing to be endowed with the buddha-field. What is the bodhisattva's viewing all dharmas equally? Examining all dharmas, without high or low. What is the bodhisattva's truly contemplating the grounds of the path? Regarding all dharmas, without any habituation and without any movement or turning. What is the bodhisattva's patience of non-arising? All dharmas are entirely without arising and without cessation; patience is without any existence. What is the bodhisattva's wisdom of non-arising? Regarding name-and-form, wisdom has no arising. What is the bodhisattva's teaching the single category? Not practicing duality. What is the bodhisattva's not conceiving any thought? Regarding all dharmas, without any thought. What is the bodhisattva's abandoning all views? Being able to abandon and depart from the grounds of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas. What is the bodhisattva's eliminating dust and defilement? All outflows, their habituated abodes, and desire-defilements are all severed. What is the bodhisattva's quiescently departing from the ground of views? Being able to accomplish the wisdom of sarvajñā. What is the mind being settled? Being without any difficulty or affliction in the three realms. What is the mind being quiescent? Being able to guide the six sense faculties. What is the bodhisattva's not abandoning wisdom? Being able to attain the dharma-eye. What is the bodhisattva's being without rashness? Contemplating the six sense-fields without any defilement or attachment. What is the bodhisattva's mind having entry? With one-pointed mind, one universally perceives the thoughts of all sentient beings. What is the bodhisattva's delighting in supernatural powers? Through supernatural powers, one delights; traveling from one buddha-field to another, in whatever place one travels, one has no thought of buddha-fields. What is the bodhisattva's seeing all buddha-fields? Abiding in this buddha-field, one sees immeasurable buddha-fields in the ten directions, without any attachment to any buddha-field. What is the bodhisattva's observing them as they are? Seeing all buddha-fields endowed with purification and adornment; in the three-thousandfold worlds where one travels, one always becomes a wheel-turning sage-king. What is the bodhisattva's paying homage to and attending upon all buddhas, taking refuge in and reflecting upon them? Distinguishing the meaning and purport of all scriptures. What is the bodhisattva's always truly contemplating the bodies of all buddhas? Through the true and correct view, one sees all buddhas as the dharma-body. What is the bodhisattva's comprehending all faculties and roots? If one can abide in the tathāgata's ten powers, then one can comprehend all the roots and origins of all sentient beings. What is the bodhisattva's purity of the buddha-field? The purity of people is precisely what is called the purity of the buddha-field. What is the illusion-samādhi? Abiding in this samādhi, the bodhisattva can transform and manifest all things, entering everywhere without any abode in the mind. What is the bodhisattva's equal samādhi? The bodhisattva regarding all samādhis has no expectation. What is the bodhisattva's ability to teach sentient beings? Whatever roots of virtue are created, following each being's practice, one converts them. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, with truthfulness, protects oneself, and in accord with each sentient being, converts and liberates them. What is the bodhisattva's truthfulness? Naturally one has the capacity to encourage and guide, wishing to liberate all sentient beings. What is the bodhisattva's certainly attaining whatever one aspires to? The bodhisattva is always endowed with the six pāramitās. What is the bodhisattva's voice such that devas, nāgas, and gandharvas, hearing the sound, each understand and are guided? Because one has great compassion and a universal, equal voice. What is the bodhisattva's entering the womb? The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, in every place of birth, generation after generation, is without any actual birth. What is the bodhisattva's being in a noble family? The bodhisattva, born among all lineages, is able to convert them. What is the bodhisattva's birth being complete? If the bodhisattva is born among the warrior class, the brāhmaṇa class, or the merchant class, one is able to encourage and convert them. What is the bodhisattva's being in an esteemed lineage? Because past bodhisattvas are all equal in nature without any difference. What is the bodhisattva's retinue being complete? The bodhisattva's attendants and retinue are without any lack. What is the bodhisattva's land being purified and adorned? At the time of one's birth, radiance illuminates innumerable worlds, and those who receive the light all attain peace and security. What is the bodhisattva's renouncing the kingdom and leaving home? When the bodhisattva-mahāsattva abandons the home to study the path, one transforms incalculable hundreds of thousands of people, and they all follow along, enabling sentient beings to be established in the three vehicles. What is the bodhisattva's proceeding to the bodhi-tree? The tree has roots, stems, branches, leaves, flowers, and fruits, all made of the seven jewels and golden-purple color, illuminating innumerable buddha-fields in the ten directions with great radiance. This is the bodhisattva's proceeding to the purified bodhi-tree. What is the bodhisattva's being completely endowed with all excellent virtues? If the bodhisattva's people are pure, then the buddha-field is pure. This is the bodhisattva's being completely endowed with excellent virtues. What is the bodhisattva's abiding on the tenth ground and becoming the Tathāgata? The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, endowed with the six pāramitās, the ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, attains the wisdom of sarvajñā, severs all dust and defilement without any obstruction. This is the bodhisattva's abiding on the tenth ground and becoming the Tathāgata. Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, through upāya-kauśalya, practices the six pāramitās, the foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, bases of supernatural power, faculties, powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, quiescently departing from views, presently entering the lineage and the eight stages of equanimity. If there is any place, the ground of desirelessness, the ground where what should be done is done, departing from the grounds of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, the bodhisattva's ground: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's entry into the ninth abode on the buddha-ground. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice of the tenth abode. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's saṃprasthita!"

## Fascicle Eight

### Chapter Nineteen: From Where the Vehicle Arises

The Buddha told Subhūti: "As you have asked: 'From where does the Vehicle arise? Where does the Vehicle abide? Who accomplishes the Vehicle?' It arises from the three realms, abides in sarvajñā; it is originally unborn and has never been about to be born. Why? The mahāyāna and the wisdom of sarvajñā: regarding these two matters, in dharma there is no conjunction and no dispersion, no form and no perception, nothing to be grasped or abandoned; it constitutes a single characteristic, which is no characteristic. Why? The dharma of signlessness has no arising. If one wishes dharma to arise, that is wishing the dharma-realm to arise. If one wishes the signless dharma to arise, that is wishing the originally rootless to arise. The signless dharma has no arising. If one wishes it to arise, that is wishing the true original limit to arise. If one wishes the signless to arise, that is wishing the inconceivable dharma-realm to arise. If one wishes the signless dharma to arise, that is wishing exclusive and devoted practice to arise. If one wishes the signless dharma to arise, that is wishing the realm of severance to arise. In brief, Subhūti, that is wishing the realm free from desire to arise. If one wishes the signless dharma to arise, that is wishing the realm of cessation to arise. Subhūti! That is wishing quiescent, empty nothingness to arise. If one wishes the signless dharma of form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness to arise, that is wishing the dharma of characteristics to arise. Why? Form is empty, arising from the three realms, abiding in sarvajñā. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also without emptiness, arising from the three realms; for sarvajñā there is no abode. Why? If one understands form, form is empty. If one understands feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, consciousness is empty. The eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are also empty. If one wishes them to arise, that is wishing empty space to arise. Eye-form-consciousness, ear-sound-consciousness, nose-smell-consciousness, tongue-taste-consciousness, body-touch-consciousness, and mind-desire-consciousness: these eighteen elements and their perceived conditions are empty and void. If one wishes them to arise, that is wishing the signless dharma to arise. Why? Subhūti! What the eye sees is all empty. The ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are likewise; their habituations are all empty. Subhūti! The three realms are empty. What the eye sees is empty, arising from the three realms; for sarvajñā there is no abode. The six sense faculties are also empty, arising through the three realms; for sarvajñā there is no abode. What the six sense faculties receive and habituate is all empty, without any characteristic. If one wishes them to arise, that is wishing dreams and illusions to arise. Why? Dreams, illusions, the moon in water, the plantain, mirages, and the echo of deep mountains are all naturally so. Natural matters are the Tathāgata's transformation. The three realms are naturally without any arising; for sarvajñā there is no abode. Why? Subhūti! Dreams are naturally so; the natural quality of dreams is entirely non-existent. Matters of illusion and transformation are likewise. Subhūti! If one wishes the dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā to arise, that is wishing the signless dharma to arise. Why? Subhūti! The six pāramitās are all naturally so, arising from the three realms; for sarvajñā there is no abode. Why? Subhūti! The six pāramitās are natural; the natural is therefore called empty. If one wishes the signless dharma to arise, that is wishing internal emptiness, external emptiness, emptiness of existence, emptiness of non-existence, proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, and true emptiness to arise. Why? Subhūti! The seven emptinesses are natural; because they are natural, arising through the three realms, for sarvajñā there is no abode. Why? Subhūti! Because the seven emptinesses are natural, they are called empty; thus emptiness is empty. Subhūti! If one wishes the signless dharma to arise, that is wishing the four foundations of mindfulness, four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, and Eightfold Path to arise. Why? All are naturally empty, arising through the three realms; for sarvajñā there is no abode. Subhūti! If one wishes the thirty-seven factors to arise, that is wishing the signless dharma to arise. Why? Subhūti! The thirty-seven factors are natural; they do not arise in the three realms; for sarvajñā there is no abode. Why? The thirty-seven factors are naturally empty; because empty, they are called empty. Subhūti! If one wishes the ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, and four analytical knowledges to arise, they are all naturally empty; because empty, they are called empty. If one wishes stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, up to tathāgatahood, arhatship, and samyak-saṃbuddhahood to arise, that is wishing the signless dharma to arise. Why? Subhūti! The three vehicles are also natural; they do not emerge from the three realms; for sarvajñā there is no abode. Why? Subhūti! The arhat is natural; being natural, it is empty; thus it is called empty. The pratyekabuddha is natural; being natural, it is empty; thus it is called empty. The Tathāgata is natural; being natural, it is empty; thus it is called empty. Subhūti! If one wishes names and designations to arise, that is wishing the signless dharma to arise. Emptiness, signlessness, and wishlessness are likewise. If one wishes words of causation to arise, that is wishing the signless dharma to arise. Why? Subhūti! Names and designations are empty; they do not arise in the three realms; for sarvajñā there is no abode. Why? Names and designations are empty; because names and designations are empty, they are called empty. Words of causation and all their locations are all empty; the locations of dharmas are empty; thus they are called empty. If one wishes the unborn to arise, that is wishing the signless dharma to arise. Why? The signless dharma is empty, entirely without any location; because the location is empty, it is called empty. If one wishes the unceasing, the thoughtless, the dustless, the wrathless, and the non-existent to arise, that is wishing the signless dharma to arise. Why? All these matters are empty; because empty, they are called empty. Names, designations, words of causation and their locations, the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, and four analytical knowledges are all likewise. Therefore, Subhūti, the mahāyāna arises from the three realms, arising as non-arising; the arising of sarvajñā is also non-arising, and there is no place of movement. Furthermore, as Subhūti has asked: 'Where does it abide?' The mind has no abode; the Vehicle has no place. Why? Because it has no abode; all dharmas also have no abode. Furthermore, Subhūti, the Vehicle abides in non-abiding. The dharma-realm also has no abode, abiding in non-abiding; the Vehicle is likewise, abiding in non-abiding. Just as the upper empty space has no turning; the Vehicle is likewise, abiding in non-abiding. Just as the unborn abides in non-abiding; the Vehicle is likewise, abiding in non-abiding. Just as the unceasing, the dustless, the wrathless, and the non-existent abide in non-abiding; the Vehicle is likewise, abiding in non-abiding. Why? The dharma-realm is naturally so, abiding in non-abiding. Why? The dharma-realm is naturally so; because it is natural, the natural is empty, together with the seven emptinesses, all non-existent. The natural is empty; emptiness is non-existent; thus it is called empty. Therefore, Subhūti, the Vehicle has no abode; abiding in non-abiding, there is no movement or turning. As Subhūti has asked: 'From where does one abide to accomplish the Vehicle?' The Vehicle has no arising. Why? There is no one who arises from within it, no one who is about to arise; all dharmas are entirely non-existent. Because of this non-existence, all dharmas are likewise; what dharma could there be that has an arising? Why? Self, person, and lifespan are likewise: there is no suchness, nothing perceived, nothing obtained; the root and end are originally pure. Therefore self, person, and lifespan, and the dharma-realm thus, are all unobtainable; the root and end are entirely empty. Therefore the Tathāgata is entirely unobtainable. The original limit is also unobtainable; the root and end are entirely pure. Therefore the inconceivable realms are all unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. Therefore the aggregates, elements, and sense-fields are all unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. Because the aggregates, elements, and sense-fields are unobtainable, the root and end are originally pure. The six pāramitās are all unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. Therefore the seven emptinesses are also unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. The foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, bases of supernatural power, faculties, powers, seven factors, Eightfold Path, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, and four analytical knowledges are also unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure.
