Stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, up to tathāgatahood, arhatship, and samyak-saṃbuddhahood are all unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. The dharma of the three vehicles and the wisdom of sarvajñā, being unobtainable, the root and end are originally pure. The arising of what is non-existent is entirely unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. The unceasing, the dustless, the wrathless, the undisputed, all that is non-existent and all that exists: all are unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. Past, future, and present matters, comings and goings, abidings and arisings: all are unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. Benefit and loss are all unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. Who shall attain the unattainable? The dharma-realm also cannot be attained; there is no one who attains it. Why? Wishing to attain the dharma-realm is unobtainable. If one seeks arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, or tathāgatahood, wishing to attain these is all unobtainable. If one wishes to attain the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, and four analytical knowledges, they are also unobtainable; no one can attain them. If one wishes to attain anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi, it is all unobtainable; the original limit is entirely empty and unobtainable. The six pāramitās and the seven emptinesses are likewise, all unobtainable. The unborn and the unceasing, the dustless, the wrathless, and the non-existent are all unobtainable. Why? When one truly and correctly contemplates, all is entirely non-existent, entirely unobtainable. If one wishes to attain the first abode, it is also unobtainable; up to the tenth abode, it is also unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. What first abode is there? Those who observe with purity, the lineage, the eight stages of equanimity, and the demonstrated grounds, these are the grounds: the ground of desirelessness, the ground where what should be done is done, the pratyekabuddha ground, the bodhisattva-path ground, the samyak-saṃbuddha ground, and the first ground: all are unobtainable. The seven emptinesses are all unobtainable. Reckoning internal emptiness, up to the ten abodes: all are unobtainable. The seven emptinesses and the ten abodes are all non-existent, all unobtainable. Why? Subhūti! The first abode is but a name; it is unobtainable. Up to the tenth abode, it is likewise. If there is anything obtained, it is unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. For sentient beings one teaches that internal emptiness is entirely unobtainable; all sentient beings are also unobtainable. For sentient beings one teaches the seven categories of emptiness; whatever is taught is entirely unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. Because of internal emptiness, the buddha-field is pure, and nothing at all is obtained. The seven emptinesses are natural; because naturally empty, the buddha-field is pure, entirely unobtainable; the root and end are originally pure. Therefore internal emptiness and the five eyes are all unobtainable; all are non-existent, natural; because naturally empty, the five eyes are entirely without any location; the root and end are originally pure. Therefore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, regarding all things being entirely without any attainment, thereby attains and accomplishes the mahāyāna saṃprasthita and the wisdom of sarvajñā."

### Chapter Twenty: Without Coming or Going

At that time, the worthy Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "What is called the mahāyāna, the import and purport of the mahāyāna: O God among Gods! In the heavens and among humans in the world, it is the most honored; none do not take refuge. The Vehicle equals emptiness. Just as empty space covers and shelters immeasurable asaṃkhyeya beings, who all look up in reverence, O God among Gods, the mahāyāna is likewise: the bodhisattva-mahāsattva covers incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings, who all thereby gain deliverance. The mahāyāna: one does not see it when it comes, does not see it when it goes, does not see where it abides. Thus, God among Gods, the mahāyāna does not apprehend past, future, or present; there is no perception in between, and nothing is obtained. Its name is equal to the three times; therefore it is called the Vehicle, and therefore it is the mahāyāna."

Then the World-Honored One told Subhūti: "It is so, it is so! What is called the mahāyāna is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's six pāramitās: dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā. This, Subhūti, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is all dhāraṇī gates, all samādhi gates, and the śūraṅgama samādhi. In brief, the samādhi of emptiness-equality, the samādhi of liberation, the samādhi of non-attachment, and the samādhi of quiescent cessation: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna is comprehending the seven emptinesses, the thirty-seven factors, the ten powers, the fearlessnesses, the eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, and the four analytical knowledges. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's mahāyāna.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, what is called the mahāyāna is supreme in the heavens and on earth, in the world the highest; none do not take refuge and look up to it. For example, Subhūti, the desire-realm is originally non-existent, and the non-existence is without any original non-existence, equal and without difference, indistinguishable, without any delusion, truthful, genuine, and natural, enduring and firm, without any dharma of separation, no conjunction and no dispersion, never having existed. This is the mahāyāna: in the heavens and on earth, among humans the most honored; none do not take refuge and look up to it.

"Suppose, Subhūti, at the end of the kalpa when all is burned, it manifests for all, teaching and converting all, causing them to know impermanence: there is no endurance, nothing firm; all is non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna, in the heavens and on earth, in the world the most honored; none do not take refuge and look up to it.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the desire-realm is thus equal and without difference, without any delusion, truthful, genuine, and natural, originally without firmness, without any dharma of separation, without any causation; what is non-existent is ultimately non-existent. This is the mahāyāna, in the heavens and on earth the most honored.

"Suppose, Subhūti, the desire-realm, with its perception of impermanence and delusion, manifests destruction: all is impermanent, without endurance, not firm; the dharma of separation is entirely non-existent. Therefore, Subhūti, the mahāyāna in the heavens and on earth; in the formless realm it is likewise.

"Suppose, Subhūti, all forms are originally non-existent, entirely without anything; it is likewise, equal and without distinction, without multiplicity, truthful, genuine, and natural, originally without firmness, without any dharma of separation; what is non-existent cannot be made to exist. This is the mahāyāna, in the heavens and on earth the most honored.

"Suppose, Subhūti, form has thought and should be pure, yet it is deluded, causing all to be satiated; all shall be impermanent, without any endurance, not firm; the dharma of separation is entirely non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. The eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are equal and without difference. Eye-form-consciousness, ear-sound-consciousness, nose-smell-consciousness, tongue-taste-consciousness, body-touch-consciousness, and mind-desire-consciousness are equal and without difference, entirely non-existent and indistinguishable. In utmost sincerity and true truth, those who reckon permanence, endurance, and firmness: this is not the mahāyāna. Through habituating the six matters, the mind has thoughts and conceptions; what is habituated through causation is deluded, seeking much to satiate oneself. All these dharmas are impermanent, without any endurance, not lasting. Therefore the mahāyāna, in the heavens and on earth the most honored.

"Suppose, Subhūti, whatever exists in the dharma-realm is entirely non-existent. This is the mahāyāna, in the heavens and on earth the most honored. It is firm, arising from non-existence. Thus, Subhūti, whatever exists in the dharma-realm is entirely non-existent; practice is non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna, in the heavens and on earth the most honored.

"Suppose, Subhūti, the Tathāgata presently having what exists: all is non-existent; the true original limit is inconceivable. Whatever exists in the realms is all non-existent. This is the mahāyāna, in the heavens and on earth the most honored.

"Even if, Subhūti, the realms are inconceivable, whatever exists in them is all non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna, in the heavens and on earth the most honored.

"Suppose, Subhūti, whatever exists of the six pāramitās is entirely non-existent, yet it is also not without existence. This is the mahāyāna.

"Even if, Subhūti, internal emptiness is neither existent nor non-existent, naturally empty, neither existent nor non-existent: this is the mahāyāna. Therefore, Subhūti, internal emptiness is naturally without existence; one who has understood emptiness finds it neither existent nor non-existent; therefore it is called the mahāyāna.

"Suppose, Subhūti, the thirty-seven factors, the ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, and four analytical knowledges are neither existent nor non-existent, nor are they non-non-existent. This is the mahāyāna.

"Even if, Subhūti, the dharma of the lineage is neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; because the dharma of the lineage is neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent, therefore the mahāyāna.

"Even if, Subhūti, the dharma of the eight stages of equanimity is neither existent nor non-existent; the dharma of stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, and all the buddha-dharmas are neither existent nor non-existent; because they are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent, therefore the mahāyāna.

"Even if, Subhūti, the dharma of the eight stages of equanimity and the buddha-dharma are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent, therefore the mahāyāna.

"Because, Subhūti, all the lineages are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; because the eight stages of equanimity are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, up to tathāgatahood, arhatship, and samyak-saṃbuddhahood are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; therefore the mahāyāna.

"Subhūti! You should know that the eight stages of equanimity, tathāgatahood, arhatship, and samyak-saṃbuddhahood are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; therefore the mahāyāna.

"Suppose, Subhūti, all devas, humans, asuras, and the world are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; because whatever exists of devas, humans, asuras, and the world is neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; therefore the mahāyāna.

"Suppose, Subhūti, the bodhisattva, from the initial generation of aspiration through to the bodhimaṇḍa, seated beneath the bodhi-tree: the mind generated therein is neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent. Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, from the initial generation of aspiration through to the bodhimaṇḍa, the mind generated therein: all is neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; therefore the mahāyāna.

"Suppose, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's honored wisdom is like vajra, neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's thorough comprehension and penetrating insight into all obstructions and defilements, attaining sarvajñā. Because, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva comprehends that all obstructions and defilements are entirely non-existent, one attains sarvajñā; therefore the mahāyāna.

"Even if, Subhūti, the Tathāgata, Arhat, Samyak-saṃbuddha's thirty-two marks of a great person are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent: therefore the Tathāgata, Arhat, Samyak-saṃbuddha is in the heavens and on earth the most honored, with divine power, sacred virtue, and radiance, subtle and wondrous, illuminating everywhere without any equal. Therefore the Tathāgata, Arhat, Samyak-saṃbuddha's divine power, majestic sacred virtue, and radiance illuminates the buddha-worlds in the ten directions as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, together with all the devas in the heavens and on earth, humans, and asuras; the radiance pervades universally. Because of being neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent, therefore the radiance of the Tathāgata, Arhat, Samyak-saṃbuddha illuminates the worlds in the ten directions as numerous as the sands of the Ganges.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the Tathāgata has the eight kinds of voice, neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; therefore the Tathāgata, Arhat, Samyak-saṃbuddha's voice resounds through the ten directions in asaṃkhyeya immeasurable worlds. Because the Tathāgata's eight kinds of voice are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent, therefore the eight kinds of voice resound through the ten directions in inconceivable immeasurable worlds.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the dharma-wheel turned by the Tathāgata is neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent. This is the Tathāgata's turning of the dharma-wheel. Śramaṇas, brāhmaṇas, and all the Brahmā hosts, in the heavens and on earth, none can match it; all are caused to accord with the dharma and each attain their proper place. Therefore the Tathāgata turns the dharma-wheel; among śramaṇas, brāhmaṇas, in the heavens and on earth, and among all humans, none can match it.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, all sentient beings are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent; therefore the Tathāgata repeatedly turns the dharma-wheel, causing sentient beings not to arrive at the realm of nirvāṇa without remainder.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, these sentient beings are neither existent nor non-existent, nor non-non-existent. Having fully comprehended this, the Tathāgata turns the dharma-wheel; therefore sentient beings arrive at the realm without remainder, and in the realm of nirvāṇa they attain parinirvāṇa."

### Chapter Twenty-One: The Vehicle Equals Emptiness

The Buddha told Subhūti: "As you have said that the Vehicle equals emptiness, what you have said is utterly sincere. It is so, it is so! The Vehicle equals emptiness.

"Just as empty space cannot be calculated or known in its distance to the east, nor can the south, west, north, four intermediate directions, above, or below be known, without distance or nearness, without any boundary; the Tathāgata's wisdom is likewise, inexhaustible in the eight directions and above and below, without any boundary, without distance or nearness; his wisdom cannot be exhausted. Just as empty space has no length or shortness, no aspect or direction, no increase or decrease; the Tathāgata's wisdom is likewise: no length or shortness, neither round nor square, no increase or decrease.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has none of the five colors, blue, yellow, red, or white; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no past, future, or present; the Vehicle is likewise, without past, future, or present.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has nothing that can increase it and nothing that can decrease it; the Vehicle is likewise, neither increasing nor decreasing. Therefore it is said that the Vehicle equals emptiness.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no defilements, no anger or hatred, nothing that is born and nothing that ceases, no abiding and no non-abiding, and no thought; the Vehicle is likewise. Therefore it is said that the Vehicle equals emptiness.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no good or evil, no speech and yet is not without speech; just as empty space has nothing seen, nothing heard, nothing thought, nothing known; the Vehicle is likewise. Therefore it is said that the Vehicle equals emptiness.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space is neither different nor not-different, with nothing severed, nothing accomplished or realized, and nothing removed; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no dharma of desire and does not depart from the dharma of desire, has no dharma of anger and does not depart from anger, has no dharma of delusion and does not depart from delusion; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space does not merge with the desire-realm, does not merge with the form-realm or the formless realm, and yet does not depart from the three realms; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no initial generation of aspiration and no first abode; the Vehicle is likewise, without any of the ten abodes.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no clarity or turbidity, nothing observed or seen, no location, no ground of lineage, no ground of the eight stages of equanimity, no demonstrated ground, no ground of possessions, no ground of desire, no ground of what is done or not done; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no fruit of stream-entry, no fruit of once-returning, no fruit of non-returning, no fruit of arhatship.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no ground of the śrāvaka, no ground of the pratyekabuddha, no ground of the samyak-saṃbuddha; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no form or image, yet is not without image, has no perception yet is not without perception, with no acceptance and no rejection, no conjunction and no dispersion; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no permanence yet no impermanence, no suffering and no happiness, no self and no non-self; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no emptiness yet no non-emptiness, no different emptiness, no different thought yet no absence of thought, no wish yet no absence of wish; the Vehicle is likewise. Therefore it is said that the Vehicle equals emptiness.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no quiescence yet no absence of quiescence, no fearlessness and no absence of fearlessness.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no radiance and no darkness; the Vehicle is likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no attainment and no non-attainment; the Vehicle is likewise. Therefore it is said that the Vehicle equals emptiness.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, just as empty space has no words and no speech, yet is not without words; the Vehicle is likewise. Therefore it is said that the Vehicle equals emptiness.

"Therefore, Subhūti, empty space is level and equal; the Vehicle is also level and equal. As Subhūti has said, just as empty space has no boundary, covering incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings, the Vehicle is likewise, sheltering incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings. Thus, Subhūti, just as empty space covers incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings, the Vehicle likewise protects incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings, reckoning persons and non-persons. Just as empty space cannot be apprehended as existent, since space is without existence, the mahāyāna is likewise. Therefore, Subhūti, the mahāyāna shelters and protects innumerable asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Because persons, empty space, and the mahāyāna: all these dharmas are entirely unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, persons are incalculable, emptiness is also incalculable, empty space is also incalculable, the mahāyāna is also incalculable; therefore the mahāyāna covers incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Subhūti! Persons, empty space, and the mahāyāna are all incalculable, all unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, all is incalculable; therefore the mahāyāna covers and protects incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, persons are non-existent, the dharma-realm is also non-existent, all dharmas are also non-existent; therefore empty space is also non-existent. Persons, empty space, and the mahāyāna are all non-existent. The asaṃkhyeya is non-existent, the immeasurable is non-existent, the bottomless is non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna covers and protects incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Because sentient beings, the dharma-realm, and the mahāyāna, together with the asaṃkhyeya, are immeasurable and unlimited, without any boundary or bottom, and all are unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, persons are non-existent, the Tathāgata is also non-existent, empty space is also non-existent, the mahāyāna is also non-existent, the asaṃkhyeya is also non-existent, the incalculable is also non-existent, the bottomless is also non-existent, all dharmas are also non-existent. Therefore, Subhūti, the mahāyāna establishes protection for incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings without boundary or bottom. Why? Because the Tathāgata, empty space, sentient beings, and the mahāyāna, their asaṃkhyeya count is incalculable and inconceivable, without boundary or bottom, and all are unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the self is non-existent, what is known and seen is also non-existent, the original limit is non-existent. One should understand thus that the original limit is non-existent, reaching the incalculable; the asaṃkhyeya and innumerable are also non-existent. Because they are non-existent, all dharmas are also non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna is called the incalculable asaṃkhyeya cover and protection of innumerable beings. Why? Subhūti! All sentient beings, what is known and seen, and the original limit, reaching the asaṃkhyeya, innumerable, and incalculable: all are unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, self and person are entirely non-existent, what is known and seen is also non-existent, the inconceivable realm is also non-existent, form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also non-existent, empty space is also non-existent, the mahāyāna is also non-existent, the asaṃkhyeya is also non-existent, the incalculable is also non-existent, the innumerable is also non-existent, all dharmas are also non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna is the cover and protection of incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Thus, Subhūti, self and all dharmas are entirely unattainable!

"Furthermore, Subhūti, self and person are entirely empty space; what is known and seen is also void; the eye is also void; the ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are also void. Because they are void, empty space is also void; because space is void, the mahāyāna is also void. Because these two are void, the asaṃkhyeya, innumerable, and incalculable are also void; because the incalculable is void, all dharmas are also void. Therefore the mahāyāna covers the innumerable, incalculable, asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Subhūti! Self and person, and all dharmas, are all unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the self is non-existent, what is known and seen is also non-existent; because what is known and seen is non-existent, the dāna-pāramitā is also non-existent; the śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are also non-existent; because the prajñāpāramitā is non-existent, empty space is also non-existent, the mahāyāna is also non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna covers and protects innumerable, incalculable, asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Subhūti! The self and lifespan, and all dharmas, are all unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, self and person are non-existent; what the world knows as internal emptiness, external emptiness, proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, true emptiness, emptiness of existence, and emptiness of non-existence are also non-existent. Because the seven emptinesses are non-existent, empty space is also non-existent, the mahāyāna is also non-existent; the innumerable, incalculable, and asaṃkhyeya are also non-existent; all dharmas are also non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna covers and protects incalculable, innumerable, asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Subhūti! Self, person, and lifespan, and all dharmas, are all unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, self, person, knowledge, and perception are all non-existent; the foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, bases of supernatural power, faculties, powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, and thirty-seven factors are also non-existent; the ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are also non-existent; empty space and the mahāyāna are also non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna covers and protects incalculable, innumerable, asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Self and person, and all dharmas, are all unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, self, person, knowledge, and perception are all non-existent; the dharmas of the lineage are also non-existent; the grounds of practice being non-existent, empty space is also non-existent, the mahāyāna is also non-existent; incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings and all dharmas are also non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna covers and protects incalculable, innumerable, asaṃkhyeya beings.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, self, person, knowledge, and perception are all non-existent; stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, and pratyekabuddhahood are also non-existent; all dharmas are also non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna covers and protects incalculable, innumerable, asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Self and person, and all dharmas, are all unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, up to tathāgatas, are also non-existent; sarvajñā is also non-existent; all dharmas are also non-existent. Therefore the mahāyāna covers and protects incalculable, innumerable, asaṃkhyeya beings. Why? Subhūti! Self, person, and all dharmas are all unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the realm of nirvāṇa covers and protects incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings; the Vehicle is likewise. Therefore the Vehicle equals emptiness, covering and protecting incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings.

"As Subhūti has asked, the mahāyāna: one does not see it when it comes, does not see it when it goes, does not see where it abides; the Vehicle is thus. Why? All dharmas cannot be moved or turned; therefore there is no one who abides, no one who comes, and no abode. Why? Subhūti! Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have nowhere from which they come, nowhere to which they go, and no abode. Subhūti! Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also pure: with nowhere from which they come, nowhere to which they go, and no abode. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without any root: with nowhere from which they come, nowhere to which they go, and no abode. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are naturally so: with nowhere from which they come, nowhere to which they go, and no abode. The natural characteristic of form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness has nowhere from which it comes, nowhere to which it goes, and no abode. The natural characteristics of the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind have nowhere from which they come, nowhere to which they go, and no abode.

"The elements of earth, water, fire, wind, and space: these various elements have no purity and no rootlessness. Their natural quality is also without the natural characteristic of the earth element: with nowhere from which it comes, nowhere to which it goes, and no abode. The water, fire, and wind elements, the space element, and the consciousness element are likewise.

"The Tathāgata is originally without naturalness and without natural characteristics: with nowhere from which he comes, nowhere to which he goes, and no abode. Subhūti! The original limit is pure, the original limit is rootless, the original source is naturally so, the original natural characteristic is incalculable and inconceivable. The pure realm has nowhere from which it comes, nowhere to which it goes, and no abode. The inconceivable and the rootless, the unthinkable realm and naturalness, the inconceivable realm's natural characteristic: all have nowhere from which they come, nowhere to which they go, and no abode.

"Subhūti! The six pāramitās are also pure. The prajñāpāramitā is also without rootlessness and without naturalness; its natural characteristic has nowhere from which it comes, nowhere to which it goes, and no abode. The thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, the purity of the path and virtue, the Buddha and right awakening: all have nowhere from which they come, nowhere to which they go, and no abode. Non-existence and rootlessness, the unconditioned that does not constitute naturalness, the unconditioned that has no natural characteristic: all have nowhere from which they come, nowhere to which they go, and no abode.

"As Subhūti has said: 'The mahāyāna does not apprehend the past, does not apprehend the future, does not apprehend the interval between. The three times are equal; the mahāyāna is but a name.' It is so, Subhūti! What is called the mahāyāna has no past, future, or present; the three times are equal; the mahāyāna is but a name. Why? Subhūti! The past is also empty, the future is also empty, the present is also empty. The three times are equal; the three times are equally empty; the mahāyāna is also equally empty. The bodhisattva is also empty. In emptiness there is no one, no two, no three, no four, not many and not few. Therefore it is called the three times being equal, which is the mahāyāna.

"The bodhisattva's merit is majestic, without any equal or companion; without correctness and without deviance; neither with desire nor departing from desire; neither with anger nor departing from anger; neither with delusion nor departing from delusion; not apprehending pride nor departing from pride; not apprehending greed, miserliness, or jealousy, and with nothing departed from; not apprehending wholesome or unwholesome dharmas; not apprehending permanence or impermanence; not apprehending suffering or happiness; not apprehending self or non-self. The desire-realm, form-realm, and formless realm are also unobtainable; one neither crosses beyond the desire-realm, nor crosses beyond the form-realm, nor crosses beyond the formless realm. Why? Naturalness is not apprehended. Past form is empty, future form is empty, present form is empty. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. Form is unobtainable; because past, future, and present form is empty, it is unobtainable; because empty, it is called empty. If emptiness is unobtainable, how much less can one conceive of emptiness having past, future, or present? Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the six pāramitās do not apprehend the past, do not apprehend the future, do not apprehend the present. Subhūti! The six pāramitās are also unobtainable, because the three times are equal. The six pāramitās being unobtainable, the equality has no past, future, or present, because of equality.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the thirty-seven factors, the ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are also unobtainable, because the past, future, and present three times are equal. The thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas are also unobtainable; the equality has no past, future, or present. The ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas have no past, future, or present; because of equality, they are called equal. How much less can the equal past, future, and present thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas be obtained?

"Furthermore, Subhūti, past, future, and present ordinary people are also unobtainable, because the three times are equal; therefore ordinary people are equal. Why? When one searches for a person, one can never find them. Stream-enterers, once-returners, non-returners, arhats, pratyekabuddhas, bodhisattvas, and tathāgatas are also unobtainable; in the future and present it is likewise, because the three times are equal. All śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, bodhisattvas, and tathāgatas are also unobtainable, because when one investigates to the utmost, the root of a person is unobtainable. Thus, Subhūti, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, abiding in this way in the prajñāpāramitā, comprehending the three times, thereby fulfills the wisdom of sarvajñā. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, for whom the mahāyāna is three-times-equal. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who abides thus is in the heavens and on earth, in the world the most honored, and thereby gives rise to the wisdom of sarvajñā."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "Excellent, excellent! O God among Gods! The mahāyāna: it is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's study of this Vehicle. Past bodhisattva-mahāsattvas also, through studying this, attained the wisdom of sarvajñā. Future bodhisattva-mahāsattvas also, through studying this, will attain the wisdom of sarvajñā. Presently, in the ten directions, in incalculable, innumerable, asaṃkhyeya worlds, all bodhisattva-mahāsattvas also study this mahāyāna and attain the wisdom of sarvajñā. Therefore, God among Gods, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva: this is the mahāyāna!"

The Buddha told Subhūti: "It is so, it is so! Past, future, and present tathāgatas, arhats, samyak-saṃbuddhas all study this dharma and attain the wisdom of sarvajñā."

## Fascicle Nine

### Chapter Twenty-Two: Pūrṇamaitrāyaṇīputra

At that time, the worthy Pūrṇamaitrāyaṇīputra addressed the Buddha: "The venerable Subhūti, whom the Buddha has instructed to teach the prajñāpāramitā, has instead been teaching about the mahāyāna?"

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "O God among Gods, have I committed any fault in teaching the mahāyāna?"

The Buddha said: "No fault. Your teaching of the mahāyāna accords with the instruction of the prajñāpāramitā. Why? Subhūti, all wholesome dharmas, the dharmas of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, and the dharma of the Buddha's right awakening all arise from the prajñāpāramitā; they originally follow its instruction."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "How is it, God among Gods, that all wholesome dharmas, the dharmas of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, the dharmas of all buddhas, and the dharma of the bodhisattva all arise from the prajñāpāramitā, all following its instruction?"

The Buddha told Subhūti: "The dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā; the four foundations of mindfulness, four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path; the gates of liberation of emptiness, signlessness, and wishlessness; the Tathāgata's ten powers, four fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, four analytical knowledges; great lovingkindness and great compassion, the dharma of unfailing mindfulness, lovingkindness, compassion, sympathetic joy, and equanimity; comprehending the factors of the path and the dharmas of practice; the dharmas of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, the dharma of the bodhisattva: all dharmas arise from within the prajñāpāramitā, all following its instruction.

"Furthermore, Subhūti, the mahāyāna prajñāpāramitā and the five pāramitās; form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness; eye-form-consciousness, ear-sound-consciousness, nose-smell-consciousness, tongue-taste-consciousness, body-touch-consciousness, and mind-dharma-consciousness; the conditions of contact and habituation, the agreeable and disagreeable seeds of habituation; the foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, bases of supernatural power, faculties, powers, seven factors, Eightfold Path; the ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas; the gates of liberation of emptiness, signlessness, and wishlessness; all wholesome dharmas with and without outflows, existent and non-existent, conditioned and unconditioned; suffering, origination, cessation, and path; the desire-realm, form-realm, and formless realm; internal emptiness, external emptiness, proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, true emptiness, emptiness of existence, and emptiness of non-existence; all equality; all samādhis and dhāraṇī gates; the dharmas comprehended by the Tathāgata and accomplished through his own attainment; the dharma-realm of all buddhas, the original limit of the Tathāgata, and the inconceivable realm; conjunction and dispersion, no conjunction and no dispersion, with form and without form, seen and unseen, with shape and without shape, with characteristics and without characteristics: all these dharmas arise from the mahāyāna, in accordance with the instruction of the prajñāpāramitā. Why? Subhūti! The mahāyāna and the prajñāpāramitā are equally without difference. The six pāramitās are also without difference. The ten powers, fearlessnesses, and all buddha-dharmas are also without difference. Therefore the mahāyāna and the dharmas of all buddhas are without difference, without duality, and without multiplicity. Therefore, Subhūti, to teach the mahāyāna is to teach the prajñāpāramitā."

### Chapter Twenty-Three: Equality of the Three Times

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "The bodhisattva does not think of the past, does not think of the future, does not think of the interval between. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also without any boundary; the bodhisattva is also without any boundary. Form and the bodhisattva are both non-existent and unobtainable. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness: consciousness and the bodhisattva are both non-existent and unobtainable. Thus, God among Gods, all bodhisattva-mahāsattvas are unobtainable. How then can one teach the bodhisattva-mahāsattva the prajñāpāramitā? When one seeks the bodhisattva, all is unobtainable and unseeable; how then can one teach the prajñāpāramitā to the bodhisattva? The bodhisattva is again called a bodhisattva, but it is only a name. Just as a person says, 'I have a self,' yet when one investigates from root to end, all is non-existent. All dharmas are naturally so; from where does form arise, what gives rise to form? From where do feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness arise, what gives rise to consciousness? O God among Gods! That which is unborn has neither form nor consciousness. What is there to be called teaching the prajñāpāramitā? How can one teach the bodhisattva? There is no different place, no arising, no obtainable bodhisattva, no attainable practitioner of the path. If the bodhisattva hears this without terror, without fear, without any dread, then the bodhisattva-mahāsattva is practicing the prajñāpāramitā."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "How is the bodhisattva of the past, future, and interval unobtainable? Why? Form is without boundary, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also without boundary, the bodhisattva is also without boundary. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are both non-existent and unobtainable; all bodhisattvas are unobtainable. How can one teach the bodhisattva-mahāsattva? What is there to be said about the prajñāpāramitā? Self is entirely unseeable; the bodhisattva is also unobtainable anywhere. How can one teach the bodhisattva-mahāsattva the prajñāpāramitā? Why do you say: 'The bodhisattva-mahāsattva is but a name. When one seeks self, there is no root or end. All dharmas are naturally so; from where does form arise? From where do feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness arise? O God among Gods, that which is unborn has no form; that which is unborn has no feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness.' Previously, Subhūti said: 'That which is unborn: how can one teach the prajñāpāramitā?' Why do you say: 'There is no different place'? Is there anything that arises from which one can find the bodhisattva? As for the practitioner of the path, why did Subhūti say: 'If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva hears this without terror or fear in the mind, this constitutes practicing the prajñāpāramitā'? What does this mean?"

Subhūti said to Śāriputra: "Because persons are non-existent, the past bodhisattva is unobtainable. All sentient beings are empty; therefore the past bodhisattva has no reception. Sentient beings are illusory; therefore the past bodhisattva has no reception. Form is non-existent; therefore the bodhisattva does not receive past feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness. Emptiness is non-existent; therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. Past form is empty; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also empty. Form is illusory; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are illusory. Form is naturally so; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are naturally so. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. The dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are all non-existent; therefore the bodhisattva does not apprehend the past. Why? Śāriputra! That which is empty cannot be apprehended in the past, future, or interval between. There is no different emptiness, no bodhisattva, no emptiness of the past bodhisattva, and no past events; all are without duality and without multiplicity. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past; the future and interval are likewise. In brief, the dāna-pāramitā is also illusory; the dāna-pāramitā is naturally so. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are also all empty; the prajñāpāramitā is also illusory and without naturalness. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. Therefore, Śāriputra, that which is empty has no past, future, or interval. Emptiness and the bodhisattva and the already-past are also without duality and without multiplicity. Therefore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva does not receive the past. The seven emptinesses are also non-existent; therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, bases of supernatural power, faculties, powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, and thirty-seven factors are also empty and illusory. The seven emptinesses are likewise. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. The ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are all empty and illusory. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. The six pāramitās are also non-existent, also illusory, and without naturalness. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, all samādhis are entirely non-existent; all dhāraṇī gates are non-existent. The samādhi gates and dhāraṇī gates are also all empty and illusory; the samādhi gates and dhāraṇī gates are all non-existent; the samādhi gates and dhāraṇī gates are also all empty and illusory; the samādhi gates and dhāraṇī gates are all without naturalness. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. The six pāramitās are likewise.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the dharma-realm is also non-existent. The dharma-realm is entirely empty, the dharma-realm is illusory, the dharma-realm is naturally so; the dharma-realm is also without the seven emptinesses. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the Tathāgata is also non-existent and entirely rootless. The rootless is illusory; the rootless is also empty. The originally rootless is also without naturalness. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. The original limit is also non-existent; the original limit is entirely empty, illusory, and without naturalness; it is inconceivable. All the realms are also without naturalness. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, all śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, and tathāgatas are also non-existent. The Tathāgata is empty and illusory, also without naturalness. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. The path is non-existent, also empty and illusory, also without naturalness. Sarvajñā is also empty and illusory, also without naturalness. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past. Why? Śāriputra! Emptiness and illusoriness, past, future, and interval: these are likewise unobtainable; the bodhisattva is also unobtainable. Therefore, Śāriputra, emptiness and illusoriness, past and future, are without duality and without multiplicity. Therefore the bodhisattva does not receive the past.

"As Śāriputra has asked: 'Why is form without boundary, and feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness without boundary, and the bodhisattva also without boundary?' Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are like the emptiness of emptiness. Just as empty space has no boundary, no interval, no bottom; empty space is but a name. Śāriputra! Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise: without boundary, without interval, without bottom, because form is empty. That which is empty has no boundary, no interval, and no obtainable bottom. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. Therefore, Śāriputra, form is without boundary; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are without boundary; the bodhisattva is also without boundary. All are non-existent and unobtainable. Therefore, Śāriputra, form and the bodhisattva are both non-existent and unobtainable. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the six pāramitās are empty; because empty, they are called empty. Internal emptiness is also empty; external emptiness is also empty. Because empty, they are empty. Proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, true emptiness, and the seven emptinesses; the thirty-seven factors, the ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas: all are also empty. Because empty, they are empty. There is no original limit and no inconceivable realm. All the realms are also empty; because empty, they are empty. The samādhi gates and dhāraṇī gates are also empty. Sarvajñā is also empty. The comprehension of the factors of the path and the wisdom of the path are also empty; because empty, they are empty. The dharma of the three vehicles is also empty. The Tathāgata is also empty. Therefore, Śāriputra, the emptiness of the Tathāgata is also without existence; form is also unobtainable; form and the bodhisattva are both non-existent and entirely unobtainable. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise.

"As Śāriputra has asked: 'Why are all bodhisattvas unobtainable? How can one teach the bodhisattva the prajñāpāramitā?' Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also unobtainable. Form is unobtainable; feeling and perception are unobtainable. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are unobtainable. What is perceived: perception is also non-existent; the perceived feeling is also non-existent; the perceived formations are also non-existent; the perceived consciousness is also non-existent and unobtainable. What consciousness cognizes: cognition is also non-existent and unobtainable; the cognized form, the cognized feeling, the cognized perception, and the cognized formations are all non-existent and unobtainable. Śāriputra! The six sense faculties are also non-existent and unobtainable. The eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are all non-existent and unobtainable. The ear is entirely non-existent and unobtainable; the ear and the eye are entirely non-existent and unobtainable; the ear and the nose are entirely non-existent and unobtainable; the nose and smelling are entirely non-existent and unobtainable; the nose and the eye are entirely non-existent and unobtainable; the nose and the tongue are entirely non-existent and unobtainable; the tongue itself is entirely non-existent and unobtainable. The tongue, eye, ear, and nose are entirely non-existent and unobtainable; smell and the body are entirely non-existent and unobtainable; the body and the body itself are entirely non-existent and unobtainable; the mind and the mind itself are entirely non-existent and unobtainable. Eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are entirely non-existent and unobtainable. Eye and form, ear and sound, nose and smell, tongue and taste, body and touch, mind and desire: the six sense faculties, six consciousnesses, six objects, and the eighteen sense-fields and their conditions: all matters are entirely non-existent and unobtainable. Internal form and external form, feeling, and all dharmas are likewise. The six pāramitās and the seven emptinesses, the thirty-seven factors, the ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas, the samādhi gates and dhāraṇī gates, the dharma of the lineage, the dharma of arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, tathāgatahood, the bodhisattva-dharma, the dharma of the ten abodes, the wisdom of sarvajñā and the wisdom of the path, up to the Tathāgata and the bodhisattva: all are non-existent and unobtainable. The bodhisattva and the prajñāpāramitā are entirely non-existent and unobtainable. Furthermore, the prajñāpāramitā regarding the prajñāpāramitā is entirely non-existent and unobtainable. The prajñāpāramitā and the bodhisattva are entirely non-existent and unobtainable. The prajñāpāramitā has no words and no speech, no teaching and no conversion; it is unobtainable. Regarding the bodhisattva, there are no words and no speech, no teaching and no conversion; it is also non-existent and unobtainable. The prajñāpāramitā is also non-existent and unobtainable. Therefore, Śāriputra, all dharmas are also non-existent and without any who attains them, because they are unobtainable. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva is also unobtainable and without any teaching, as Śāriputra has said.

"Why is it designated, and from where does the designation of 'bodhisattva' come? The name: where does the bodhisattva abide, that one is called a bodhisattva? Therefore one is named 'bodhisattva.' To say 'bodhisattva' is but a name; from where does it come? Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are but names; one merely designates and speaks, yet there is no form and no feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness. Why? Names are also empty; names are naturally empty. It is not because of this that one is called a bodhisattva; there is also no inherent designation as a bodhisattva.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the six pāramitās are but names; it is not because of the name that there are six pāramitās. What is called 'bodhisattva' is but a name. What is called 'prajñāpāramitā' is but a name; it is not because of the name that there is prajñāpāramitā. The prajñāpāramitā has no name at all. Why? The name and the prajñāpāramitā: both are empty and unobtainable. Śāriputra! What is called 'bodhisattva' is but a conventional designation. What is called internal emptiness, external emptiness, proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, true emptiness, emptiness of existence, and emptiness of non-existence are but names; the seven emptinesses are not empty because of names. Why? It is not because of the name that there is emptiness; these emptinesses are unobtainable. Therefore, Śāriputra, what is called 'bodhisattva' is but a conventional designation. Śāriputra! These names are conventional designations. The foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, faculties, powers, factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, and thirty-seven factors; the ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are but conventional designations. It is not because of the name that there are buddha-dharmas; the buddha-dharmas are empty. Therefore, Śāriputra, what is called 'bodhisattva' is but a conventional designation. The samādhi gates and dhāraṇī gates; stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, bodhisattvahood, up to buddhahood: all are also conventional designations, not making names into names. What is called self and 'mine,' when one investigates the root and end, is also non-existent and without accomplishment. The self is unobtainable; how much less can there be any attainment on the path? What is known and seen is also unobtainable; how much less can one wish something to be accomplished? Śāriputra! Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness: the root and end are also unobtainable; how much less can one wish consciousness to accomplish the eye, or the eye and the conditions of contact and feeling? Ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind; the six sense-fields are also unobtainable. The six pāramitās and seven emptinesses: the root and end are empty and also unobtainable; how much less can one wish something to be accomplished? The thirty-seven factors, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas: when one investigates the root and end, they are also unobtainable; how much less can one wish something to be accomplished? The samādhi gates and dhāraṇī gates: when one investigates the root and end, all is unobtainable; how much less can one wish something to be accomplished? Śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, tathāgatas, arhats, samyak-saṃbuddhas are entirely unobtainable. Therefore, Śāriputra, what is called self is entirely non-existent; all dharmas are also non-existent; all is naturally so. Why? The natural has no conjunction and no dispersion."

Śāriputra asked Subhūti: "What do you mean by 'naturally without conjunction and dispersion'?"

He answered: "Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, being natural, have no conjunction and no dispersion. The eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind; what the six sense faculties receive and give rise to; the conjunction of feeling: all is naturally so, without conjunction and without dispersion. The six pāramitās are also without conjunction and without dispersion; all is naturally so. Therefore, Śāriputra, all dharmas are entirely non-existent; all is naturally so.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, all dharmas have no permanence and no destination."

Śāriputra asked Subhūti: "What do you mean by 'all dharmas have no permanence and no destination'?"

Subhūti said: "Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no permanence and no destination. Why? That which has no permanence is entirely non-existent and without any existence. Therefore all dharmas have no permanence and no destination. All dharmas with their existence are likewise: all are without permanence and without destination. All that has outflows, and even that which is without outflows; whatever can be spoken of, and the dharma without any speech; that which has permanence is entirely non-existent and without any existence. Therefore, Śāriputra, all myriad things have no permanence and no destination.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, all dharmas have no accumulation and no destruction."

Again he asked Subhūti: "How is it that all dharmas have no accumulation and no destruction?"

He answered: "Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no accumulation and no destruction. Why? Because they are pure. All wholesome and unwholesome, existent and non-existent dharmas, dharmas with and without outflows: all have no accumulation and no destruction. Why? Because they are pure. Therefore, Śāriputra, all that exists is entirely non-existent.

"Śāriputra has asked: 'From where does form arise?' Form has no arising; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no arising. Why? Śāriputra, form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are entirely non-existent. The practitioner who comprehends finds no form and no arising; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness also have no arising. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are entirely non-existent. Why? The practitioner who comprehends finds no existence of the eye; the eye is non-existent. Why? The practitioner who comprehends finds all non-existent; the six sense faculties are likewise.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, all dharmas are entirely non-existent. Why? The practitioner who comprehends creates nothing that exists. Therefore, Śāriputra, form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no arising.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, what you have asked about: form having no arising means it is not form, nor is it feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness. Why? Form is pure and empty, without arising or ceasing, without any abode, and without any distinction. Because feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also pure, emptiness is pure; therefore it is called pure, without any arising, without any ceasing, without any abode, and indistinguishable. All that exists is also pure; because emptiness is pure, it is called pure, without any arising, without any ceasing, without any abode, and unknowable through discrimination. Therefore, Śāriputra, form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no arising.

"As Śāriputra has asked: 'Why do you say all this is unborn? From where shall one teach the prajñāpāramitā? The prajñāpāramitā also has no arising. If there is no arising, the prajñāpāramitā also has no emergence; there is no duality and no multiplicity.' Therefore this is said; from where shall one teach the prajñāpāramitā? Śāriputra asked: 'The bodhisattva does not arise from any different place, and one attains the path-practice.' Why? The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the prajñāpāramitā does not arise from anything different and does not perceive anything different. The prajñāpāramitā also does not distinguish a different place, yet sees everything equally; the practices of all bodhisattvas also have no arising. Furthermore, the bodhisattva has no duality and no multiplicity; one does not perceive form, feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness arising from any different place. Why? Because there is no arising, form has no duality and no multiplicity; it does not arise from anything different and has no different arising; one does not perceive form arising from any different place. Why? Form has no arising; consciousness has no designation and no multiplicity. The eighteen elements, thirty-seven factors, buddha-dharmas, the seven emptinesses, and the dharma of the three vehicles: one does not perceive their arising. Why? Because there is no arising, there is no duality and no multiplicity. Therefore, Śāriputra, one does not find the bodhisattva arising from any different place and practicing the path.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, regarding what was previously asked: 'Suppose the bodhisattva-mahāsattva hears this teaching without any terror, without fear, and without any dread; this constitutes practicing the prajñāpāramitā.' Why? The bodhisattva-mahāsattva contemplates all dharmas as entirely like a dream, like an illusion, a mirage, a plantain, a shadow, an echo. Therefore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who hears this without terror, without fear, and without dread is practicing the prajñāpāramitā."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "God among Gods! When the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practices the prajñāpāramitā and contemplates dharmas thus, one does not receive form, feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness; one neither rejects, abides in, nor clings to the prajñāpāramitā. In the prajñāpāramitā there is no form, feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness; one does not receive, reject, abide in, or cling to any of them, without any discrimination. One does not receive the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, mind, and the six sense faculties on which they depend; one does not receive self. One does not receive the dāna-pāramitā; one neither rejects, abides in, nor clings to it; one does not abide in self. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are likewise. One does not receive the seven emptinesses; one neither rejects, abides in, nor clings to them; one does not abide in self.

"Furthermore, God among Gods, the practitioner of the prajñāpāramitā, regarding the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, is likewise: one does not receive, reject, abide in, or cling to them; one does not abide in self.

"Furthermore, God among Gods, the bodhisattva does not receive any samādhi gate or dhāraṇī gate; one does not receive, reject, abide in, or cling to them; one does not abide in self. Why? The bodhisattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā does not perceive form, feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness; does not perceive the eighteen elements, thirty-seven factors, or seven emptinesses; does not perceive śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas; up to the Buddha and sarvajñā, one perceives nothing. Why? There is no form, feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness; there is no arising and no consciousness. The six sense faculties have no arising and there are no six sense faculties. The six pāramitās have no arising and there are no six pāramitās. The prajñāpāramitā has no arising, and there is no duality and no multiplicity. Internal emptiness and external emptiness have no arising; proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, true emptiness, emptiness of existence, and emptiness of non-existence are likewise. Why? The seven emptinesses have no arising, and there is no duality and no multiplicity. Therefore, God among Gods, the seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas have no arising, and there is no duality and no multiplicity. Why? God among Gods, this is non-arising. Therefore there is no duality and no three; because there is no multiplicity, the buddha-dharmas are all without arising. If there were arising, it would not be the buddha-dharma. O God among Gods, that which is rootless is also inconceivable. The dharma-realm of all dharmas also has no arising. The inconceivable realm has no duality and no multiplicity. O God among Gods, stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, and bodhisattvahood, up to the wisdom of sarvajñā: all are without arising and non-existent. Therefore sarvajñā is without arising. Why? There is no exertion; this is without duality, without three, and without multiplicity. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are completely ceased, and there is no form; therefore consciousness is also completely ceased, and there is no duality and no multiplicity. Why? God among Gods, exertion has no one, no two, no three, and no multiplicity. The exertion of consciousness also has no consciousness. This is the dāna-pāramitā: also without arising, without exertion, without duality, without three, and without multiplicity. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are likewise, as are the seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas. His words: 'God among Gods, there is no exertion!' In this practice, no one can reckon the five aggregates, six sense-objects, six pāramitās, the dharma of the three vehicles, up to the wisdom of sarvajñā; they are likewise."

### Chapter Twenty-Four: Contemplative Practice

At that time, Subhūti said to Śāriputra: "How does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practice the prajñāpāramitā and contemplate dharmas? What does it mean that the bodhisattva practices the path for all people, and that the bodhisattva comprehends all dharmas of the path, and regarding all dharmas has no attachment? To comprehend all dharmas is to comprehend form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, and regarding the matters of consciousness, to have no attachment. To comprehend the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas, and to have no attachment. What are the matters of all dharmas?"

Subhūti said to Śāriputra: "To contemplate the form, image, signs, and portents of all dharmas; form, sound, smell, taste, tangibility, and dharmas; internal and external dharmas, conditioned and unconditioned, existent and non-existent; form, image, signs, and portents are understood to be without causation. This is contemplating dharmas.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra has asked: 'What is the prajñāpāramitā?' Complete non-delight is called the prajñāpāramitā. What is 'complete non-delight'? Śāriputra! Not delighting in the aggregates, elements, or sense-fields; not delighting in the six pāramitās: the śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā; not delighting in the seven emptinesses; not delighting in the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas: this is called complete non-delight. This is the prajñāpāramitā. Regarding sarvajñā also having no delight: this is the prajñāpāramitā. This is called complete non-delight; this is the prajñāpāramitā.

"Regarding what was asked, 'What is contemplation?' The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, when practicing the prajñāpāramitā, does not contemplate form as permanent or impermanent; does not contemplate form as suffering or happiness; does not contemplate form as having self or being without self; does not contemplate form as empty or not-empty, with characteristics or without characteristics, with wish or without wish; does not contemplate form as quiescent or not-quiescent; does not contemplate form as illusory or not-illusory. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, the seven emptinesses, and the three gates of liberation are likewise. One does not contemplate the thirty-seven factors: the foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, bases of supernatural power, faculties, powers, seven factors of awakening, and Eightfold Path, or the buddha-dharmas, as suffering or happiness, good or evil, having self or being without self, permanent or impermanent. The samādhi gates, dhāraṇī gates, and the wisdom of sarvajñā: permanent or impermanent, suffering or happiness, good or evil, having self or being without self, empty or not-empty, and the three gates of liberation. Śāriputra! This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's contemplative practice of the prajñāpāramitā."

Śāriputra asked Subhūti: "What do you mean by 'form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no arising, and consciousness is therefore non-existent'; and that the faculties, powers, factors of awakening, thirty-seven factors, seven emptinesses, four laws of impermanence, and the wisdom of sarvajñā all have no arising, and sarvajñā is therefore non-existent?"

Subhūti said to Śāriputra: "Form and the seven emptinesses: that which is empty has no form. Therefore form is without arising, and there is no form. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. The six pāramitās are empty; that which is already empty is not the prajñāpāramitā; wisdom has no arising. Therefore, Śāriputra, the prajñāpāramitā has no arising and is not the prajñāpāramitā; the seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, buddha-dharmas, samādhi gates, dhāraṇī gates, and the wisdom of sarvajñā are likewise. Form having no arising means there is no form, no feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness; up to the wisdom of sarvajñā, it is likewise. That which has no arising has no wisdom."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "What do you mean by 'form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, up to the wisdom of sarvajñā, have no duality'?"

Subhūti said: "It is so, it is so! That which is without duality: form has no duality. Feeling, perception, formations, consciousness, and all dharmas of consciousness have no conjunction and no dispersion, no form and no perception, nothing to grasp or reject. Such a characteristic is without any thought. The seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, four laws of impermanence, and the wisdom of sarvajñā are likewise. The five aggregates and six sense-objects, up to sarvajñā: all are without duality."

Śāriputra asked Subhūti: "What do you mean by 'form has no duality, is pure, and is without coming'; and feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, up to the wisdom of sarvajñā?"

Subhūti said to Śāriputra: "It is so, it is so! Form is not different and has no arising; and that which has no arising is also not different from form. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, up to the wisdom of sarvajñā, are likewise. Thus, Śāriputra, form has no duality. The five aggregates and six sense-objects, up to the wisdom of sarvajñā, are also without duality; all are pure and without any coming."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, when practicing the prajñāpāramitā and contemplating dharmas, sees that all form has no arising and is originally pure. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. Self, knowledge, and perception are all without arising and originally pure. The dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are likewise: all are without arising and originally pure. The seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, faculties, powers, factors of awakening, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas: one does not perceive their arising; they are originally pure. One contemplates the samādhi gates, dhāraṇī gates, and the wisdom of sarvajñā and does not perceive their arising; they are originally pure. One contemplates the dharma of ordinary people and sees the dharma of ordinary people: all is without arising and originally pure. One contemplates stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, and bodhisattvas, and sees all these dharmas as entirely without arising and originally pure. One contemplates all buddha-dharmas and sees them as without arising and originally pure; one does not perceive any arising."

Śāriputra asked Subhūti: "How should one understand what you have now said? The five aggregates, six sense-objects, the dharma of the three vehicles, and sarvajñā are all without arising. If so, there are no five destinies, no bodhisattva-mahāsattva, and no attainment of supernatural powers. If, Subhūti, all dharmas are entirely without arising, why then does the stream-enterer sever the three fetters and cultivate the path? Why does the once-returner also sever the three fetters, with desire, anger, and delusion becoming thin, and cultivate the path? Why does the non-returner cast off the heavy burden, sever all the fetters, and cultivate the path? Why does the arhat sever and remove all fetters and the five faculties, having no more birth-and-death, and cultivate the path? Why does the pratyekabuddha vehicle awaken through causation and cultivate the path? Why does the bodhisattva diligently practice the path with hardship for innumerable sentient beings? Why does one accomplish anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi and turn the dharma-wheel?"

Subhūti said: "I do not wish to have the dharma of non-arising attain anything, nor do I wish the dharma of non-arising to reach stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, or pratyekabuddhahood; these are likewise. I also do not cause the bodhisattva-mahāsattva to practice with hardship, nor cause the bodhisattva to diligently practice with hardship. Why? Śāriputra! It is not through different characteristics and diligent hardship that one delivers incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the practitioner of the bodhisattva-path should deliver incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings, thinking of them as a mother, thinking of them as a father, thinking of them as a child, thinking of them as oneself; and one's practice also has no arising. The bodhisattva should think: 'When one seeks self, all is non-existent and unobtainable; one should understand internal and external dharmas thus.' If one gives rise to conceptual thought, one does not think of diligent hardship and does not give rise to thought. Why? All dharmas are entirely without arising and unobtainable.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, I also do not wish to make the Tathāgata without arising, without anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi, nor do I wish him to not turn the dharma-wheel, nor do I wish to attain the dharma of non-arising."

Śāriputra asked Subhūti: "What do you mean? Do you wish there to be arising in order to attain dharma? But you say that non-arising does not attain dharmas."

Subhūti said: "Not through non-arising does one attain dharmas, nor through arising does one attain dharmas."

Again he asked Subhūti: "How is it that the dharma of non-arising, and also not non-arising, attains dharmas?"

Subhūti said: "I do not wish to make non-arising arise to attain dharmas, nor do I wish to make there be nothing attained."

Śāriputra said: "What does Subhūti think? Is there no attainment and no accomplishment of the path?"

Subhūti said: "There is attainment and there is the path; in truth there is no duality. Furthermore, Śāriputra, attainment and accomplishment of the path are worldly, conventional speech. What is called stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, and pratyekabuddhahood: all exist through conventional teaching, giving rise to these words. When one investigates the root and end, there is no attainment, no accomplishment of the path, and no three vehicles."

Śāriputra asked Subhūti: "Is the attainment and accomplishment of the path based on worldly convention? Thus the five destinies are worldly, conventional speech; all that exists is destroyed and is not the true truth."

He answered: "It is so; what is said is based on worldly convention. One says there is attainment and accomplishment of the path; the five destinies are likewise. Worldly convention is entirely destroyed; it is not the true truth. Why? Wishing to accomplish the true truth, there is no good or evil, no arising or ceasing, no defilements and no anger or hatred. This is the true truth."

Śāriputra asked Subhūti: "Does the unborn dharma have any arising? Does the born dharma give rise to birth?"

Subhūti said: "The unborn dharma also has no arising; the born dharma also does not arise."

Śāriputra said: "How can one wish the unborn dharma to have arising?"

Subhūti said: "Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness also have no arising; they are naturally empty. One does not wish them to arise. Śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, up to the buddha-path: all are without arising, naturally empty. One does not wish them to arise."

Śāriputra said: "Does the born have arising? Does the unborn give rise to birth?"

Subhūti said: "The born also has no arising; the unborn also has no arising. Why? Śāriputra! The born and the unborn: these two dharmas have no conjunction and no dispersion, no form and no perception, nothing to be received or held. They constitute a single characteristic, the characteristic of non-existence. Therefore, Śāriputra, the born and the unborn: the unborn also does not arise."

Śāriputra said: "Who can be equal to the dharma of non-arising? Subhūti! The dharma of non-arising, its non-arising, and the dharma of non-arising also have no arising."

Subhūti said: "The non-arising of non-arising: the dharma of non-arising is non-arising; one who is equal to non-arising: the dharma of non-arising is non-arising. Why? The dharma of non-arising, that which is non-arising, together with eloquence, are all non-arising. All these dharmas have no conjunction and no dispersion, no form and no perception, nothing to be received or held. They constitute a single characteristic, the characteristic of non-existence."

Śāriputra said: "Non-arising and non-arising eloquence: the dharma of non-arising also has no arising. Therefore one is equal to it?"

Subhūti said: "It is so, it is so! Because of non-arising, there is non-arising eloquence. The dharma of non-arising also has no arising; this is being equal to it. Why? Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness also have no arising. The six sense faculties and four great elements, the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind also have no arising. Earth, water, fire, wind, space, and the consciousness element also have no arising. Actions of body, speech, and mind also have no arising. Śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, up to the Buddha also have no arising. Therefore, Śāriputra, non-arising eloquence has no non-arising; the dharma of non-arising therefore has no arising. The practitioner of this is able to be equal to the dharma of non-arising."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "What the worthy Subhūti has taught is the foremost and most honored. Why? Whatever is asked, one responds to each question, and regarding all dharmas, one has no attachment."

Śāriputra said: "How is it that regarding all dharmas one has no attachment?"

Subhūti said: "Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are pure and empty, without any attachment, neither internal nor external, and without any interval. The six sense-fields, the eighteen elements, are also empty and pure, not attached to internal or external, and without any interval. The six pāramitās and the seven emptinesses, the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are also pure and empty, not attached to internal or external, and without any interval. Thus, Śāriputra, regarding all dharmas one has no attachment. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who practices the six pāramitās: regarding form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, all is pure, up to sarvajñā; all is pure."

Śāriputra said: "What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's exclusive practice of the six pāramitās that purifies the bodhisattva-path?"

Subhūti said: "The dāna-pāramitā has worldly giving that does not constitute crossing beyond. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā have worldly wisdom and also transcendent wisdom."

Śāriputra asked: "What is the worldly dāna-pāramitā and the transcendent dāna-pāramitā?"

Subhūti said: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva gives generously to śramaṇas, brāhmaṇas, the poor, and beggars: food to the hungry, drink to the thirsty, incense, flowers, music, residences, the seven jewels, the necessities of life, medicine for the sick. According to each person's desire, whether sons and daughters, spouse and children, head, eyes, and flesh: whatever people covet, one gives without begrudging, generously bestowing all. One calls out: 'I give this without any jealousy! I am a donor who relinquishes all, following the Buddha's teaching and practicing the dāna-pāramitā.' Having given thus, one has expectations. Regarding all sentient beings, one's intention is deluded, taking this as essential. One uses the merit to encourage anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. Through this giving, one causes all beings to have peace and security in the present life and to attain parinirvāṇa in the realm without remainder. In this, one conjoins three matters when giving. What are the three? The thought of self, the thought of 'I,' and the reckoning that others exist with the thought of the reward of giving. These are the three. This is the worldly dāna-pāramitā, not the transcendent. Why is it called the worldly dāna-pāramitā, not the transcendent?
