Abiding in the world without change, one does not attain liberation to the unobstructed. This is called the worldly dāna-pāramitā. One can purify three things. What are the three? The bodhisattva-mahāsattva gives without apprehending self, without perceiving a recipient, and whatever is grasped, without conceiving of a reward. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's purification of the three things.

"Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva gives to sentient beings, yet there is no person. Through this, one encourages anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi, without any thought of a multitude, without perceiving anything. This is the transcendent dāna-pāramitā. Why is it called the dāna-pāramitā? Because it is transcendent, one is not attached to the world. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are likewise: with expectations, it is worldly wisdom; without expectations, it is transcendent wisdom. Śāriputra! This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's exclusive practice of the six pāramitās that accomplishes the bodhisattva-path."

Śāriputra again asked Subhūti: "What is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's accomplishment of the bodhisattva-path?"

Subhūti said: "The foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, bases of supernatural power, faculties, powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas; the three gates of liberation of emptiness, signlessness, and wishlessness; the seven emptinesses; all samādhis and dhāraṇī gates; the four analytical knowledges, great lovingkindness, and great compassion: this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's path."

Śāriputra said: "Excellent, excellent! Subhūti! Which pāramitā is able to accomplish courageous vigor and is the foremost for crossing beyond?"

Subhūti said: "The prajñāpāramitā, through its grace of courageous vigor, accomplishes the crossing beyond. Why? The prajñāpāramitā is the mother of all dharmas. It protects and delivers śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, causing them to accomplish the bodhisattva; therefore it is called the prajñāpāramitā. The prajñāpāramitā fully enters the three vehicles. Past, future, and present tathāgatas, arhats, samyak-saṃbuddhas in the buddha-worlds of the ten directions all, through the prajñāpāramitā, attain anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi and accomplish abhisaṃbuddhahood. If there is a bodhisattva-mahāsattva who hears the teaching of the prajñāpāramitā without any doubt and without hesitation, one should know that this bodhisattva-mahāsattva is a leader of all sentient beings. For the sake of all, without any attachment, one can give everything without any delusion. This person does not depart from the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice. To think thus is to contemplate the immeasurable great compassion."

Śāriputra said to the venerable Subhūti: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who contemplates and delights in great compassion: this bodhisattva-mahāsattva is then departing from all sentient beings. Why? Because all sentient beings do not depart from thought."

Subhūti said: "Excellent, excellent! Śāriputra! I now praise what the worthy one has said, for it is true and genuine. Persons are non-existent; what is thought is also non-existent. Persons are not naturally so; what is thought is also not naturally so. Persons are empty; thoughts are also empty. Persons are illusory; thoughts are also illusory. The person-body is empty and void; thoughts are also empty and void. Persons have no awareness; thoughts also have no awareness. Form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also non-existent; what is thought is also non-existent. The seven emptinesses are also non-existent. Non-existent form is empty and illusory; form has no awareness, and thoughts also have no awareness. The eighteen elements, earth, water, fire, wind, consciousness-element; the dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā; the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas; all samādhis and dhāraṇī gates; the wisdom of sarvajñā: one who comprehends all these finds them entirely non-existent. This is the path. What is thought is non-existent; persons have no awareness, and what is thought also has no awareness. One should comprehend this and thereby accomplish right awakening. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva should practice thus. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who does not depart from this thought thereby accomplishes right awakening."

At that time, the Buddha praised Subhūti: "Excellent, excellent! The bodhisattva-mahāsattva should teach the prajñāpāramitā in this way. As you have said, all is sustained by the divine power of the Tathāgata. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva should practice the prajñāpāramitā in this way."

When the worthy Subhūti was teaching the prajñāpāramitā, the great trichiliocosm shook in six ways: east, west, south, north, above, and below all trembled. At that time, the Buddha smiled.

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "Now, God among Gods, why do you smile? There must be a meaning."

The Buddha told Subhūti: "Just as I today in this land of endurance teach the prajñāpāramitā, the presently existing tathāgatas, arhats, samyak-saṃbuddhas in the ten directions also each teach the prajñāpāramitā."

When the Buddha spoke these words, twelve nayutas of devas and humans all attained the patient acceptance of the non-arising of dharmas. At that time, all were able to see the buddhas of the ten directions, all teaching the prajñāpāramitā. When these words were spoken, innumerable asaṃkhyeya beings all generated the aspiration for anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi.

## Fascicle Ten

### Chapter Twenty-Five: Questions

At that time, all the Śakras of the great trichiliocosm, all the Four Heavenly Kings, all the Yāma devas, all the Tuṣita devas, all the Nirmāṇarati devas, all the Paranirmitavaśavartin devas, all the Brahmā devas, all the Brahmakāyika devas, and all the Śuddhāvāsa devas, each with innumerable hundreds of thousands of devas and humans, gathered together. These devas and humans, by virtue of past merit, had majestic radiance; yet compared to the Tathāgata's light, even a hundred billion, a thousand billion, a myriad billion times greater, the Tathāgata's light was the most honored, the highest, without equal or match, pervading everywhere. At that time, Śakra addressed the worthy Subhūti: "Now all the Four Heavenly Kings of the great trichiliocosm, all the Śuddhāvāsa devas, and all the devas and humans have come to this great assembly, wishing to hear Subhūti teach the dharma of the prajñāpāramitā. How does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva abide in the prajñāpāramitā? How should one practice?"

Subhūti said to Śakra: "If the devas delight in listening, I shall teach."

Subhūti, sustained by the Buddha's divine power and aided by the Buddha's grace, taught the prajñāpāramitā: "As the bodhisattvas should establish their practice: may all devas who have not yet generated the aspiration for anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi now generate it. Those who have entered right view cannot generate the aspiration for the great path. Why? Because it blocks the path of birth-and-death. Even if these people practice the bodhisattva-path, I rejoice on their behalf, encouraging them to generate the aspiration for anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. I shall never sever their merit. I wish them to take up the correct and honored dharma; I wish them to ascend to the Buddha's limitless path."

Subhūti said to Śakra: "Regarding what you asked: 'How does the bodhisattva abide in the prajñāpāramitā?' The bodhisattva-mahāsattva generates the aspiration for sarvajñā, not reckoning form as permanent or impermanent, as suffering or happiness, as having self or being without self; not reckoning the affliction of illness, grief, or distress; not reckoning harmfulness or harmlessness, bondage or freedom, deliverance or non-deliverance. Through dissolution and fearlessness, through habituation and meeting, one reaches the body of emptiness and nothingness, completely without any reliance, without any contention, without any thought, and without any delusion. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. Eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind; earth, water, fire, wind, space, and the consciousness element: one does not perceive permanence or impermanence, self or non-self, suffering or happiness, illness, grief, or affliction. Regarding all sounds and forms, one has no thought and no delusion. The five aggregates, six sense-objects, and the consciousness elements are quiescent and illusory. Whatever thoughts examine the buddha-dharma, all are delusion.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, wishing to accord with the aspiration for sarvajñā, practices the dāna-pāramitā without any attachment; the śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, and dhyāna-pāramitā are all without any attachment.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, practicing the prajñāpāramitā, contemplates and comprehends all dharmas. Comprehending all dharmas, they progressively accomplish one another. Through progressively accomplishing one another, one comprehends all dharmas: there is no self and no body. The aspiration for the path that the bodhisattva encourages: that aspiration for the path is also non-existent."

Subhūti said to Kauśika: "Knowing that the encouraged aspiration for the path is non-existent, one then knows that the aspiration for the path, being non-existent, is unobtainable. If one encourages the aspiration for the path and it is unobtainable, this, Kauśika, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's prajñāpāramitā contemplation of all dharmas: one does not perceive any dharma that can be obtained."

Śakra asked the venerable Subhūti: "How is the encouraged aspiration for the path non-existent? How is the encouraged aspiration for the path unobtainable? How is the encouraged aspiration for the path non-existent and unobtainable?"

Subhūti said to Śakra: "Kauśika! The encouraged mind, the root of mind, and the aspiration for the path: thus there is no different mind. There being no mind, one encourages with non-mind. There being no thought, one encourages with non-thought. If through non-mind there is non-mind, then there is no thought. Through having no thought, this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's prajñāpāramitā."

The Buddha said: "Excellent, excellent! Subhūti! That you are able to encourage the bodhisattva-mahāsattva and teach the prajñāpāramitā: it is indeed thus."

Subhūti addressed the Buddha: "I myself, God among Gods, should repay the Buddha's grace and practice reciprocity. Why? The past tathāgatas, arhats, samyak-saṃbuddhas instructed their disciples to teach the prajñāpāramitā for the bodhisattvas. In the time of past buddhas, one encouraged and taught the six pāramitās for the bodhisattvas, praising, guiding, and advancing them, establishing them in the factors of the path. At that time, the World-Honored One originally cultivated the six pāramitās with the bodhisattvas, attained anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi, and accomplished abhisaṃbuddhahood. Now I likewise, God among Gods, should also encourage all the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas, arousing their faith and delight in receiving the six pāramitās, teaching and establishing them on this buddha-path. Having received it all and having encouraged their delight, with earnest encouragement and establishment, I shall cause the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas to swiftly accomplish anuttarā abhisaṃbuddhahood."

Subhūti said to Śakra: "Now listen, Kauśika! Regarding what you asked: 'How should the bodhisattva abide in the prajñāpāramitā, and yet have no abode?' Kauśika! What is called form: form is empty. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also empty. What is called 'bodhisattva': the bodhisattva is empty. Because form is empty, the bodhisattva is empty; there is no duality and no multiplicity. Because feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are empty, the bodhisattva is empty; there is no duality and no multiplicity. This, Kauśika, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's abiding in the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, what is called 'eye': the eye is empty. Ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are likewise. What is called 'bodhisattva': the bodhisattva is also empty. Because eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are empty, the bodhisattva is empty; there is no duality and no multiplicity. Earth, water, fire, and wind are all empty; therefore the bodhisattva is empty. The six matters within the body are all non-existent; the root and end are entirely empty, and there is no duality and no multiplicity. Thus, Kauśika, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva abides in the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā understands that ignorance is empty. Form, the six sense-fields, contact, feeling, craving, grasping, becoming, birth, and aging, illness, and death are also empty. Because the twelve links of dependent origination are completely ceased, they are called empty. Because the twelve links of dependent origination are empty, the bodhisattva is empty. The twelve links of dependent origination being empty, the bodhisattva being empty: there is no duality and no multiplicity. Thus, Kauśika, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva abides in the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, because the dāna-pāramitā is empty, the bodhisattva is empty. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā being empty, it is likewise. Because the six pāramitās are empty, the bodhisattva is empty. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's abiding in the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, because internal emptiness, external emptiness, proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, true emptiness, emptiness of existence, and emptiness of non-existence are empty, the bodhisattva is empty. The four foundations of mindfulness, four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, all samādhis, and dhāraṇī gates being empty, the bodhisattva is empty. The six pāramitās, thirty-seven factors, seven emptinesses, buddha-dharmas, samādhis, and dhāraṇīs being empty: there is no duality and no multiplicity. This, Kauśika, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's abiding in the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, because stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, bodhisattvahood, tathāgatahood, arhatship, and samyak-saṃbuddhahood are empty, the bodhisattva is empty. The four emptinesses, the emptiness of śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, the emptiness of the Tathāgata, and the emptiness of the bodhisattva: there is no duality and no multiplicity. This, Kauśika, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's abiding in the prajñāpāramitā.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, because sarvajñā is empty, and because sarvajñā is empty the bodhisattva is empty; the emptiness of sarvajñā and the emptiness of the bodhisattva: there is no duality and no multiplicity. This, Kauśika, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's abiding in the prajñāpāramitā."

At that time, Śakra asked the venerable Subhūti: "How does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva abide in the prajñāpāramitā?"

Subhūti said to Śakra: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā should not abide in form; should not abide in feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness. Should not abide in the habituations of the eye; ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are likewise, without any habituation and entirely without any abode. Earth, water, fire, and wind elements are also without any habituation and without any abode. Should not abide in the foundations of mindfulness, correct exertions, faculties, powers, factors of awakening, or Eightfold Path. Should not abide in sarvajñā. Should not abide in stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, or the buddha-path. Should not abide in form as permanent or impermanent; should not abide in feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness as permanent or impermanent. Should not abide in form as suffering or happiness; should not abide in form as pure or impure; should not abide in form as mine or not mine; should not abide in form as empty or not empty; should not abide in quiescence or non-quiescence; should not abide in illusory or non-illusory. Should not abide in the existence or non-existence of stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, or buddhahood. Should not abide in the blessings of the four paths. Should not abide in the blessings of the pratyekabuddha or the Buddha.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā should not abide in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, eighth, ninth, or tenth bodhisattva ground. From the initial generation of aspiration through to the stage of non-retrogression, one should have no abode. The bodhisattva should not abide in the fulfillment of the dāna-pāramitā; the śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā are likewise. Should not abide in the thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, or eighteen unique buddha-dharmas. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva should not make the thought: 'I have entered the bodhisattva-dharma.' Should not make this abode: 'I have entered the stage of non-retrogression.' The bodhisattva-mahāsattva should not abide in the five supernatural powers; should not abide in the bodhisattva's five supernatural powers, which traverse innumerable asaṃkhyeya buddha-fields to see the buddhas, God among Gods, to pay homage, and to hear the dharma they teach, and as one has received the dharma, to teach it to the assembly. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva should not make this abode: 'As that Buddha, God among Gods, has manifested his land, I shall likewise transform the world.' The bodhisattva-mahāsattva should not make this abode: 'I shall teach and convert all sentient beings.' Should not think: 'I shall dwell in innumerable asaṃkhyeya worlds, see all the tathāgatas, and make offerings of flowers, incense, powdered incense, mixed incense, silk banners, and parasols.' Should not think: 'I shall teach and convert innumerable asaṃkhyeya beings, causing them to generate the aspiration for anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi.' The bodhisattva-mahāsattva should not make the thought: 'I shall establish and fully accomplish the five eyes.' What are the five? The flesh eye, the divine eye, the wisdom eye, the dharma eye, and the buddha eye. Should not think: 'I shall establish all equality and accomplish the samādhi gates, delighting therein.' Should not think of oneself: 'I shall attain the dhāraṇī gates, the Tathāgata's ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, four unguarded aspects, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas.' Should not think: 'I shall be fully endowed with great lovingkindness and great compassion.' Should not abide in the thirty-two marks and the eighty secondary characteristics that adorn the body. Should not abide in the eight stages of earnest faith and upholding the dharma. Should not abide in stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, or pratyekabuddhahood. Should not abide in the stream-enterer's seven deaths and seven rebirths before crossing beyond. Should not abide in the once-returner's single birth, reaching the end of all defilements. Should not abide in the stream-enterer's parinirvāṇa in the interval. Should not abide in the once-returner's fruit. Why? Going and returning in the world, one exhausts suffering and attains cessation. Should not abide in the realization of the non-returner's fruit. Why? Having accomplished non-returning, one attains parinirvāṇa in the heavens. Should not abide in the realization of the arhat's fruit. Why? Having accomplished the arhat's path, one dwells in the realm of nirvāṇa without remainder in this very life. One should not attain parinirvāṇa there; therefore one should not abide. The pratyekabuddha-path surpasses the ground of the śrāvaka but cannot reach the buddha-path of parinirvāṇa; therefore one should not abide in the pratyekabuddha-path. Should not abide in the matters of the path; regarding the wisdom of the path, one has no attachment. Should not abide in the wisdom of sarvajñā. Why? The wisdom of sarvajñā comprehends all dharmas and accomplishes abhisaṃbuddhahood, severing all obstructions and the fetters of defilement. Why? When the Tathāgata accomplishes abhisaṃbuddhahood, he turns the dharma-wheel, performing the buddha's work, delivering incalculable asaṃkhyeya beings and causing them to attain parinirvāṇa; therefore the Buddha should not abide therein. Abiding in the four bases of supernatural power, with this form and samādhi, one transcends the samādhi and remains for kalpas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. Should not abide in innumerable lifespans. Should not abide in the thirty-two marks. Each mark is accomplished through a hundred merits of virtue. Should not abide in buddha-worlds as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. Should not abide in any single buddha-field of the east, west, south, north, four intermediate directions, above, or below. Should not abide in making the ten directions' buddha-fields into a single land. Should not abide in sitting beneath the bodhi-tree, and when the fragrance arises in this form, causing all sentient beings who smell this fragrance not to be bound by desire, anger, or delusion, not generating the intention of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, all aspiring to anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi. When sentient beings smell this fragrance, their body, speech, and mind are all free from illness. In that buddha-field, one also has no abode; there is no sound of form, no sound of feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness. Should not abide in the sound of the dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, or prajñāpāramitā. Should not abide in the sound of the four correct exertions, four bases of supernatural power, five faculties, five powers, seven factors of awakening, Eightfold Path, ten powers, fearlessnesses, or eighteen unique buddha-dharmas. Should not abide in the sound of stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, parinirvāṇa, tathāgatahood, arhatship, samyak-saṃbuddhahood, abhisaṃbuddhahood, or the dharma-sound. Thus, Kauśika, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā should not abide in any of these sounds of attachment."

At that time, the worthy Śāriputra thought to himself: "How does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practice the prajñāpāramitā?"

Subhūti, knowing what Śāriputra was thinking, said to Śāriputra: "What do you think? Where does the Tathāgata abide?"

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "The Tathāgata has no abode and yet is not without abode. The Buddha has no mind and no form; he does not abide in form, does not abide in feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness; does not abide in the conditioned realm or the unconditioned realm; does not abide in the emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, or the wisdom of sarvajñā."

Subhūti said to Śāriputra: "It is so, it is so! The bodhisattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā should abide in this way. Just as the Tathāgata, Arhat, Samyak-saṃbuddha abides and yet has no abode, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva studying the prajñāpāramitā should abide in this way: abiding in non-abiding."

At that time, the devas in the assembly each thought to themselves: "The speech and thoughts of yakṣas can be understood; the sounds that writing conveys can be known. But the words and speech of Subhūti cannot be understood."

Subhūti, knowing what the devas were thinking, said to the devas: "Do you not understand?"

The devas answered: "We do not understand."

Then Subhūti explained to the devas: "There is not a single letter that can be spoken; there is no distinguishing and no one who hears. Why? The prajñāpāramitā has no letters and no speech; there is also no one who listens. Why? The Tathāgata has no letters. By way of analogy, devas, suppose the Tathāgata were to transform and create transformation-beings, and those transformation-beings were to transform the four assemblies of bhikṣus, bhikṣuṇīs, upāsakas, and upāsikās, transforming the four assemblies and teaching the dharma for them. What do the devas think? Would there be anyone who teaches and anyone who understands?"

They answered: "No."

Subhūti said: "Thus, devas, all dharmas are also transformations; there is no teacher and no listener. It is like hearing the Buddha teach a sūtra in a dream. What do you think? Is there anyone who teaches and anyone who listens and understands?"

They answered: "No."

Subhūti said: "Devas! All dharmas are entirely like a dream; there is no teaching, no hearing, and no one who knows. Suppose, devas, two persons standing at the gate of hell praise the Buddha, dharma, and sangha, and the voices of the two persons both emerge. What do you think? Does the first voice respond to the second voice?"

They answered: "No."

"Suppose an illusionist at a crossroads transforms and creates a tathāgata who teaches the dharma for the four assemblies. What do you think? Is there anyone who teaches the dharma and anyone who listens and understands?"

The devas then thought to themselves: "The prajñāpāramitā that Subhūti teaches is profoundly deep, reaching the subtle and wondrous."

Subhūti, knowing what the devas were thinking, said to the devas: "Is form not profoundly deep and subtle and wondrous? Are feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness not profoundly deep and subtle and wondrous? Is form not naturally profound and subtle and wondrous? Are feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness not naturally profound and subtle and wondrous? Eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are likewise. The dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā: are they not naturally profound and wondrous? Internal emptiness, external emptiness, proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, true emptiness, emptiness of existence, emptiness of non-existence; the ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas; all samādhis, dhāraṇī gates, and the wisdom of sarvajñā: are they not naturally subtle and wondrous?"

Then the devas thought to themselves: "Does the dharma teacher not give a decisive resolution regarding form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness? Does he not give a decisive resolution regarding the six pāramitās, seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas? Does he not give a decisive resolution regarding stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, and pratyekabuddhahood? Does he not give a decisive resolution regarding the Buddha's wisdom, the inexhaustible wisdom?"

Subhūti, knowing what the devas were thinking, said to the devas: "It is so, devas! The buddha-path has no attainment. The Tathāgata also does not teach the dharma; there is no one who listens and no one who understands. If one wishes to attain the fruit of stream-entry, to realize the fruit of stream-entry, the fruits of once-returning, non-returning, and arhatship, one cannot endure this and departs. The pratyekabuddha-path is likewise. The buddha-path is likewise: one cannot endure this and departs. Thus, devas, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who has initially generated the aspiration, abiding in the prajñāpāramitā, has no words and no speech, and there is also no hearing."

### Chapter Twenty-Six: The Dharma Teacher Like an Illusion

At that time, the devas thought to themselves: "The venerable Subhūti teaches the dharma in this way; how should we listen?"

Subhūti, knowing what the devas were thinking, said to the devas: "The dharma teacher is like an illusion; the listener is like a transformation. Those who hear in this way also do not realize any attainment."

The devas then thought to themselves: "How is it, Subhūti, that persons are like illusions and the dharma teacher is like an illusion? That persons are like transformations and the listener is like a transformation?"

Subhūti said: "It is so, it is so, devas! Persons are like illusions; the dharma teacher is like an illusion. Persons are like transformations; the dharma teacher is like a transformation. Self is like a dream; form is likewise. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are also like a dream. Eye and form are like a dream; ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are likewise. The habituations and contacts are also like a dream. Internal emptiness, external emptiness, proximate emptiness, distant emptiness, true emptiness, emptiness of existence, and emptiness of non-existence are all also like a dream. The thirty-seven factors, ten powers, four fearlessnesses, four analytical knowledges, and eighteen unique buddha-dharmas are also like a dream, like an illusion, like a transformation. The fruits of stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, and arhatship are also like an illusion and a dream. Pratyekabuddhahood, up to samyak-saṃbuddhahood, is also like an illusion and a dream."

The devas said to Subhūti: "Even the buddha-path is like an illusion and a dream?"

Subhūti said: "Even nirvāṇa is like an illusion and a dream."

The devas asked Subhūti: "Even nirvāṇa: nirvāṇa is also like a dream?"

Subhūti said: "Even if there were a dharma more honored than nirvāṇa, at root and end it would also be non-existent. I would also call it like an illusion and a dream. Why? Illusions, dreams, and nirvāṇa have no duality and no multiplicity; all are empty and non-existent."

Then the worthy Śāriputra, Mahāmaudgalyāyana, Mahākauṣṭhila, Mahākātyāyana, Pilindavatsa, and Mahākāśyapa, together with innumerable thousands of bodhisattvas, asked the venerable Subhūti: "This prajñāpāramitā is profoundly deep, difficult to understand and comprehend, quiescent, and subtle and wondrous. What deeply subtle and difficult-to-reach persons can receive it?"

Subhūti said to the disciples and bodhisattvas: "Avaivartika bodhisattva-mahāsattvas can receive this profoundly deep, thoughtless, inconceivable practice that emerges from the far-reaching, difficult to reach and comprehend, quiescent and majestic, dwelling in the noble and wise, knowing, discerning, and wise. They can receive this prajñāpāramitā. Persons of true insight who have become arhats, whose aspirations are fulfilled, who have already undertaken practices under past buddhas, who have made offerings to innumerable hundreds of thousands of buddhas, who have planted roots of merit, who are guided and protected by good teachers: such good men and good women can receive this profound prajñāpāramitā. They listen to and receive this teaching, understanding that form is empty, without conceiving; form being empty, without conceiving; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness being empty, without conceiving; spiritual consciousness being empty, without conceiving; being attached to form, also without conceiving. If one thinks of the absence of form, one does not conceive attachment to the five aggregates' signlessness; one does not conceive spiritual consciousness' signlessness. One does not conceive consciousness' wishlessness; one does not conceive form's wishlessness. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. One does not conceive the five aggregates' thoughtlessness; one does not conceive the five aggregates' non-thoughtlessness. One does not conceive form's non-arising; one does not conceive form's non-ceasing; one does not conceive quiescence or illusoriness. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. One does not conceive the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, or mind's non-arising, non-ceasing, quiescence, or illusoriness. One does not conceive the habituations, contacts, and conditions. The dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā: one does not conceive their arising or their non-ceasing, quiescence, or illusoriness. Up to the seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, eighteen unique buddha-dharmas, all samādhis, and dhāraṇī gates: it is likewise; one does not conceive their arising or their non-ceasing. The fruits of stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, and arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, and the wisdom of sarvajñā: one fully knows they are empty. The wisdom of sarvajñā: one does not conceive emptiness. The wisdom of sarvajñā: one also has no wish. Having no wish, one also does not conceive. The wisdom of sarvajñā: what exists, one does not conceive as empty; the empty, one also does not conceive as existent. Wishlessness and thoughtlessness are likewise. The unconditioned realm: one does not conceive it as empty; the empty, one also does not conceive as the unconditioned realm. Thoughtlessness and wishlessness are likewise. There is no non-arising and no non-ceasing, no quiescence, no illusoriness, and no conception."

Subhūti said to the devas: "This prajñāpāramitā is profoundly subtle and wondrous. It is not what the noble and wise perceive and receive. Why? The dharma has no reception, no hearing, and no manifest teaching. If there is no hearing and no teacher of the dharma, then there is no person and no reception."

Śāriputra said to the venerable Subhūti: "Does this prajñāpāramitā not broadly teach the matters of the arhat, pratyekabuddha, and samyak-saṃbuddha vehicles? Guarding and protecting the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice, from the initial aspiration through to the tenth-abode bodhisattva-path, the six pāramitās, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas? The bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā: the supernatural powers that arise are unfailing. Following the dharma thus, from one buddha-field to another, through the merit one has achieved, one wishes to make offerings to the buddha world-honored ones, and whatever one aspires to, one entirely attains. Having completed the offerings, one then hears and receives the sūtras from the buddhas, never forgetting; through one's own attainment one accomplishes the wisdom of sarvajñā. Constantly in samādhi concentration, the mind never disordered, never thinking conceptually, with unobstructed eloquence. Whatever path one teaches, none can interrupt. One's eloquence accords as it should, with import honored and wondrous, surpassing all worldly understanding."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "It is so, it is so! As the venerable one has said, the prajñāpāramitā explains and teaches the three vehicles. This constitutes the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's eloquent wisdom that surpasses the world, honored and without equal. The mind has no attachment; one comprehends the body, without any delusion, and does not rely on what is perceived. What is perceived regarding form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness: one does not rely on the six pāramitās. One is not attached to the seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, or buddha-dharmas; one also does not rely on the wisdom of sarvajñā."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "For what reason does the prajñāpāramitā broadly teach the three vehicles? Does this constitute the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's obtaining the bodhisattva's eloquence, surpassing all the world without any attachment?"

Subhūti replied to Śāriputra: "Because of internal and external emptiness, one broadly teaches the three vehicles. The seven emptinesses are likewise; all is non-existent, therefore one teaches the three vehicles. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, fully comprehending all the emptinesses, therefore teaches and protects the practitioners. For this reason, one surpasses all the world; one's eloquence is the most honored, without any attachment."

### Chapter Twenty-Seven: Raining Dharma Jewels

At that time, Śakra thought to himself: "What the venerable Subhūti has now taught is a rain of dharma jewels upon the great trichiliocosm, from the Four Heavenly Kings up to the Akaniṣṭha heaven. Now what Subhūti teaches is a rain of dharma jewels. I should transform and create a rain of flowers upon the Buddha, the bodhisattvas, the holy assembly, and Subhūti." Śakra, together with the devas of the great trichiliocosm, each transformed and created flowers, scattering them upon the World-Honored One, all the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas, the bhikṣu assembly, and Subhūti as an offering, taking refuge in the prajñāpāramitā. As soon as they were scattered, the flowers spread across two thousand buddha-fields, and in the upper empty space they transformed into tiered pavilions, towering and majestic, of indescribable delight.

The venerable Subhūti thought to himself: "In the past, I have traveled through all the heavenly palaces, but I have never seen flowers like these. The flowers that were scattered are transformation-flowers, not arising from trees. The flowers that the devas scattered arise from the mind-tree, not from trees."

Śakra replied to Subhūti: "These flowers have no origin; they do not arise from the mind-tree."

Subhūti said: "As Kauśika says, these flowers have no origin; they do not arise from the mind-tree. But, Kauśika, if they have no origin, then they are not flowers."

Śakra replied to Subhūti: "In truth, the flowers have no origin. Form has no origin; feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no origin."

Subhūti said: "Kauśika! These flowers do not have no origin. Form has no arising; what has no arising has no form. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness have no origin; what has no arising has no consciousness. The eye has no arising; what has no arising has no eye. Ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind are likewise. The dāna-pāramitā also has no arising; what has no arising has no dāna. The śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, and prajñāpāramitā also have no arising; what has no arising has no prajñāpāramitā. The seven emptinesses and thirty-seven factors, Kauśika, have no origin; what has no arising has no seven emptinesses and no thirty-seven factors. The ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas have no origin; what has no arising has no dharmas. Stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, the Buddha's wisdom of sarvajñā: all have no arising. What has no arising has no sarvajñā."

Śakra thought to himself: "The wisdom that the venerable Subhūti has entered is profoundly deep. Whatever dharma he teaches is entirely without contention and without confusion."

Then the Buddha told Śakra: "It is so, Kauśika! The wisdom that Subhūti has entered is profoundly deep. Whatever wisdom he has entered and whatever sūtras he teaches are entirely without contention and without confusion."

Śakra addressed the Buddha: "How has the venerable Subhūti so deeply entered wisdom, such that whatever wisdom he enters and whatever sūtras he teaches are entirely without contention and without confusion?"

The Buddha told Śakra: "His entry into form, having entered this dharma, whatever dharma he teaches, is entirely without contention and without confusion. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. Why? The dharma as it is has no harmony and no contention. What Subhūti teaches is likewise: no agreement and no disorder. The six pāramitās are likewise. The seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas are without agreement and without disorder. Stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, and the Buddha's wisdom of sarvajñā are likewise: without agreement and without disorder. Why? What Subhūti teaches has no harmony and no contention; that which is without harmony and contention has no contention. Thus, Kauśika, the wisdom that Subhūti has entered and what he teaches is subtle and wondrous, majestic in this way."

Subhūti said to Śakra: "As the World-Honored One has said, teaching all dharmas: the bodhisattva-mahāsattva comprehends thus, understanding all dharmas. Studying the prajñāpāramitā should also be thus. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who studies in this way does not study receiving form, feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness. Why? Because one does not perceive form; because one does not perceive feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness having any study. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who studies in this way does not study the dāna-pāramitā, śīla-pāramitā, kṣānti-pāramitā, vīrya-pāramitā, dhyāna-pāramitā, or prajñāpāramitā. Why? Because one does not perceive studying the prajñāpāramitā. One does not study the seven emptinesses or thirty-seven factors. Why? Because one does not perceive the seven emptinesses or thirty-seven factors. One does not study the ten powers, four fearlessnesses, or eighteen unique buddha-dharmas. One does not study stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, or the Buddha's wisdom of sarvajñā. Why? Because one does not perceive studying the wisdom of sarvajñā."

Śakra said to the venerable Subhūti: "Subhūti, why does one not perceive form, feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness, the seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, or the Buddha's wisdom of sarvajñā?"

Subhūti said: "Because form is empty; because feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are empty; up to sarvajñā being also empty. Kauśika! Because form is empty, one does not study empty form. Because feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are empty, and because consciousness is empty, one does not study empty consciousness; up to the wisdom of sarvajñā being also empty, one does not study empty wisdom. Kauśika! This is through emptiness. That which is empty does not study emptiness. If one were to study emptiness, it would not be one dharma but two dharmas. If one studies form as empty, that is not one. Up to the wisdom of sarvajñā: if one studies wisdom, that is not one. Therefore, Kauśika, because form, feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are empty, there is no duality. Up to the wisdom of sarvajñā, because all is empty, there is no duality. The six pāramitās are likewise: all without duality. The seven emptinesses, thirty-seven factors, ten powers, fearlessnesses, and buddha-dharmas; śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, up to samyak-saṃbuddhahood: also without duality. The wisdom of sarvajñā is also without duality. One who can study the Buddha's wisdom of sarvajñā thereby studies incalculable asaṃkhyeya dharmas. Having been able to study incalculable asaṃkhyeya buddha-dharmas, one does not study form as beneficial or harmful. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise; up to the wisdom of sarvajñā, without increase or decrease. Having studied the five aggregates without increase or decrease, one can then study the wisdom of sarvajñā. Having been able to study the wisdom of sarvajñā without increase or decrease, one does not study receiving form and there is no loss. One does not study receiving feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness, and there is no loss. One does not study receiving śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, up to the wisdom of sarvajñā, and there is no loss."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva studies in this way, it is non-study, non-reception, and without loss."

Subhūti said: "It is so, Śāriputra! If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva studies in this way, it is non-study, not receiving form, feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness, and there is no loss. Not studying and not receiving sarvajñā, there is also no loss."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "Why does the bodhisattva-mahāsattva not receive the five aggregates and yet have no loss? Not study and not receive sarvajñā and yet have no loss?"

Subhūti said: "Form is non-existent and cannot be received or held; there is no one who receives form. Feeling, perception, formations, consciousness, and the wisdom of sarvajñā are all non-existent and cannot be received or held. There is no one who receives sarvajñā. This, Śāriputra, is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's having no reception regarding all dharmas and accomplishing sarvajñā."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva studies in this way, does one study the prajñāpāramitā and give rise to sarvajñā?"

Subhūti said: "It is so, Śāriputra! If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva studies in this way, one studies the prajñāpāramitā and gives rise to sarvajñā, because regarding all dharmas one has no reception."

Śāriputra said to Subhūti: "If the bodhisattva-mahāsattva studies in this way, regarding all dharmas having no reception, studying without any loss: the bodhisattva-mahāsattva who studies in this way gives rise to sarvajñā."

Subhūti said: "The bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā does not perceive form as having arising or ceasing; one does not receive or reject, without any holding or contending, without increase or decrease. Why? Śāriputra, because form is naturally so, there is no form. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness: one does not perceive their arising or ceasing; one does not receive or reject; there is no defilement and no hatred, no releasing and no non-releasing, no increase and no decrease. Why? The wisdom of sarvajñā is naturally so and entirely non-existent. Therefore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva, regarding all dharmas without arising or ceasing, without reception or rejection, without defilement or hatred, without releasing or non-releasing, without increase or decrease, having studied the prajñāpāramitā, gives rise to sarvajñā through non-study and non-arising."

Śakra said to Śāriputra: "Where should the bodhisattva-mahāsattva seek the prajñāpāramitā?"

Śāriputra said: "Kauśika! One should seek it from the venerable Subhūti."

Śakra asked Subhūti: "Is it the venerable one's divine power and the venerable one's establishment that caused Śāriputra to say: 'Subhūti teaches the prajñāpāramitā; one should seek it from him'?"

Subhūti said to Śakra: "It is not my divine power or my establishment."

Again he asked: "Whose divine power and grace has established this?"

He answered: "Kauśika! It is the Tathāgata's divine power and grace that has established this."

Śakra said to Subhūti: "All dharmas are entirely without any establishment. How then has the Tathāgata's divine power established this? There is also no different place that has established it. Reckoning all dharmas, one does not find the Tathāgata; there is also no different place where one can find the Tathāgata."

The venerable Subhūti said to Śakra: "It is so, Kauśika! The Tathāgata has no abode and no different place where one should abide. There is no different Tathāgata to be found; he also does not depart from his abode. The Tathāgata has no abode; regarding all dharmas, he does not depart from his abode. It is not through form that the Tathāgata is the Tathāgata; it is not through rootlessness that the Tathāgata exists. It is not through form's rootlessness that the Tathāgata exists. It is not that the Tathāgata's rootless form, the rootless form-dharma, is the Tathāgata; it is not that the Tathāgata is rootless. Because the dharma is rootless, all forms are rootless. Because feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are rootless, the Tathāgata is rootless. It is not through the Tathāgata's rootlessness that feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are not rootless in consciousness. This is the Tathāgata's dharma; it is not that the Tathāgata's dharma is the dharma of consciousness. Śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, up to sarvajñā: the rootless Tathāgata; it is not through the Tathāgata's rootlessness. Sarvajñā is rootless; it is not that the dharma of sarvajñā is the dharma of the Tathāgata, and it is not that the dharma of the Tathāgata is the dharma of sarvajñā.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, the Tathāgata, regarding all form-dharmas, has no conjunction and no dispersion. Regarding feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness, he has no conjunction and no dispersion. Not apart from the five aggregates is there conjunction or dispersion. Not in the Tathāgata is there conjunction or dispersion. Not in the dharma of sarvajñā is there conjunction or dispersion. In sarvajñā, the Tathāgata has no conjunction and no dispersion. Not in the dharma of sarvajñā is there conjunction or dispersion. Not apart from sarvajñā does the Tathāgata have conjunction or dispersion.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, regarding all these dharmas without conjunction and without dispersion: through this divine power there is establishment and abiding. As Kauśika previously asked: 'Where should the bodhisattva-mahāsattva seek the prajñāpāramitā?' One does not seek it in form; one does not seek it apart from form. One does not seek it in feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness; one does not seek it apart from consciousness. The prajñāpāramitā regarding form, feeling, perception, formations, consciousness, and all dharmas has no conjunction and no dispersion, no form and no perception; it cannot be received or held. It constitutes a single characteristic, the characteristic of non-existence.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, the bodhisattva-mahāsattva practicing the prajñāpāramitā, up to sarvajñā, has nothing to seek; one does not seek sarvajñā in any different place. Why? Seeking the prajñāpāramitā and sarvajñā: regarding all dharmas there is no conjunction and no dispersion, no form and no perception; it cannot be received or held. It constitutes a single characteristic, the characteristic of non-existence. Why? Kauśika! The prajñāpāramitā has no form and no different form; it has no feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness, and no different consciousness. Consciousness is not different from the prajñāpāramitā; nor is there a different sarvajñā. It is not that the prajñāpāramitā has no different sarvajñā. The prajñāpāramitā and the Tathāgata's prajñāpāramitā have no form and no different form, no different feeling, perception, formations, or consciousness. The prajñāpāramitā is not different from consciousness. Sarvajñā is not the prajñāpāramitā; the prajñāpāramitā is not different from sarvajñā. The Tathāgata's prajñāpāramitā has no form and no different form. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise: not different from consciousness and not without rootlessness. The prajñāpāramitā has no form-dharma and no different form-dharma. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. The prajñāpāramitā has no form and no rootlessness, no different form and no rootlessness. The prajñāpāramitā has no form-dharma and no different form-dharma. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. Śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, up to sarvajñā are likewise: there is no form-dharma of sarvajñā and no different form-dharma of sarvajñā. The prajñāpāramitā has no rootlessness of sarvajñā and no different rootlessness of sarvajñā. The prajñāpāramitā has no rootlessness of sarvajñā and no different rootlessness of sarvajñā."

Śakra said to Subhūti: "This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' mahā-prajñāpāramitā, without difference, a pāramitā without limit. What the bodhisattva-mahāsattva should study: stream-entry, once-returning, non-returning, arhatship, pratyekabuddhahood, bodhisattvahood, and buddhahood: one should study in accordance with this. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva who studies this dharma, through teaching and converting sentient beings and purifying the buddha-field, attains anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi."

Subhūti said to Śakra: "It is so, Kauśika! This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' mahā-prajñāpāramitā: a pāramitā without difference, a pāramitā without limit. One should study in accordance with this. Through the three vehicles, all arise from this. The bodhisattva-mahāsattva, through one's own attainment of anuttarā-samyak-saṃbodhi, accomplishes abhisaṃbuddhahood. Form is without boundary; this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā without limit. Why? One cannot apprehend past form, nor can one apprehend form in the interval, nor can one apprehend future form. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness are likewise. Consciousness is without boundary; the pāramitā is without limit. Why? One cannot apprehend past consciousness, nor consciousness in the interval, nor future consciousness. Śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, up to the Buddha: limitless and boundless, it is likewise. Therefore, Kauśika, this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' limitless pāramitā.

"Form is without measure; the prajñāpāramitā is also without measure. Why? Because form cannot be delimited. Just as, Kauśika, empty space cannot be bounded or delimited; form being without measure is likewise. Because empty space is limitless, form is limitless. Because form is limitless, the prajñāpāramitā is limitless. Up to sarvajñā, it is also limitless. Therefore the prajñāpāramitā is limitless; this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' practice. Why? Kauśika, because the wisdom of sarvajñā cannot be bounded or delimited. Just as empty space cannot be bounded, the wisdom of sarvajñā is likewise. Because empty space is limitless, sarvajñā is also limitless. Because sarvajñā is limitless, the prajñāpāramitā is limitless. Therefore, Kauśika, the prajñāpāramitā is limitless; this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' practice.

"Empty space is boundless; form is bottomless; the pāramitā is bottomless. Why? Kauśika, form has no boundary and no interval. Feeling, perception, formations, and consciousness also have no boundary and no interval. Therefore the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā has no boundary and no bottom. Why? Spiritual consciousness cannot be bottomed; it has no interval. Up to sarvajñā, it also has no bottom; the pāramitā also has no bottom. This is the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' practice. Why? Kauśika, sarvajñā cannot be bounded and has no interval. The pāramitā is bottomless; this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's practice. Because form is bottomless, sarvajñā is also bottomless.

"Furthermore, Kauśika, matters are without beginning or end; the pāramitā is bottomless. One who comprehends this is the bodhisattva-mahāsattva."

Śakra asked Subhūti: "For what reason are matters without beginning or end, and the pāramitā bottomless?"

Subhūti said: "Kauśika! Because the matters of sarvajñā are without beginning or end, the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā is bottomless. Furthermore, Kauśika, the dharma is without beginning or end; therefore the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā is bottomless."

Śakra said to Subhūti: "For what reason is the dharma without beginning or end, and the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's pāramitā bottomless?"

Subhūti said: "Because the dharma-realm is bottomless, the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā is bottomless. Furthermore, Kauśika, the rootless matters are all without beginning or end; therefore the bodhisattva-mahāsattva's pāramitā is bottomless."

Śakra asked Subhūti: "For what reason are the rootless matters all without beginning or end, and the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā bottomless?"

"Kauśika! What is rootless is bottomless; therefore it is bottomless. Because matters are without beginning, they are rootless and bottomless. Being rootless and bottomless, matters are therefore bottomless. Because matters are bottomless, the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā is bottomless.

"Furthermore, persons are bottomless; therefore the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā is bottomless."

Śakra asked Subhūti: "For what reason are persons bottomless, and the bodhisattva-mahāsattvas' pāramitā bottomless?"

Subhūti said: "What does Kauśika think? In what dharma does one teach in this way, calling someone a bodhisattva-mahāsattva?"

Śakra replied to Subhūti: "There is no dharma-teaching and no non-dharma-teaching. This name comes from conditions and is adventitious; all is non-existent and without any original form. It is but a conventional name, what is called a 'person.' Persons have no causation; the designation is arbitrarily established. What does Kauśika think? Does this prajñāpāramitā manifest and proclaim a place for persons?"

He answered: "No."

Subhūti said: "Kauśika! If persons are not spoken of, is there not a bottomlessness? Consider, Kauśika: if the Tathāgata, Arhat, Samyak-saṃbuddha, with a lifespan as long as the sands of the Ganges in kalpas, were to speak of persons and persons, would there be any person with arising or ceasing?"

He answered: "No, Subhūti! Why? Because persons are originally pure."

"Therefore, Kauśika, persons are bottomless; the prajñāpāramitā is bottomless. The bodhisattva who studies should know thus; the practice of the prajñāpāramitā dharma is like this."
